That is, in his statement: 'Whoever usurps a cloth and dyes it red' and he guarded by this condition against the misunderstanding that this ruling which Abu 'Ismah mentioned is connected to what follows from the matter of accidental dyeing (insibagh); and even if the matter of accidental dyeing is like that, yet Abu 'Ismah's statement in the original matter restricts it with that to correct the transmission. [From 'Inayah] [Page 359] Chapter of Usurpation. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of al-Hidayah, volume 12. 'He takes his cloth and five dirhams because one of the two fives is compensated by the dye.' Translation: Abu 'Ismah said in the original matter: If the owner of the cloth wishes, he may sell the cloth; then in its price he will be a partner according to his white cloth, and the dyer will be entitled according to the increase of the dye, because the owner of the cloth has the option not to own the dye for its value; and in case of his refraining, consideration of both sides is determined through sale. And this statement also applies when the cloth becomes dyed by itself. And from the mentioned explanation, the reason is clear in the matter of barley (sawiq) except that barley is among mithliyyat, so he is liable for its similar; and the cloth is among qimiyyat, so he is liable for its value. And in al-Asl (al-Mabsut) it is said that he is liable for the value of the barley because toasting makes the barley vary, so it does not remain mithli. And it is said that by 'value' is meant 'similar'; it is called value because it stands in its place. And yellow dye is like red. And if he dyes it black, then this is a decrease (nuqsan) according to Abu Hanifa, and an increase according to the two (Sahibayn). And it is said that this is only a difference of era and time. And it is said that if it is a cloth that black dye decreases, then it is a decrease; and if it is a cloth such that black dye increases it, then it is like red. And this is known in another place. And if it is a cloth such that red dye decreases its value – for example, its value was thirty dirhams and after dyeing red it decreased to twenty dirhams – then it is narrated from Muhammad that one looks at a cloth in which red dye increases value. So if the increase is five dirhams, then he takes his cloth and five dirhams, because the loss of one of the two fives is compensated by the dye. (His statement: 'Qasbaghuhu' ?) Commentary: 'His statement: Abu 'Ismah said...' – Sheikh Abu 'Ismah Sa'd ibn Mu'adh al-Marwazi (who was a student of Ibrahim ibn Yusuf, who was a student of Imam Abu Yusuf) said in the original matter, i.e., 'And whoever usurps a red cloth', that the owner of the cloth also has the option to sell the cloth; then in its price the owner of the cloth will be a partner according to his white cloth, and the owner of the dye will be entitled according to the increase of the dye, because the owner of the cloth has the option not to accept ownership of the dye by paying its value. (His statement: 'And this applies...') However, the mentioned statement of Sheikh Abu 'Ismah applies not only to the original matter but also to the case when the cloth becomes dyed by itself without any action of the dyer, because in that case he will not have the option to take compensation from the dyer since he has no fault. So when the owner of the cloth refrains from taking ownership (tamalluk) of the cloth and the dyer is ready to be compelled as a guarantor, then for him to receive his right the method of sale is determined, since the owner of the cloth is not satisfied with giving the value of the dye and taking ownership of the dye. As for the case of usurpation, if the owner of the cloth refrains from taking ownership of the dye, the method of sale is not determined for receiving his right, because he has [the option of] holding the usurper liable for the white cloth. (His statement: 'And it has become clear from what we mentioned...') – From the mentioned statement in the matter of dyeing and accidental dyeing, the ruling of the matter of barley and its reason also became apparent.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute, presenting the opinion of Sheikh Abu 'Ismah and the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding black dye. The text first explains that Abu 'Ismah's statement (that the owner may also sell the cloth and share the proceeds) is actually part of the original matn, not a separate issue, and it also applies when the cloth becomes dyed accidentally. The reason is that if the owner does not want to pay for the dye and take ownership, sale becomes the method to give each party their due. In cases of pure usurpation, this sale option is not required because the owner can simply hold the usurper liable for the white cloth. The text then discusses the nature of compensation: barley is mithli (fungible) so similar is owed, but if toasting changes it, it becomes qimi (value-based). Similarly, cloth is qimi. A key point: black dye is considered a decrease (nuqsan) by Imam Abu Hanifa, but an increase (ziyada) by Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad. This difference may be based on custom and time. The later preferred view is to look at the actual effect: if the cloth's value increases with black dye, it is an increase; if it decreases, it is a decrease. The same applies to red dye: if red dye decreases value (e.g., from 30 to 20 dirhams), one looks at a cloth where red dye increases value; then the owner takes his cloth plus the amount of increase (5 dirhams) to compensate for the loss.

Key Terms
تملك الصبغ (tamalluk al-sabgh): Taking ownership of the dye by paying its value
نقصان (nuqsān): Decrease in value
زيادة (ziyādah): Increase in value

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling when a garment's value decreases due to red dye (e.g., from 30 dirhams to 20 dirhams)?
A) The owner takes the garment and the usurper compensates the full value of white cloth.
B) The owner looks at a garment where red dye increases value, takes the increase amount (e.g., 5 dirhams) plus the cloth.
C) The garment is sold and proceeds divided equally.
D) The usurper must restore the garment to its original color.

Key Takeaway
Abu Ismah's ruling provides an alternative sale option, and the classification of black dye as increase or decrease depends on its actual effect on the cloth's value, not a fixed rule.

Distinction Between Sawiq and Cloth in Guarantee
Compares the ruling for sawiq with dyed cloth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish mithli from qimi goods in Hanafi fiqh and state the compensation rule for each in cases of mixing.

Core Idea
Sawiq is mithli — guaranteed by like; cloth is qimi — guaranteed by value.

In the previous lesson on dyeing cloth, we learned the ruling of sale and division when a usurper mixes his property with another's. This passage extends that principle to sawiq mixed with flour. The key difference lies in the nature of the goods: sawiq is fungible (mithli), while cloth is non-fungible (qimi). This distinction determines whether the guarantor must return the exact like or pay market value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Recognize that the passage compares two scenarios: sawiq mixed with flour (by usurper or accidentally) and dyed cloth mixed by a usurper.
Both involve mixing without consent, triggering a guarantee.
2
State the common ruling
Both cases apply the same principle: the mixture is sold and the proceeds divided proportionally, as per Shaykh Abu 'Asma.
This is the default when separation is impossible.
3
Differentiate the compensation
For sawiq (mithli), the guarantor must return the like (same quantity and quality). For cloth (qimi), the guarantor must pay the market value at the time of loss.
The nature of the good determines the type of compensation.
4
Apply the distinction
In any mixing case, first classify the item as mithli or qimi, then apply the appropriate guarantee.
Mithli items have standard units; qimi items are unique or have no exact market substitute.
5
Recognize accidental mixing
The same ruling applies even if the mixing occurs without intentional wrongdoing (e.g., spontaneous mixing).
The guarantee is tied to the fact of mixing causing loss, not just intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وقد ظهر بما ذكرنا ... الخ - مسئلہ صبغ وانصباغ میں مذکورہ بیان سے ستو کے مسئلہ کا حکم اور اس کی وجہ بھی ظاہر ہوگئی ۔ یعنی ستو کومسکہ میں خلط کرنے یا خود بخو د خلط ہو جانے میں بھی یہی دلیل جاری ہے۔ اور اس میں بھی شیخ ابو عصمتہ کا قول چل سکتا ہے صرف اتنا فرق ہے کہ ستو متلی چیزوں میں سے ہے تو اس کے مثل کا تاوان دے گا اور کپڑا ایسی چیزوں میں سے ہے جس کا تاوان بقیمت ہوتا ہے لہذا اس کی قیمت کا ضامن ہو گا۔
His statement: 'And it has become apparent from what we mentioned... etc.' - From the above explanation of the issue of dyeing and being dyed, the ruling and its reason for the issue of sawiq also become apparent. That is, in the case of mixing sawiq with flour or it being mixed by itself, the same evidence applies. And in that case also the statement of Shaykh Abu 'Asma can apply, except that sawiq is among mithli things, so he will guarantee its like; while cloth is among things whose guarantee is by value, so he will be liable for its value.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This lesson applies the same principle of sale and division to the case where sawiq (roasted grain) is mixed with flour, either by a usurper or accidentally. The ruling of Shaykh Abu 'Asma (selling and dividing) is equally valid here. However, the key difference is in the type of property: sawiq is mithli (fungible), meaning it can be replaced with an identical item, so the guarantor (the one who caused the mixing) must return the like (mithl). Cloth is qimi (non-fungible), valued by its market price, so the guarantor must pay its value. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh for determining compensation.

Key Terms
مثلي (mithli): A fungible good that can be replaced by an identical item in the market.
قيمي (qimi): A non-fungible good that has no exact substitute, valued by market price.
سويق (sawiq): Roasted grain (wheat or barley) used as food.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of mixing sawiq with flour, what is the guarantor liable for?
A) The value of the sawiq
B) The like of the sawiq (same quantity and quality)
C) Only if the mixing was intentional
D) The sawiq and flour combined

Key Takeaway
The distinction between mithli and qimi goods determines whether compensation is by like or by value, and this classification is based on fungibility, not processing.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Guarantee of Sawiq by Value or by Like
Intra-Hanafi refinement of sawiq guarantee in Al-Mabsut.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over the guarantee of sawiq in Al-Mabsut and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Roasting makes sawiq non-fungible, so it is guaranteed by value, not like — a key Hanafi refinement.

This passage highlights a nuanced legal distinction within the Hanafi school. While earlier rulings considered sawiq a fungible good (mithli) guaranteed by a like substitute, Imam Muhammad in Al-Mabsut ruled that roasting changes the grain's nature, making it unique (qimi) and therefore guaranteed by value. Later scholars weighed in, and some harmonised 'value' with 'like'. This demonstrates the depth of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
From the passage, the earlier ruling (Al-Asl) says guarantee by like; Imam Muhammad in Al-Mabsut says by value.
Note the difference in source authority.
2
Analyse the legal reasoning
Imam Muhammad's reason: roasting changes the sawiq, so it is no longer fungible (mithli). This makes it qimi, guaranteed by value.
3
Examine the scholarly commentary
Shaykh 'Ala' al-Din al-Asbijabi supports the value position. Some mashayikh interpret 'value' as 'like' to harmonise.
This shows later scholars engaged in tarjih and interpretation.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Based on Zahir al-Riwayah and Al-Asbijabi's preference, the relied-upon position is value.
Authority weight: Zahir al-Riwayah.

قوله وقال فی الاصل ... الخ - او پر معلوم ہوا کہ مسئلہ سویق میں ستو کے مثل کا تاوان دے گا۔ مگر اصل یعنی مبسوط میں مذکور ہے کہ سٹو کی قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ بھوننے سے سٹو میں تفاوت ہو جاتا ہے تو وہ متلی نہیں رہتا ۔ شیخ علاؤالدین اسپیجابی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہی صحیح ہے۔ اس لئے کہ سویق ، بھنے ہوئے گیہوں کے اجزاء کا نام ہے۔ اور بھن جانے کی وجہ سے گیہوں ذوات الا مثال ہونے سے نکل جاتا ہے اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ مبسوط میں قیمت سے مراد شل ہی ہے۔ امام محمد نے اس کو قیمت سے اس لئے تعبیر کیا ہے کہ مثل مغصوب کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے۔
His statement: 'And he said in Al-Asl... etc.' - From above it became known that in the issue of sawiq, he will guarantee the like of the sawiq. But in Al-Asl, i.e., Al-Mabsut, it is mentioned that he will be liable for the value of sawiq. Because roasting causes sawiq to become different, so it does not remain mithli. Shaykh 'Ala' al-Din al-Asbijabi says that this is correct. Because sawiq is the name for roasted wheat particles, and due to roasting, wheat exits from being among things that have likes. And some mashayikh have said that in Al-Mabsut, by 'value' is meant 'like'. Imam Muhammad expressed it as 'value' because it stands in place of the usurped item.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi refinement. Earlier it was stated that sawiq is mithli and guaranteed by like. However, Imam Muhammad in Al-Mabsut (one of the Zahir al-Riwayah books) ruled that the guarantor pays the value, because roasting changes the grain, making it arguably non-fungible. Al-Asbijabi supports this. Some scholars harmonize by interpreting 'value' as meaning the 'like' itself, since the like serves as a substitute. This shows the meticulous nature of Hanafi legal analysis, where even within the school there are differing positions that later scholars weigh.

Key Terms
مبسوط (Mabsut): A major work of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
قيمة (qimah): Market value, here possibly meaning the replacement cost.
سویق (sawiq): Roasted wheat, a type of processed grain.
مثل (mithl): Like, similar item used as compensation for fungibles.
متلی (mithli): Fungible good that can be substituted by an identical item.
قیمی (qimi): Non-fungible good, compensated by value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad in Al-Mabsut, why is sawiq not considered mithli?
A) Because it is always traded by weight
B) Because roasting changes its nature, making it unique
C) Because the usurper is always a wrongdoer
D) Because it is mixed with flour

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school refined its position on sawiq guarantee: the later authoritative view in Al-Mabsut requires payment of value, not like, due to the effect of roasting.

Black Dye: Deficiency or Enhancement?
Intra-Hanafi dispute resolved by custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi ruling on black dye depends on custom and apply 'urf as a tarjih factor in intra-madhhab disputes.

Core Idea
A ruling may change with custom: black dye is a deficiency in one era and an enhancement in the next.

In this passage, we encounter a fascinating intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree on whether black dye added to a usurped cloth constitutes a deficiency or an enhancement. At first glance, this seems like a purely factual disagreement, but the commentators reveal that the real cause is differing social and political customs in their respective eras. This lesson will teach you how to analyze such differences, recognizing that 'urf (custom) can determine the legal value of an act, even within the same school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Question
Start by recognizing the core issue: whether black dye on a usurped cloth is a deficiency (nuqsan) or an enhancement (ziyadah). This affects the owner's right to reclaim the cloth without payment or the usurper's entitlement to compensation.
2
State the Positions of the Imams
Abu Hanifa holds it is a deficiency; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is an enhancement. Note who held which view and the practical consequence (owner takes cloth free vs. must pay for the enhancement).
3
Analyze the Reason for Disagreement
The disagreement is traced to the political and cultural context: Umayyads disliked black (Abu Hanifa's time) and Abbasids favored it (Sahibayn's time). Thus each imam ruled based on the prevailing custom they observed.
This is a key point: the difference is not a matter of proof (dalil) but of changing 'urf.
4
Apply the Principle of Custom
The mashayikh resolved the ikhtilaf by stating that the ruling follows the custom of the time and place. Therefore, a mufti today must determine the market value of black dye in his own society.
5
Note the Practical Nuance
Imam Abu Yusuf himself changed his view after becoming a qadi and being required to wear black, showing that even a mujtahid's fatwa can adapt when circumstances change.
This illustrates the dynamism of Hanafi fiqh.

His statement: 'And if he dyes it black... etc.' - If the usurper dyes the usurped cloth black, this is a deficiency according to Imam Abu Hanifa. So the owner can take his cloth without giving anything to the usurper. And according to the Sahibayn, black dye is an enhancement like red and yellow. So the same ruling applies as for those. His statement: 'Difference of era and time... etc.' Some mashayikh have said that the difference regarding black dye being deficiency or enhancement is only a difference of their own times. Because in the time of Imam Abu Hanifa, the Banu Umayya were rulers, who detested black color, and thus black color was undervalued. And in the time of the Sahibayn, the Banu Abbas were rulers, who liked black color, so black color gained value. Thus each imam gave a ruling according to what he saw in his time. So now too, wherever that color is valued or undervalued, ruling shall be given accordingly. Benefit: Initially, Imam Abu Yusuf also held the same opinion as Imam Abu Hanifa. But when he was appointed judge and ordered to wear black clothing, he had to adopt the opinion that black is also an enhancement and addition. It is also narrated that Harun al-Rashid consulted him about the color of clothing and he said: 'The color with which the Book of Allah is written.' Harun al-Rashid liked this answer and adopted black color. And those after him followed.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about whether black dye on a usurped cloth counts as a deficiency (nuqsan) or an enhancement (ziyadah). Imam Abu Hanifa views it as a deficiency because in his era the Umayyads disliked black, reducing its value. The Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) consider it an enhancement, reflecting the Abbasid preference. The commentary resolves this by attributing the difference to custom ('urf) varying by time and place. The ruling is thus relative: a judge should consider local market conditions. A historical note mentions that Imam Abu Yusuf himself changed his view after being appointed qadi and required to wear black, illustrating that fatwa may adapt to prevailing customs.

Key Terms
نقصان (nuqsan): Decrease in value; here, black dye causing a drop in cloth price.
زيادة (ziyadah): Increase in value; enhancement due to dye.
عرف ('urf): Custom or common practice that can influence legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because of the political and cultural preferences of their respective eras
C) Because Abu Hanifa disliked black personally
D) Because the cloth was silk

Key Takeaway
Custom ('urf) can cause an intra-madhhab disagreement to be resolved by local market practice.

Red Dye Causing Deficiency in Value
Ruling when red dye reduces cloth value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of qiyas based on custom (urf) to determine whether red dye is an enhancement or deficiency in compensation cases.

Core Idea
The ruling on red dye depends on market custom – if it reduces value, it is a deficiency; if it enhances, it is an improvement.

In the previous lesson, we learned that red dye is generally considered an enhancement. But what if the market actually dislikes red? This passage from al-Hidayah shows that the Hanafi school does not enforce a fixed ruling; instead, it looks to the actual market effect (urf). The conclusion is that there is no real dispute – it simply depends on the custom of each time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the new case (far')
The passage extends the earlier ruling on black dye to red dye when it causes loss. The new case is a cloth whose value decreases due to red dye.
The marker 'قوله تنقصه الحمرة' signals the new case.
2
Recall the original ruling (asl)
The original case is red dye that increases value – it is an enhancement, and the dyer is entitled to compensation for the increase.
This ruling was established in the previous lesson.
3
Extract the illa (effective cause)
The effective cause is the change in market value. Whether the dye increases or decreases value determines the ruling.
The illa is not the colour itself but the market impact.
4
Apply qiyas
Since the illa (market value decrease) is present in the new case, the ruling follows: red dye is a deficiency. The owner may take the cloth without additional payment.
Analogy is based on the shared illa of value change.
5
Note the role of custom
The passage emphasizes that there is no real difference of opinion because the ruling is tied to custom (adah). Each era's market practice determines the outcome.
Custom (urf) is a recognized source in Hanafi fiqh.

And if the cloth is such that black dye increases its value, then it will be considered an enhancement like red. The author of Hidayah says that this matter is known outside this context in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi and other books of Mabsut. The conclusion is that there is no real difference in this issue, as it refers to the custom of each time. Imam al-Quduri mentioned similarly in his Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi. His statement: 'Redness reduces it... etc.' - And if there is a cloth such that redness causes loss. For example, its price was ten dirhams and due to red dye it decreased to five dirhams. Then from Imam Muhammad, through Hisham, it is narrated that such a cloth should be compared with a cloth in which redness
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This final passage extends the rationale of custom to red dye. Even though red dye is typically an enhancement (as per earlier ruling), if in a particular case it actually reduces the cloth's value, the ruling should reflect that: the dye is treated as a deficiency. The Hidayah notes that this is not a genuine dispute but simply a consequence of varying customs (adat). To determine compensation, one should look at a similar cloth where red dye increases value, measure the enhancement, and then calculate the deficiency in the current case. The text cites a narration from Hisham from Imam Muhammad. This illustrates the Hanafi method of qiyas and istihsan: the ruling is not fixed but flexible based on market reality.

Key Terms
عادة (adah): Custom or common practice in the market that determines valuation.
قيمة (qimah): Market value of the cloth.

The Ruling on Dyeing a Usurped Cloth: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and the Role of Custom
Intra-Hanafi dispute resolved by custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on black dye as increase or decrease, and state how custom ('urf) resolves the ikhtilaf in this and similar cases.

Core Idea
The ruling on dyeing a usurped cloth follows custom: black may be increase or decrease depending on time and place.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: is black dye on a usurped cloth an increase (ziyada) or a decrease (naqs)? Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differed, but later scholars resolved the issue by appealing to custom. By studying this case, you will learn how the Hanafi school reconciles apparent disagreements through contextual factors and the flexibility of 'urf.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the two opposing positions: one says black dye is a decrease, the other says it is an increase like red or yellow.
The dispute is between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).
2
Identify each imam's position and its basis
Abu Hanifa considered black a decrease (naqs) based on the custom of his time (Umayyad rule). The Sahibayn considered it an increase (ziyada) based on the custom of their time (Abbasid rule).
Note the role of political context in shaping custom.
3
Recognize the historical context
The Umayyads despised black, so black garments had low value; the Abbasids favored black, so black garments had high value.
This explains the difference without requiring a substantive legal disagreement.
4
Understand the resolution by 'urf
Later scholars (e.g., in Al-Hidayah) stated that the ruling follows the custom of the time and place. There is no fixed answer; it varies.
This resolution preserves the authority of both positions by referring to external circumstances.
5
Apply to a modern scenario
If black dye is currently valued in a given market, it is an increase; if not, it is a decrease. The same principle applies to any dye color.
This shows the dynamic nature of Hanafi fiqh.

He said: 'And if he dyes it black ... etc.' - If the usurper dyes the usurped cloth black, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa this is a decrease (naqs). So the owner of the cloth can take his cloth without giving anything to the usurper. According to the Sahibayn, black dye, like red and yellow, is an increase (ziyada). So the same ruling applies. He said: 'Difference of era and time ... etc.' Some mashayikh have said that the disagreement regarding black dye being a decrease or increase is only a difference of their own time. In Imam Abu Hanifa's time, the Umayyads ruled, who hated black, so black was valueless. In the Sahibayn's time, the Abbasids ruled, who liked black, so black gained value. Thus each imam gave the ruling according to what he saw of black in his time. So now too, wherever this color has value or lack of it, the ruling will be given accordingly. Benefit: Initially Imam Abu Yusuf also held the same view as Abu Hanifa. But when he was appointed as qadi and ordered to wear black garments, he had to adopt the view that black is also an increase and addition. It is also narrated that Harun al-Rashid consulted him about the color of garments, and he said: 'The color with which the Book of Allah is written.' Harun al-Rashid liked this answer greatly and adopted black, and those after him followed. He said: 'It is said that if the cloth ... etc.' - Some have said that if the cloth is such that black causes it loss, then this color is considered a decrease; and if the cloth is such that black increases its value, then it is considered an increase like red. The author of Al-Hidayah says that this point is known in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi and other books of Al-Mabsut. The conclusion is that there is no real disagreement in this issue; it is referred back to the custom of each time. Imam Quduri has mentioned similarly in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi. He said: 'The redness decreases it ... etc.' - And if there is a cloth in which redness causes decrease, for example, its price was ten dirhams and due to red dye it decreased to five dirhams, then in the narration of Hisham from Imam Muhammad, one looks at a cloth in which redness increases value. So if the increase is, say, five dirhams, the owner will take his cloth and five dirhams. Because the owner is entitled to ten dirhams loss, and the dyer is entitled to five dirhams as the value of the dye, so five is offset against five. Then the remaining loss, i.e., five dirhams, he will take back.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute resolved by appeal to custom. It begins by stating that according to Abu Hanifa, black dye on a usurped cloth is a decrease (naqs), so the owner may take his cloth without paying the usurper anything. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), black is like red and yellow—an increase (ziyada). The commentator then explains that some scholars attribute this difference to the political context: Abu Hanifa lived under the Umayyads, who despised black, so it was valueless; the Sahibayn lived under the Abbasids, who favoured black, so it was valuable. Hence each ruled according to their time's custom. A benefit (fa'ida) notes that Abu Yusuf initially agreed with Abu Hanifa but changed his view after becoming qadi when the Abbasid caliph ordered wearing black. An anecdote about Harun al-Rashid further illustrates the acceptance of black. The commentator then clarifies that the real criterion is whether the dye in fact increases or decreases the cloth's value; this is determined by prevailing custom ('urf). Thus, the apparent disagreement is not a substantive legal difference but a reflection of different times. The section ends with a specific example of red dye that decreases value: if red dye causes a loss of five dirhams, the owner is entitled to that loss, and the dyer is entitled to the value of his dye (five dirhams in the example given), leading to offsetting and the owner taking his cloth plus the net loss.

Key Terms
نقصان (naqs): Decrease in value; in this context, the dye reduces the cloth's market value.
زیادت (ziyada): Increase in value; the dye adds to the cloth's value.
عرف ('urf): Custom or prevailing practice; used here to determine the effect of dye on value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the final ruling according to Al-Hidayah on whether black dye on a usurped cloth is an increase or decrease?
A) Black dye is always an increase, following the Sahibayn.
B) Black dye is always a decrease, following Abu Hanifa.
C) It depends on the custom of the time and place.
D) The owner always pays the value of the dye.

Key Takeaway
The apparent intra-Hanafi dispute on black dye is resolved by referring to custom ('urf), showing that Hanafi fiqh considers social context in determining legal outcomes.

Ownership Transfer to Usurper Upon Payment of Value: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Explains inter-madhhab dispute on usurper's ownership upon payment of value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on ownership transfer to a usurper and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
When the usurper pays full value, the item transfers ownership to avoid double compensation – provided the item is transferable.

This passage explores a key inter-madhhab dispute on the effect of paying compensation for a usurped item. The Hanafi school holds that the usurper becomes the owner once the owner accepts the value, while Imam al-Shafi'i rejects this. The disagreement hinges on the legal nature of the substitute (badal) and the transferability of the original item (mubdal).

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
What is the precise question being debated? Does the usurper become owner when he pays the value of the usurped item that has disappeared?
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school (along with Imam Malik) says yes. The proof: the owner has fully acquired the substitute (badal), and the original (mubdal) is capable of transfer. Ownership transfers to prevent harm.
Key terms: badal (substitute), mubdal (original), qabil li al-naql (transferable).
3
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i (and Ahmad) say no. Their proof: usurpation is pure aggression (عدوان محض) and cannot be a cause for ownership. They analogize to the mudabbar case, where consensus holds that the usurper does not become owner even after paying value.
Mudabbar: a slave whose emancipation is deferred to the master's death; not freely transferable.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the mudabbar analogy
The Hanafi response distinguishes the mudabbar because it is not freely transferable due to the mudabbar's right. The non-mudabbar item is fully transferable, so the analogy fails. The principle of substitution (badal) overrides the initial wrong to prevent loss.
The mudabbar can become transferable only if a judge annuls the tadbir, but that is a separate scenario.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Hanafi law, the usurper can resell the item after paying value; under Shafi'i law, the item remains the owner's, so if it reappears, the usurper must return it, and the owner may face double recovery issues.
This affects how courts resolve property disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غصب سے متعلق متفرق مسائل
فصل . ومن غصب عينا فغيّبها فضمنه المالك قيمتها ملكها وهذا عندنا وقال الشافعي لا يملكها لان الغصب عدوان محض، فلا يصلح سببا للملك كما فى المدبر، ولنا انه ملك البدل بكماله والمبدل قابل للنقل من ملک الی ملک فیملـكـه دفعا للضرر عنه بخلاف المدبر، لانه غير قابل للنقل لحق المدبر نعم قد يفسخ التدبير بالقضاء لكن البيع بعده يصادف القنَّ.
ترجمہ: کسی نے مال عین غصب کر کے اس کو غائب کر دیا۔ اور مالک نے اس کی قیمت کا تاوان لے لیا تو غاصب اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ یہ ہمارے نزدیک ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ اس کا مالک نہ ہو گا ۔ کیونکہ غصب تو ظلم محض ہے۔ پس وہ ملک کا سبب نہیں ہو سکتا جیسے مدبر میں ہماری دلیل یہ ہے۔ کہ مالک پورے عوض کا مالک ہو چکا اور مبذل ایسی چیز ہے جو ایک ملک سے دوسری ملک کی طرف منتقل ہونے کے قابل ہے تو غاصب اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ اس سے ضرر دور کرنے کے لئے بخلاف مدبر کے کہ وہ حق مدبر کی وجہ سے قابل نقل نہیں ہے۔ ہاں کبھی بحکم قضاء تدبیر رفع کر دی جاتی ہے لیکن اس کے بعد ہونے والی بیع مملوک محض پر واقع ہوگی ۔
تشریح قوله ومن غصب عينا .... الخ - اگر غاصب نے کوئی چیز غصب کر کے اس کو غائب کر دیا۔ اور مالک کو اس کی قیمت کا تاوان دے دیا تو ہمارے اور امام مالک کے نزدیک غاصب اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ امام شافعی اور امام احمد کے نزدیک مالک نہ ہو گا۔ وہ یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ غصب ظلم محض ہے جو نعمت ملک کا سبب نہیں ہو سکتا۔ جیسے کوئی مد بر غلام کو غصب کر کے غائب کر دے اور اس کی قیمت کا تاوان دیدے تو وہ بالا تفاق اس کا مالک نہیں ہوتا۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ ملک مشروع ہے اور غصب غیر مشروع ہے اور جو امر غیر مشروع ہو دہ مشروع کے حصول کا سبب نہیں ہوتا۔
قوله ولنا انه ملک..... الخ - ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مالک فی مغصوب کے بدل یعنی اس کی قیمت کا بطریق کمال مالک ہو چکا اور جو شخص بدل کا مالک ہو جاتا ہے تو مبدل اس کی ملک سے خارج ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور صاحب بدل کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو جاتا ہے تا کہ مالک بدل کا نقصان لازم نہ آئے ۔ البتہ اس کے لئے یہ ضروری ہے کہ مبدل میں ایک سے دوسری ملک کی طرف منتقل ہونے کی صلاحیت ہو اور یہاں یہ شرط موجود ہے۔ یعنی مبدل قابل نقل ہے بخلاف مدبر کے کہ وہ قابل نقل نہیں فافتر قا۔
قوله نعم قد يفسخ ... الخ - ایک اشکال کا جواب ہے۔ اشکال یہ ہے کہ قابل نقل تو مدبر بھی ہے۔ چنانچہ آقا اگر اس کو فروخت کر دے اور مشتری تسلیم مدیر کا مخاصمہ کرے اور قاضی اس کی بیچ کے جواز کا فیصلہ کر دے تو بیع جائز اور تدبیر سخ ہو جاتی ہے اور مشتری اس مد بر کو لے لیتا ہے۔
Miscellaneous issues related to usurpation.
Section: And whoever usurps a specific property and then makes it disappear, and the owner takes its value as compensation, then the usurper becomes its owner. This is our view. Imam al-Shafi'i says he does not become its owner, because usurpation is pure aggression, so it cannot be a cause for ownership, as in the case of a mudabbar (a slave whose emancipation is deferred to the master's death). Our proof is that the owner has fully acquired the substitute (badal), and the original (mubdal) is capable of transfer from one ownership to another, so the usurper becomes its owner to repel harm from himself, unlike the mudabbar, because it is not capable of transfer due to the mudabbar's right. Yes, sometimes the tadbir may be annulled by judicial decree, but the sale after that occurs on a pure slave.

Commentary:
He said: 'And whoever usurps a specific property... etc.' - If a person usurps something and makes it disappear, and pays the owner its value, then according to us and Imam Malik, the usurper becomes its owner. According to Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad, he does not become its owner. They say that usurpation is pure aggression, which cannot be a cause for ownership, just as if someone usurps a mudabbar slave and makes him disappear and pays his value, he does not become his owner by consensus. The reason is that ownership is legitimate and usurpation is illegitimate, and an illegitimate thing cannot be a cause for attaining a legitimate thing.

He said: 'And for us, that he has owned... etc.' - Our proof is that the owner has fully acquired the substitute for the usurped property, i.e., its value. And when a person becomes the owner of the substitute, the original leaves his ownership and enters the ownership of the owner of the substitute, so that the owner of the substitute does not suffer loss. However, this requires that the original be capable of transfer from one ownership to another, and this condition is present here: the original is transferable, unlike the mudabbar, which is not transferable, so they differ.

He said: 'Yes, sometimes... etc.' - This is a response to an objection. The objection is that the mudabbar is also transferable, for if the master sells him and the buyer disputes, and the judge decrees the validity of the sale, the sale is valid and the tadbir is annulled, and the buyer takes the mudabbar.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on a fundamental issue in the law of usurpation (ghasb). The Hanafi position (with Malik) holds that when a usurper takes a specific item ('ayn) and then makes it disappear, and the owner accepts its value as compensation, the usurper becomes the owner of the item. Imam al-Shafi'i (and Ahmad) disagree, arguing that usurpation is a wrongful act (عدوان محض) and cannot serve as a valid cause for ownership, just as in the case of a mudabbar slave (whose emancipation is tied to the master's death) — if such a slave is usurped and lost, and the value is paid, the usurper does not become owner by consensus. The Hanafi response is grounded in the principle of substitution (بَدَل): once the owner has fully received the substitute (the value), the original (the item) must leave his ownership to avoid double compensation. This transfer is possible because the usurped item is freely transferable (قابل للنقل). The mudabbar is distinguished because it is not freely transferable due to the slave's right to emancipation upon the master's death; the tadbir restricts transfer. The commentator then addresses an objection: even a mudabbar can become transferable if a judge annuls the tadbir in a sale dispute. However, the Hanafi response clarifies that this is a secondary scenario; the initial ruling stands because before such annulment, the mudabbar is not transferable. Thus, the key difference lies in the transferability of the item. The Hanafi school prioritizes the principle of preventing loss (دفع ضرر) and the completion of the exchange (ملك البدل بكماله).

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Substitute or compensation; in this context, the value (qimah) paid by the usurper to the owner.
مبدل (mubdal): The original item that was usurped; its ownership is transferred upon receipt of the badal.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose emancipation is deferred to the master's death; such a slave is not freely transferable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key distinguishing factor ('illa) that allows the usurper to become owner of the usurped item according to the Hanafi school?
A) The usurper's payment of value
B) The item must be freely transferable (qabil li al-naql)
C) The owner's consent after the fact
D) The usurper's repentance

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the usurper becomes owner upon paying value because the owner has fully received the substitute (badal) and the item is transferable, distinguishing it from non-transferable items like mudabbar.

Ownership Transfer When Usurper Pays Value
Inter-madhhab dispute on ownership transfer after compensation for usurped property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that a usurper becomes owner upon paying the value, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the mudabbar analogy.

Core Idea
Ownership transfers to the usurper when he pays the value — the substitute replaces the original.

When a person usurps property and it is lost, the owner may claim its value. But does paying the value transfer ownership to the usurper? The Hanafi school, along with Imam Malik, answers yes, while the Shafi'i school disagrees. This lesson explores the reasoning behind each position and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the usurper becomes owner of the lost object when he pays its value to the original owner.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Identify the opponent's view
State the Shafi'i (and Hanbali) position: the usurper does not become owner because usurpation is pure aggression and cannot be a cause for ownership.
They analogize to the case of a mudabbar slave.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Explain the Shafi'i analogy: just as usurping a mudabbar does not lead to ownership even after paying value, so too with any usurped object.
Mudabbar: a slave whose emancipation is deferred until the master's death.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal: the mudabbar is not analogous because it is not freely transferable due to the master's right of tadbir. The ordinary usurped object is transferable, and ownership of the substitute (value) entails transfer of the original to the payer.
Additionally, ownership is based on payment of compensation, not on the usurpation itself.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the object is later found, the Hanafi school says it belongs to the usurper; the Shafi'i school says it belongs to the original owner, who must return the value.
This affects real-world disputes over lost property.

Source Text

اگر غاصب نے کوئی چیز غصب کر کے اس کو غائب کر دیا۔ اور مالک کو اس کی قیمت کا تاوان دے دیا تو ہمارے اور امام مالک کے نزدیک غاصب اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ امام شافعی اور امام احمد کے نزدیک مالک نہ ہو گا۔ وہ یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ غصب ظلم محض ہے جو نعمت ملک کا سبب نہیں ہو سکتا۔ جیسے کوئی مد بر غلام کو غصب کر کے غائب کر دے اور اس کی قیمت کا تاوان دیدے تو وہ بالا تفاق اس کا مالک نہیں ہوتا۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ ملک مشروع ہے اور غصب غیر مشروع ہے اور جو امر غیر مشروع ہو دہ مشروع کے حصول کا سبب نہیں ہوتا۔ قوله ولنا انه ملک..... الخ - ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مالک فی مغصوب کے بدل یعنی اس کی قیمت کا بطریق کمال مالک ہو چکا اور جو شخص بدل کا مالک ہو جاتا ہے تو مبدل اس کی ملک سے خارج ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور صاحب بدل کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو جاتا ہے تا کہ مالک بدل کا نقصان لازم نہ آئے ۔ البتہ اس کے لئے یہ ضروری ہے کہ مبدل میں ایک سے دوسری ملک کی طرف منتقل ہونے کی صلاحیت ہو اور یہاں یہ شرط موجود ہے۔ یعنی مبدل قابل نقل ہے بخلاف مدبر کے کہ وہ قابل نقل نہیں فافتر قا۔ قوله نعم قد يفسخ ... الخ - ایک اشکال کا جواب ہے۔ اشکال یہ ہے کہ قابل نقل تو مدبر بھی ہے۔ چنانچہ آقا اگر اس کو فروخت کر دے اور مشتری تسلیم مدیر کا مخاصمہ کرے اور قاضی اس کی بیچ کے جواز کا فیصلہ کر دے تو بیع جائز اور تدبیر سخ ہو جاتی ہے اور مشتری اس مد بر کو لے لیتا ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل ہ یہ ہے کہ ہاں بات تو یہی ہے۔ کبھی ایسا ہوتا ہے کہ قاضی کے حکم سے مدبر ہونا فسخ کر دیا جاتا ہے پر اس کے بعد جو بیچ واقع ہوتی ہے وہ محض مملوک پر واقع ہوتی ہے۔ پس یہ نقل مد بر نہ ہوا بلکہ نقل فن ہوا۔ فائدہ صاحب عنایہ نے شرح کلام کے بعد لکھا ہے کہ صاحب ہدایہ کا کلام اس طرف مشیر ہے کہ ملک کا سبب وہی غصب ہے۔ ورنہ امام شافعی کی طرف سے مذکورہ تعلیل نا مناسب ہوگی۔ قاضی ابو زید د بوسی کا مذہب یہی ہے ۔ چنانچہ موصوف نے کتاب الاسرار میں ہمارے علماء کا قول ذکر کیا ہے کہ قضاء بالضمان یا تراضی کے وقت غصب مفید ملک ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن شمس الائمہ نے مبسوط میں کہا ہے کہ یہ بنی بروہم ہے اس لئے کہ اداء عمان کے وقت غاصب کیلئے غصب کے وقت سے ملک حقیقہ ثابت نہیں ہوتی اسی لئے مغضوب شی کے زوائد اس کو سپر دنہیں کئے جاتے۔ اگر ملک کا سبب غصب ہی ہوتا تو اس سبب کے ذریعہ سے ملک نام ہو جانے کے بعد غاصب زوائد متصلہ و منفصلہ کا بھی مالک ہو جاتا حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے۔ مگر بعض حضرات نے اس کا جواب دیا ہے کہ اداء ضمان کے وقت غصب کے سبب ملک ہونے کا یہ مطلب نہیں ہے کہ وہ علی الاطلاق موجب ملک ہوتا ہے بلکہ اس کا سبب ملک ہونا بطریق استناد ہوتا ہے جو من وجہ ثابت اور من وجہ غیر ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے زوائد منفصلہ میں اس کا کوئی اثر ظاہر نہ ہوگا۔
Section: And whoever usurps an object and causes it to disappear, then the owner takes its value as compensation, he (the usurper) becomes its owner. This is according to us. Al-Shafi'i said: He does not become its owner, because usurpation is pure aggression, so it is not suitable as a cause for ownership, like the mudabbar. And our proof is that he (the owner) has fully owned the substitute, and the substituted object is capable of transfer from one ownership to another, so he (the usurper) becomes its owner to remove harm from him, unlike the mudabbar, because it is not capable of transfer due to the right of tadbir. Yes, tadbir may be annulled by judicial decree, but the sale after that occurs on a pure slave.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether a usurper (ghasib) becomes the owner of a usurped object after it is lost and he pays its value (al-qimah) as compensation (daman). The Hanafi position, shared by Imam Malik, is that the usurper does become owner. The Shafi'i and Hanbali positions hold that he does not. The Shafi'i argument is that usurpation (ghasb) is pure transgression, which cannot be a legitimate cause for ownership. They analogize to a mudabbar (a slave whose emancipation is deferred after the master's death): if someone usurps a mudabbar and it is lost, paying its value does not transfer ownership, by consensus. The Hanafi response is that the owner has fully received the substitute (badal), which is the value, and the original object (mubdal) is transferable. To prevent harm to the owner (who might otherwise lose both object and value), ownership transfers to the usurper. The exception of the mudabbar is because it is not freely transferable due to the master's right of tadbir. The passage then addresses an objection: a mudabbar can be sold if the master sells it and the buyer contests, and the judge allows the sale, annulling the tadbir. The answer is that in that case, the sale occurs on the slave as a pure slave after the tadbir is annulled; it is not a transfer of the mudabbar as such. The commentator also notes a difference of opinion among later Hanafi scholars about whether the cause of ownership is the usurpation itself or the payment of compensation. The relied-upon view (as per Hidayah) is that ownership is established at the time of payment, not from the moment of usurpation. This is supported by the fact that the usurper does not become owner of the accrued increments (zawa'id) of the object that occurred before payment.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation: taking another's property without right and with aggression.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose emancipation is deferred until after the master's death.
بدل (badal): Substitute or compensation; here, the value (qimah) paid by the usurper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a usurper become the owner of a lost usurped object?
A) At the moment of usurpation
B) When he pays its value to the owner
C) Never, because usurpation is a sin
D) Only if the owner agrees to the sale

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, payment of the full value of a lost usurped object transfers ownership to the usurper, based on the principle of substitute (badal) and to prevent harm.

Whose Statement is Accepted Regarding the Value of Usurped Property
Ruling on acceptance of usurper's statement with oath and its consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi evidentiary rule for valuing usurped property and apply it to scenarios where the original object reappears, distinguishing between cases where the owner's consent was full or partial.

Core Idea
The usurper's word with oath sets the value unless the owner proves otherwise; if the object reappears, the owner's rights depend on how the value was determined.

When a usurped object is damaged or destroyed, the value must be determined. But who decides the amount? In Hanafi law, the principle is that the denier's statement with oath is accepted. The owner may override this only with proof. This passage from al-Hidayah explores what happens if the original object is later found: does the owner get it back, or keep the payment? The answer hinges on whether the owner fully consented to the valuation process.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default evidentiary rule
Note that the usurper's statement about the value is accepted when supported by his oath, because the owner claims a higher value and the usurper denies it. This follows the general principle that the denier's (munkir) word is taken with oath.
The owner's claim alone is not sufficient; he must provide evidence to override the usurper's statement.
2
Understand the owner's recourse with proof
If the owner produces conclusive evidence (bayyinah) of a higher value, the usurper's statement is overridden, and the payment is based on the owner's proof.
This is because evidence (bayyinah) is a compelling proof (hujjah mulzimah) that establishes the fact definitively.
3
Analyze the scenarios when the object reappears
The passage distinguishes two situations: (1) when the value was set based on the owner's claim (by his own statement, his proof, or the usurper's refusal to swear), and (2) when it was set based on the usurper's statement with oath.
In the first case, the owner has no option; ownership is complete because his consent attached to that amount. In the second, the owner has an option (khiyar) because his consent was incomplete.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Al-Karkhi held that if the reappearing object is equal or less in value, the owner has no option. The zahir al-riwayah position, declared al-ashah by al-Marghinani, gives the owner an option in all such cases.
The difference hinges on whether the option is based on loss or on incomplete consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال القول فى القيمة قول الغاصب مع يمينه لان المالك يدعى الزيادة وهو ينكر والقول قول المنكر مع يمينه، الا ان يقيم المالك البيئة باكثر من ذلك لانه اثبته بالحجة الملزمة. قال فان ظهرت العين وقيمتها اكثر مما ضمن وقد ضمنها بقول المالك و ببينة اقامها او بنكول الغاصب عن اليمين فلا خيار للمالك وهو للغاصب لانه تم له الملك بسبب اتصل به رضاء المالك حيث ادعى هذا المقدار . قال فان كان ضمنه بقول الغاصب مع يمينه فهو بالخيار ان شاء امضى الضمان وان شاء اخذ العين ورد العوض، لانه لم يتم رضاه بهذ المقدار حيث يدعى الزيادة واخذه دونها لعدم الحجة، ولو ظهرت العين وقيمتها مثل ما ضمنه او دونه في هذ الفصل الاخير، فكذلك الجواب فى ظاهر الرواية وهو الاصح خلافا لما قاله الكرخى انه لا خيار له لانه لم يتم رضاه حيث لم يعط له ما يدعيه والخيار لفوات الرضاء. ترجمہ اور قیمت کے بارے میں قول غاصب کا مقبول ہوگا اس کی قسم کے ساتھ کیونکہ مالک زیادتی کا مدعی ہے اور غاصب اس کا انکا کرتا ہے اور قول منکر مقبول ہوتا ہے اس کی قسم کے ساتھ ۔ مگر مالک بینہ قائم کر دے اس سے زیادہ کا۔ کیونکہ اس نے حجت ملزمہ سے ثابت کر دیا۔ پھر اگر عین مال ظاہر ہوا۔ اور حال یہ کہ اس کی قیمت اس سے زیادہ ہے جو غاصب نے تاوان دی اور وہ اس کا ضامن مالک کے کہنے یا اس کے بینہ قائم کرنے یا قسم سے غاصب کے انکار کرنے سے ہوا تھا تو مالک کے لئے کوئی اختیار نہ ہوگا اور وہ چیز غاصب کی ہوگی. کیونکہ اس نے اسی مقدار کا دعوی کیا تھا۔ اور اگر مالک نے غاصب کے قول مع قسم پر تاوان لیا ہو تو اس کو اختیار ہوگا چاہیے تاوان مذکور جان کھنے اور چاہے مال عین لے لے اور عوض واپس کر دے۔ کیونکہ اس مقدار کے ساتھ اس کی رضامندی پوری نہیں ہوئی تھی اس لئے کہ
He said: The statement regarding the value is the statement of the usurper with his oath, because the owner claims an increase and he denies, and the statement of the denier is accepted with his oath, unless the owner establishes evidence for more than that, because he has proven it by a compelling proof. He said: If the object appears and its value is more than what he paid, and he had paid based on the owner's statement, or on evidence he produced, or on the usurper's refusal [nukul] to take an oath, then the owner has no option, and it is for the usurper, because ownership was completed for him due to the owner's consent being attached to it, since he (the owner) claimed this amount. He said: If he paid based on the usurper's statement with his oath, then he (the owner) has an option: if he wishes he may uphold the payment, and if he wishes he may take the object and return the compensation, because his consent to this amount was not complete, since he claims an increase and took it without proof. And if the object appears and its value is like what he paid or less in this last case, the answer is the same in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), and this is the more correct, contrary to what al-Karkhi said that he has no option, because his consent was not complete since he was not given what he claims, and the option is for the loss of consent.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on a procedural issue: when the value of a usurped object is disputed, whose statement is accepted? The default principle is that the denier's (munkir) word is accepted with oath. Since the owner claims a higher value and the usurper denies, the usurper's statement (with oath) is taken as correct. However, the owner can override this by producing evidence (bayyinah) of a higher value. The passage then discusses various scenarios that arise if the original object (al-'ayn) is later found. If the value had been determined based on the owner's claim (either by his own statement, his evidence, or the usurper's refusal to swear), and the object's actual value is higher, the owner has no option to take back the object; it belongs to the usurper. This is because the owner consented to that amount. But if the value was set based on the usurper's statement with oath, and the actual value is higher, then the owner has an option (khiyar): he may either accept the payment as is or take back the object and return the payment. This option exists because his consent was not fully given to that lower amount. If the actual value is equal to or less than what was paid, the same option applies in the relied-upon narration (zahir al-riwayah), contrary to al-Karkhi who held no option because the owner's consent was incomplete. The Hanafi school follows the principle that consent must be complete for the transfer to be irrevocable.

Key Terms
قول الغاصب مع يمينه (qawl al-ghasib ma'a yaminihi): The statement of the usurper supported by his oath; it is accepted in determining the value of the usurped object.
خيار (khiyar): Option; the owner's choice to either accept the payment or reclaim the object upon its reappearance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the usurper's statement with oath was used to determine the value, and the original object later appears with a higher value, what option does the owner have?
A) He must accept the object and return the payment
B) He may either accept the payment or take back the object and return the payment
C) He has no option; the object belongs to the usurper
D) He can demand additional payment from the usurper

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of the usurper's statement with oath is conditional; if the object reappears, the owner's consent is key: full consent (when value set by his own claim) makes transfer irrevocable; partial consent (when set by usurper's oath) gives the owner an option.

Does Usurpation (Ghaṣb) Cause Ownership Upon Compensation?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on causation of ownership via usurpation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two intra-Hanafi positions on whether usurpation itself is the cause of ownership upon compensation and identify the practical consequence regarding owned increases.

Core Idea
Usurpation is not an absolute cause of ownership; compensation triggers ownership only in a derivative sense.

The relationship between usurpation (ghaṣb) and ownership is subtle. This passage presents a debate within the Hanafi school: does the act of usurpation itself, once compensated, make the usurper the owner from the time of the wrongful taking? Or is ownership established only at the moment of compensation, with the earlier usurpation serving as a mere occasion? Understanding this distinction has direct implications for who owns any increases that accrued on the usurped property before compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Positions
First, recognize that Qāḍī Abū Zayd and the author of al-Hidāyah hold that the cause of ownership is the usurpation itself at the time of judgment or agreement. Second, note that Shams al-Aʾimmah al-Sarakhsī rejects this, arguing that true ownership does not date back to the usurpation.
Both are Hanafi scholars; this is an intra-madhhab dispute.
2
Analyze Each Dalīl
For the first view, the proof is that otherwise Imām al-Shāfiʿī’s objection would be misdirected. For the second, the proof is that if usurpation were the cause, the usurper would own all increases from the moment of usurpation, which is contrary to the ruling that disconnected increases are not owned.
The core of the dispute is the legal effect of the act of usurpation.
3
Understand the Response (Istiqnād)
Some scholars answer the second objection by distinguishing 'absolute causation' from 'causation by attribution' (istiqnād). Ownership is established at compensation but is attributed back to the usurpation only in a limited way – it is valid from one aspect but not from another.
This nuanced solution preserves the idea that the usurpation is a cause without making the usurper the owner of all increases.
4
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilāf)
The practical difference is whether the usurper owns disconnected increases that occurred before compensation. According to the first view, yes; according to the second (and the preferred opinion), no. Connected increases (e.g., natural growth) may be treated differently based on other rules.
The dispute is not fully settled; later Hanafi practice tends to follow al-Sarakhsī.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب کا حاصل ہ یہ ہے کہ ہاں بات تو یہی ہے۔ کبھی ایسا ہوتا ہے کہ قاضی کے حکم سے مدبر ہونا فسخ کر دیا جاتا ہے پر اس کے بعد جو بیچ واقع ہوتی ہے وہ محض مملوک پر واقع ہوتی ہے۔ پس یہ نقل مد بر نہ ہوا بلکہ نقل فن ہوا۔ فائدہ صاحب عنایہ نے شرح کلام کے بعد لکھا ہے کہ صاحب ہدایہ کا کلام اس طرف مشیر ہے کہ ملک کا سبب وہی غصب ہے۔ ورنہ امام شافعی کی طرف سے مذکورہ تعلیل نا مناسب ہوگی۔ قاضی ابو زید د بوسی کا مذہب یہی ہے ۔ چنانچہ موصوف نے کتاب الاسرار میں ہمارے علماء کا قول ذکر کیا ہے کہ قضاء بالضمان یا تراضی کے وقت غصب مفید ملک ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن شمس الائمہ نے مبسوط میں کہا ہے کہ یہ بنی بروہم ہے اس لئے کہ اداء ضمان کے وقت غاصب کیلئے غصب کے وقت سے ملک حقیقہ ثابت نہیں ہوتی اسی لئے مغضوب شی کے زوائد اس کو سپرد نہیں کئے جاتے۔ اگر ملک کا سبب غصب ہی ہوتا تو اس سبب کے ذریعہ سے ملک نام ہو جانے کے بعد غاصب زوائد متصلہ و منفصلہ کا بھی مالک ہو جاتا حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے۔
مگر بعض حضرات نے اس کا جواب دیا ہے کہ اداء ضمان کے وقت غصب کے سبب ملک ہونے کا یہ مطلب نہیں ہے کہ وہ علی الاطلاق موجب ملک ہوتا ہے بلکہ اس کا سبب ملک ہونا بطریق استناد ہوتا ہے جو من وجہ ثابت اور من وجہ غیر ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے زوائد منفصلہ میں اس کا کوئی اثر ظاہر نہ ہوگا۔
The summary of the answer is that yes, this is the case. Sometimes it happens that by the judge's order the tadbīr is annulled, and then the sale that occurs takes place on the owned property. Thus this is not a transfer of the mudabbar but a transfer of property. Benefit: The author of al-ʿInāyah wrote after explaining the text that the statement of the author of al-Hidāyah indicates that the cause of ownership is the usurpation itself. Otherwise, the mentioned reasoning from Imām al-Shāfiʿī would be inappropriate. This is the madhhab of Qāḍī Abū Zayd al-Dabūsī. Accordingly, he mentioned in Kitāb al-Asrār the statement of our scholars that at the time of judgment for compensation or mutual agreement, usurpation is effective for ownership. However, Shams al-Aʾimmah said in al-Mabsūṭ that this is based on a doubt, because at the time of paying the compensation, true ownership is not established for the usurper from the time of usurpation. For this reason, the increases of the usurped property are not given over to him. If the cause of ownership were the usurpation itself, then after ownership is established by this cause, the usurper would also own the connected and disconnected increases, but this is not the case. But some scholars have answered this by saying that at the time of paying compensation, the meaning of ownership by the cause of usurpation is not that it is absolutely a cause of ownership, but rather its being a cause of ownership is by way of attribution (istiqnād), which is established from one aspect and not established from another aspect. Therefore, its effect will not appear in the disconnected increases.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the nature of ownership when a usurper compensates the owner. The author of al-Hidāyah suggests that the cause of ownership is the usurpation itself, which is supported by Qāḍī Abū Zayd al-Dabūsī in Kitāb al-Asrār. However, Shams al-Aʾimmah al-Sarakhsī in al-Mabsūṭ objects that if usurpation were the direct cause, the usurper would own the increases from the moment of usurpation, which is not the case. In response, some scholars clarify that ownership is established only at the time of compensation, and the causation is not absolute but relative (min wajh). Hence, disconnected increases are not owned by the usurper.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation: taking another's property without right, which obligates compensation.
ملک (milk): Ownership; the legal dominion over a property.
ضمان (ḍamān): Compensation or guarantee; here, the payment made by the usurper to the owner.
استناد (istiqnād): Attribution; a cause that is effective only in a relative sense, not absolutely.
زوائد منفصلہ (zawāʾid munfaṣilah): Disconnected increases; such as offspring or fruit that is separate from the principal property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the practical consequence of al-Sarakhsī's position that usurpation is not the cause of ownership?
A) The usurper owns the property from the time of usurpation, but must pay compensation.
B) The usurper does not own any increases that occurred before compensation.
C) The usurper owns both connected and disconnected increases, but not the principal.
D) The usurper must return the property and does not own it even after compensation.

Key Takeaway
Ownership through usurpation is not automatic upon compensation; the dominant view limits ownership to the principal and does not extend to disconnected increases.

Ruling on the Usurper’s Statement of Value and the Owner’s Option Upon Reappearance
Detailed rulings on evidence and option in usurpation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule for accepting the usurper's statement on value, distinguish the three scenarios of compensation determination, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the owner's option when the property reappears with equal or lesser value.

Core Idea
The usurper's statement with oath is accepted as denier, but the owner's option upon reappearance hinges on how compensation was determined.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical dispute: when a usurped property is destroyed, and later the property reappears, who decides its value and does the owner have a choice to take it back? The general evidentiary rule places the burden on the owner to prove a higher value, but the compensation method affects subsequent options. The author also presents a nuanced disagreement within the Hanafi school between the relied-upon Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and Imām al-Karkhī, centering on the completeness of the owner's consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general evidentiary rule
Recognize that in a dispute over the value of usurped property, the usurper's statement with oath is accepted because he is the denier, unless the owner brings conclusive evidence.
This is based on the principle 'al-bayyinah ʿalā al-muddaʿī wa al-yamīn ʿalā al-munkir'.
2
List the three methods of compensation determination
The text categorizes compensation based on: (1) owner's statement/evidence or usurper's refusal to swear, (2) usurper's own statement with oath, leading to different consequences when property reappears.
These are not mutually exclusive; they are distinct scenarios.
3
Apply the rule to each scenario
If compensation was based on owner's claim/evidence/refusal, the owner has no option if property reappears with higher value; if based on usurper's oath, the owner has an option to take back the property or keep compensation.
The key is whether the owner's consent was perfected or not.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
When the reappeared property's value equals or is less than compensation (paid based on usurper's oath), Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah gives the owner an option, while al-Karkhī denies it. Identify each imam's reasoning.
Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is the muftā bihī position.
5
Understand the rationale behind the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah position
The option exists because the owner's consent was not complete; he claimed more and only accepted due to lack of evidence, not because he was satisfied with that amount.
The commentary also compares with the depositee to clarify evidentiary distinctions.

Source Text

مغصوبہ کی قیمت کے بارے میں غاصب کا قول معتبر ہو گا تم کے ساتھ
قال القول فى القيمة قول الغاصب مع يمينه لان المالك يدعى الزيادة وهو ينكر والقول قول المنكر مع يمينه، الا ان يقيم المالك البيئة باكثر من ذلك لانه اثبته بالحجة الملزمة. قال فان ظهرت العين وقيمتها اكثر مما ضمن وقد ضمنها بقول المالك و ببينة اقامها او بنكول الغاصب عن اليمين فلا خيار للمالك وهو للغاصب لانه تم له الملك بسبب اتصل به رضاء المالك حيث ادعى هذا المقدار . قال فان كان ضمنه بقول الغاصب مع يمينه فهو بالخيار ان شاء امضى الضمان وان شاء اخذ العين ورد العوض، لانه لم يتم رضاه بهذ المقدار حيث يدعى الزيادة واخذه دونها لعدم الحجة، ولو ظهرت العين وقيمتها مثل ما ضمنه او دونه في هذ الفصل الاخير، فكذلك الجواب فى ظاهر الرواية وهو الاصح خلافا لما قاله الكرخى انه لا خيار له لانه لم يتم رضاه حيث لم يعط له ما يدعيه والخيار لفوات الرضاء
ترجمہ اور قیمت کے بارے میں قول غاصب کا مقبول ہوگا اس کی قسم کے ساتھ کیونکہ مالک زیادتی کا مدعی ہے اور غاصب اس کا انکا کرتا ہے اور قول منکر مقبول ہوتا ہے اس کی قسم کے ساتھ ۔ مگر مالک بینہ قائم کر دے اس سے زیادہ کا۔ کیونکہ اس نے حجت ملزمہ سے ثابت کر دیا۔ پھر اگر عین مال ظاہر ہوا۔ اور حال یہ کہ اس کی قیمت اس سے زیادہ ہے جو غاصب نے تاوان دی اور وہ اس کا ضامن مالک کے کہنے یا اس کے بینہ قائم کرنے یا قسم سے غاصب کے انکار کرنے سے ہوا تھا تو مالک کے لئے کوئی اختیار نہ ہوگا اور وہ چیز غاصب کی ہوگی. کیونکہ اس نے اسی مقدار کا دعوی کیا تھا۔ اور اگر مالک نے غاصب کے قول مع قسم پر تاوان لیا ہو تو اس کو اختیار ہوگا چاہیے تاوان مذکور جان کھنے اور چاہے مال عین لے لے اور عوض واپس کر دے۔ کیونکہ اس مقدار کے ساتھ اس کی رضامندی پوری نہیں ہوئی تھی اس لئے کہ زیادہ کا مدعی تھا۔ اور زیادتی کے بغیر لینا حجت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے تھا۔ اور اگر مال عین ظاہر ہوا اس حال میں کہ اس کی قیمت اس کے برابر ہے جو غاصب نے ادا کی یا اس سے کم ہے اس آخری صورت میں تو جواب یوں ہی ہے ظاہر الروایۃ میں اور یہی اصح ہے برخلاف اس کے جو امام کرخی نے کہا ہے کہ مالک کے لئے اختیار نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کی رضا مندی پوری نہیں ہوئی بایں معنی کہ اس کو وہ نہیں دیا گیا جس کا وہ دعوی کرتا تھا اور اختیار کا ہونا فوات رضا ء ہی کی وجہ سے ہے۔ تشریح قوله والقول فى القيمة ... الخ - اگر مالک اور غاصب کے درمیان قیمت کے بارے میں اختلاف ہو تو غاصب کا قول اس کی قسم کے ساتھ مقبول ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مالک مدعی زیادہ ہے اور غاصب اس کا منکر ہے اور قول منکر ہی کا معتبر ہوتا ہے اس کی قسم کے ساتھ ہاں اگر مالک اس سے زیادہ قیمت ہونے پر بلینہ قائم کر دے تو اس کا بینہ مقبول ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ اس نے حجت ملزمہ سے ثابت کر دیا۔ فائدہ اگر مالک اقامت بینہ سے عاجز ہو جائے اور غاصب سے قسم کا مطالبہ کرے۔ جب کہ غاصب کے پاس ایسا مبینہ موجود ہے جو قیمت منصوب کے لئے شاہد ہے تو غاصب کامبینہ مقبول نہ ہوگا بلکہ اس سے قسم ہی لی جائے گی اس لئے کہ اس کا مبینہ نافی زیادہ ہے۔ اور جو بینہ نفی پر ہو وہ مقبول نہیں ہوتا۔ پھر بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ اسقاط یمین کے لئے غاصب کا مبینہ مقبول ہونا چاہیے جیسے مودع اگر ودیعت کا دعوی کرے تو اس کا قول مقبول ہوتا ہے اور اگر وہ اس پر بینہ قائم کرے تو بینہ بھی مقبول ہوتا ہے۔ قاضی ابو علی نفی کہتے تھے کہ یہ مسئلہ مشکل شمار کیا گیا ہے اور بعض مشائخ نے ان دونوں میں فرق کیا ہے اور یہی صحیح پہلے اس لئے کہ مودع کے ذمہ صرف دعوی ہے جس کو اس نے بینہ قائم کر کے ساقط کر دیا اور خصومت جاتی رہی۔ رہا غاصب سو اس پر یہاں یمین اور قیمت دو چیزیں لازم ہیں اور اقامت بینہ سے صرف یمین ساقط ہوئی ہے پس غاصب مودع کے معنی میں نہیں ہے۔
قوله فان ظهرت ... الخ - پھر اگر شی مغصوب کسی وقت ظاہر ہو اور اس کی قیمت اس مقدار سے زائد ہو جس کا غاصب نے تاوان دیا ہے اور تاوان بھی مالک کے قول کے مطابق یا اس کے بینہ کے مطابق یا اپنے انکار قسم کے سبب سے دیا ہے تو شی مغصوب غاصب کی مملوک ہوگی اور مالک کو اس میں اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مالک اسی مقدار کا مدعی تھا اور اس پر راضی ہو چکا تھا اور اگر غاصب نے اپنے قول کے موافق قسم کھا کر تاوان دیا ہو تو مالک کو اختیار ہوگا چاہے شی مغصوب لے کر اس کا ضمان واپس کر دے۔ اور چاہے اس ضمان کو برقرار رکھے۔ کیونکہ اس مقدار کے ساتھ اس کی رضا مندی پوری نہیں ہوئی تھی اس لئے کہ وہ زیادہ کا دعی تھا اور بغیر زیادتی کے لے لینا صرف اس وجہ سے تھا کہ اس کے پاس بینہ نہیں تھا۔ میں رضا مندی ثابت نہ ہوئی۔
قوله ولو ظهرت العين .... الخ ۔ اور اگر قسم کے ساتھ غاصب کے کہنے پر تاوان لینے کی صورت میں جب مال ظاہر ہوا اور اس کی قیمت اس مقدار کے برابر ہے جو غاصب نے اداء کی تھی یا اس سے کم ہے تو امام کرخی کے نزدیک مالک کو واپس لینے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مالک کو اس کی ملک کا پورا بدل مل چکا۔ لیکن ظاہر الروایۃ میں اس کو اختیار ہے کہ اگر چاہے مال عین واپس لے کر نتاوان پھیر دے۔ اور یہی اصح ہے کیونکہ اصل یعنی مبسوط میں مطلقاً یہی مذکور ہے۔ اسی طرح امام طحاوی نے بھی روایت کو مطلق ہی ذکر کیا ہے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ مالک کی رضا مندی پوری نہیں ہوئی۔ اس لئے کہ مالک کا جو دھویا تھا وہ اس کو نہیں دیا گیا اور اختیار اسی لئے حاصل ہوا کہ اس کی رضامندی پوری نہیں ہوئی نہ اس لئے کہ اس کی قیمت پوری نہیں۔
Regarding the value, the statement of the usurper with his oath is accepted, because the owner claims an increase and he denies, and the statement of the denier is accepted with his oath, unless the owner provides evidence for more than that, because he has proven it with a compelling proof. He said: If the property appears and its value is more than what he compensated, and he compensated it by the owner's statement or by his establishing evidence or by the usurper's refusal to swear, then there is no option for the owner, and it belongs to the usurper, because ownership has been perfected for him by a cause connected with the owner's consent, since he claimed this amount. He said: If he compensated by the usurper's statement with his oath, then he has the option: if he wishes he may confirm the compensation, and if he wishes he may take the property and return the compensation, because his consent with this amount was not perfected, since he claimed the increase and took without it due to lack of evidence. And if the property appears and its value is like what he compensated or less, in this last case the answer is the same in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, and it is the more correct view, contrary to what al-Karkhī said that he has no option, because his consent was not perfected since he was not given what he claimed, and the option is due to the absence of consent. Translation: And regarding the value, the statement of the usurper is accepted with his oath because the owner claims an increase and the usurper denies it, and the statement of the denier is accepted with his oath. But if the owner establishes evidence for more than that, it is accepted because he has proven it with a compelling proof. Then if the property appears and its value is greater than the compensation paid, and the compensation was based on the owner's statement, his evidence, or the usurper's refusal to swear, then the owner has no option, and the property belongs to the usurper, because he claimed that amount and consented. And if the owner took compensation based on the usurper's statement with oath, then he has the option: either keep the compensation or take the property and return the compensation, because his consent with that amount was not complete, as he claimed more and only took without increase due to lack of evidence. And if the property appears with a value equal to or less than the compensation, in this last case the answer is the same in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, and it is the more correct view, contrary to what Imām al-Karkhī said that he has no option, because his consent was not complete in the sense that he was not given what he claimed, and the option is due to the absence of consent. Commentary: If there is a dispute between the owner and the usurper regarding the value, the usurper's statement with his oath is accepted, because the owner is the claimant of excess and the usurper is the denier, and the statement of the denier is accepted with his oath. However, if the owner establishes evidence for a higher value, his evidence is accepted because he has proven it with a compelling proof. Benefit: If the owner is unable to provide evidence and demands an oath from the usurper, and the usurper has evidence that shows the value he claims, that evidence is not accepted; rather the oath is required, because his evidence is to negate excess, and evidence to negate is not accepted. Then some mashāyikh said that for dropping the oath, the usurper's evidence should be accepted, like the depositee (mūdaʿ) if he claims that the deposit was lost, his statement is accepted, and if he brings evidence, it is also accepted. Qāḍī Abū ʿAlī al-Nafī used to say that this issue is considered difficult, and some mashāyikh distinguished between the two, and that is correct: first because the depositee only has a claim which he dropped by bringing evidence, so the dispute ends. As for the usurper, here two things are obligatory: the oath and the value, and by bringing evidence only the oath is dropped, so the usurper is not like the depositee. His statement: "If the property appears..." - If the usurped property appears at some time and its value is more than the amount the usurper paid as compensation, and the compensation was according to the owner's statement or his evidence or due to the usurper's refusal to swear, then the usurped property becomes owned by the usurper and the owner has no option, because the owner claimed that amount and was satisfied with it. And if the usurper paid compensation according to his own statement after swearing, then the owner has the option: either take the property and return the compensation, or keep the compensation. Because his satisfaction with that amount was not complete, as he claimed more and only took without increase because he had no evidence. His statement: "And if the property appears..." - In the case where compensation was taken based on the usurper's statement with oath, when the property appears and its value is equal to or less than the compensation paid, according to Imām al-Karkhī, the owner does not have the option to take it back, because the owner has received the full replacement of his property. But in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, he has the option: if he wishes, he may take the property and return the compensation. And this is the more correct view, because the original (al-Mabsūṭ) mentions this absolutely. Similarly, Imām al-Ṭaḥāwī mentioned the narration absolutely. The reason is that the owner's consent was not complete, because what the owner claimed was not given to him, and the option arises from the incompleteness of consent, not from the insufficiency of value.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rules for disputes over the value of usurped property and what happens when the property reappears. The general rule is that the usurper's statement with oath is accepted because he is the denier, unless the owner provides evidence. Then three scenarios are discussed based on how the compensation was determined. If compensation was based on the owner's claim, evidence, or the usurper's refusal to swear, the owner has no option and the property belongs to the usurper if it appears with a higher value. If compensation was based on the usurper's own statement with oath, the owner has the option to take back the property or keep compensation. If the value is equal or less, in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah the owner still has the option, contrary to Imam al-Karkhī. The commentary also discusses a nuance: if the usurper has evidence to support his value, it is not accepted to avoid the oath because it is negative evidence. A comparison with the depositee is made: the depositee's evidence is accepted because it ends the dispute, but the usurper's evidence only drops the oath, not the liability. The author of al-Hidāyah follows Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah giving the owner an option even when value equals compensation, based on the principle that consent was not fully given for that amount.

Key Terms
قول القيمة (qawl al-qīmah): The statement regarding the value of the usurped property; whose assertion is accepted in case of dispute.
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The well-known transmitted rulings from the six books of Imam Muḥammad al-Shaybānī.
الكرخي (al-Karkhī): Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhī, a Hanafi jurist who held a differing opinion on this issue.
مودع (mūdaʿ): A depositee: one who has been entrusted with a deposit (wadīʿah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following scenarios does the owner have no option to take back the usurped property when it reappears with a higher value?
A) Compensation was based on the usurper's statement with oath.
B) Compensation was based on the owner's statement or evidence, or the usurper's refusal to swear.
C) Compensation was based on the usurper's statement without oath.
D) The owner always has an option regardless of how compensation was determined.

Key Takeaway
The owner's option to reclaim usurped property upon reappearance depends on the method of compensation determination; when based on the usurper's oath, incomplete consent preserves the owner's option even if the value is equal or less.
