Owner's Choice When Usurped Property Reappears After Compensation
Expansion of Hidayah on owner's option after compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the owner's choice (ikhtiyar) when the usurped property reappears after compensation, distinguish the scenarios based on how compensation was paid, and explain the intra-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Karkhi.

Core Idea
The owner's right to reclaim usurped property hinges on the completeness of consent, not the sufficiency of value.

This lesson delves into the nuanced ruling from classical Hanafi fiqh regarding a usurped property (maghsūb) that reappears after the usurper has paid compensation. The central question is whether the owner can reclaim the property and return the compensation. The answer depends crucially on how the compensation was determined and the completeness of the owner's consent. We will also explore an internal Hanafi dispute with Imam al-Karkhi, and learn why the relied-upon position favors the owner's choice even when the property's value is equal to or less than the compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
First, understand the two main scenarios based on how the compensation was paid: (1) based on the owner's own claim or evidence, and (2) based on the usurper's oath (i.e., the owner accepted a lower amount due to lack of proof).
The ruling differs in each scenario.
2
Analyze the effect of consent
The key legal principle is that the owner's consent (riḍā) determines the outcome. If the owner claimed a specific amount and was fully satisfied, ownership transfers to the usurper permanently. If the owner accepted less due to inability to prove his claim, his consent is incomplete.
Incomplete consent preserves the owner's right to reclaim the property.
3
Examine the intra-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Karkhi holds that when the property's value equals or is less than the compensation, the owner has no choice because he received full market value. The majority (Zahir al-Riwayah) disagree, citing that the basis is consent, not value.
The dispute is over the 'illah (legal cause) for the option: consent vs. value.
4
Apply the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is from Zahir al-Riwayah: the owner always has the choice when his consent was incomplete, regardless of the property's value relative to the compensation. This is supported by the absolute narrations in al-Mabsut and al-Tahawi.
This is the more correct (asahh) view.

كتاب الغصب
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ زیادہ کا مدعی تھا۔ اور زیادتی کے بغیر لینا حجت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے تھا۔ اور اگر مال عین ظاہر ہوا اس حال میں کہ اس کی قیمت اس کے برابر ہے جو غاصب نے ادا کی یا اس سے کم ہے اس آخری صورت میں تو جواب یوں ہی ہے ظاہر الروایۃ میں اور یہی اصح ہے برخلاف اس کے جو امام کرخی نے کہا ہے کہ مالک کے لئے اختیار نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کی رضا مندی پوری نہیں ہوئی بایں معنی کہ اس کو وہ نہیں دیا گیا جس کا وہ دعوی کرتا تھا اور اختیار کا ہونا فوات رضا ء ہی کی وجہ سے ہے۔ تشریح قوله والقول فى القيمة ... الخ - اگر مالک اور غاصب کے درمیان قیمت کے بارے میں اختلاف ہو تو غاصب کا قول اس کی قسم کے ساتھ مقبول ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مالک مدعی زیادہ ہے اور غاصب اس کا منکر ہے اور قول منکر ہی کا معتبر ہوتا ہے اس کی قسم کے ساتھ ہاں اگر مالک اس سے زیادہ قیمت ہونے پر بلینہ قائم کر دے تو اس کا بینہ مقبول ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ اس نے حجت ملزمہ سے ثابت کر دیا۔ فائدہ اگر مالک اقامت بینہ سے عاجز ہو جائے اور غاصب سے قسم کا مطالبہ کرے۔ جب کہ غاصب کے پاس ایسا مہینہ موجود ہے جو قیمت منصوب کے لئے شاہد ہے تو غاصب کامہینہ مقبول نہ ہوگا بلکہ اس سے قسم ہی لی جائے گی اس لئے کہ اس کا مبینہ نافی زیادہ ہے۔ اور جو بینہ نفی پر ہو وہ مقبول نہیں ہوتا۔ پھر بعض مشائخ نے کہا ہے کہ اسقاط یمین کے لئے غاصب کا مبینہ مقبول ہونا چاہیے جیسے مودع اگر ردیعت کا دعوی کرے تو اس کا قول مقبول ہوتا ہے اور اگر وہ اس پر بینہ قائم کرے تو بینہ بھی مقبول ہوتا ہے۔ قاضی ابو علی نفی کہتے تھے کہ یہ مسئلہ مشکل شمار کیا گیا ہے اور بعض مشائخ نے ان دونوں میں فرق کیا ہے اور یہی صحیح پہلے اس لئے کہ مودع کے ذمہ صرف پیٹین ہے جس کو اس نے بینہ قائم کر کے ساقط کر دیا اور خصومت جاتی رہی۔ رہا غاصب سو اس پر یہاں یمین اور قیمت دو چیزیں لازم ہیں اور اقامت بینہ سے صرف یمین ساقط ہوئی ہے پس غاصب مودع کے معنی میں نہیں ہے۔
قوله فان ظهرت ... الخ - پھر اگرشی مغصوب کسی وقت ظاہر ہو اور اس کی قیمت اس مقدار سے زائد ہو جس کا غاصب نے تاوان دیا ہے اور تاوان بھی مالک کے قول کے مطابق یا اس کے بینہ کے مطابق یا اپنے انکار قسم کے سبب سے دیا ہے توشی مغصوب غاصب کی مملوک ہوگی اور مالک کو اس میں اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مالک اسی مقدار کا مدعی تھا اور اس پر راضی ہو چکا تھا اور اگر غاصب نے اپنے قول کے موافق قسم کھا کر تا وان دیا ہو تو مالک کو اختیار ہوگا چاہے شی مغصوب لے کر اس کا ضمان واپس کر دے۔ اور چاہے اس ضمان کو بر قرار رکھے۔ کیونکہ اس مقدار کے ساتھ اس کی رضا مندی پوری نہیں ہوئی تھی اس لئے کہ وہ زیادہ کا دعی تھا اور بغیر زیادتی کے لے لینا صرف اس وجہ سے تھا کہ اس کے پاس بینہ نہیں تھا۔ میں رضا مندی ثابت نہ ہوئی۔
قوله ولو ظهرت العين .... الخ ۔ اور اگر قسم کے ساتھ غاصب کے کہنے پر تاوان لینے کی صورت میں جب مال ظاہر ہوا اور اس کی قیمت اس مقدار کے برابر ہے جو غاصب نے اداء کی تھی یا اس سے کم ہے تو امام کرخی کے نزدیک مالک کو واپس لینے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مالک کو اس کی ملک کا پورا بدل مل چکا۔ لیکن ظاہر الروایۃ میں اس کو اختیار ہے کہ اگر چاہے مال عین واپس لے کر نتاوان پھیر دے۔ اور یہی اصح ہے کیونکہ اصل یعنی مبسوط میں مطلقاً یہی مذکور ہے۔ اسی طرح امام طحاوی نے بھی روایت کو مطلق ہی ذکر کیا ہے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ مالک کی رضا مندی پوری نہیں ہوئی۔ اس لئے کہ مالک کا جود ھوئی تھا وہ اس کو نہیں دیا گیا اور اختیار اسی لئے حاصل ہوا کہ اس کی رضامندی پوری نہیں ہوئی نہ اس لئے کہ اس کی قیمت پوری نہیں۔
Book of Usurpation. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, volume 12. [He] was claimant of more. And taking without the excess was due to lack of proof. And if the property appears while its value equals what the usurper paid or is less, then in the latter case the answer is as in Zahir al-Riwayah, and it is more correct, contrary to what Imam al-Karkhi said: that the owner has no choice. Because his consent was not complete in the sense that what he claimed was not given to him, and the existence of choice is due only to lack of consent. Explanation of his statement 'And the statement regarding value...' - If there is a dispute between owner and usurper about value, the usurper's statement with his oath is accepted. Because the owner is the claimant of more, and the usurper is denier, and the denier's statement is deemed valid with his oath. Yes, if the owner establishes proof of higher value, his proof is accepted because he established it with binding evidence. Benefit: If the owner is unable to establish proof and demands an oath from the usurper, while the usurper has a document that bears witness to the stipulated value, the usurper's document is not accepted; rather, an oath is taken from him because his document is for negation of increase, and a document for negation is not accepted. Then some scholars said that for the negation of the oath, the usurper's document should be accepted, like the depositary if he claims return, his statement is accepted, and if he establishes proof, his proof is also accepted. Qadi Abu Ali al-Nafi used to say that this issue is considered problematic. And some scholars differentiated between them, and this is correct. First, because only the depositary is liable for a trust that he disproved by establishing proof, and the dispute ceases. As for the usurper, here an oath and value are both obligatory, and by establishing proof only the oath is removed; so the usurper is not like the depositary. His statement: 'If it appears...' - Then if the usurped property appears at some time and its value is more than the amount the usurper paid as compensation, and the compensation was paid according to the owner's statement, or according to his proof, or by his own denial oath, then the usurped property becomes owned by the usurper, and the owner has no choice. Because the owner claimed that amount and was satisfied with it. But if the usurper paid compensation after swearing according to his own statement, then the owner has a choice: either he can take the property and return the compensation, or he can let the compensation stand. Because his consent with that amount was not complete, because he claimed more, and taking without the excess was only because he had no proof. Consent was not established. His statement: 'And if the property appears...' - And if in the case of taking compensation upon the usurper's statement with oath, when the property appears and its value equals what the usurper paid or is less, then according to Imam al-Karkhi the owner has no option to take it back, because he received the full substitute for his property. But in Zahir al-Riwayah he has the option: he may take back the property and return the compensation. And this is more correct because in the original (Mabsut) it is absolutely mentioned. Similarly, Imam al-Tahawi narrated the report absolutely. The reason is that the owner's consent was not complete, because what he claimed was not given to him, and the choice accrued only because his consent was not complete, not because the value was not full.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings in Al-Hidayah regarding the owner's choice (ikhtiyār) when the usurped property (maghsūb) reappears after the usurper has paid compensation (taʿwīḍ). The commentary first addresses the scenario where there is a dispute between the owner and usurper about the value of the property. The default rule is that the usurper's statement is accepted with his oath because he is the denier (munkir) while the owner is the claimant (muddaʿī). If the owner can produce evidence (bayyinah) of a higher value, that evidence takes precedence. There is a discussion about the validity of a written document (mubayyanah) from the usurper: it is not accepted because it is evidence for negation (nafy), which is generally not accepted in court. The author then distinguishes between the depositary (mūdiʿ) and the usurper: in the case of the depositary, a document can negate the oath, but for the usurper, both the oath and the value are obligatory, so a document only removes the oath, not the value. Then the commentary explains the main ruling: if the usurped property appears after compensation, and its value is more than what was paid, the property belongs to the usurper permanently; the owner has no choice because he claimed that lower amount and was satisfied. However, if the compensation was paid based on the usurper's own oath (i.e., he underpaid), then the owner still has a choice: he can either return the compensation and take back the property, or keep the compensation and let the property go. This is because his consent was not complete (lam takun raḍāʾuhu tāmmatan) since he accepted less only due to lack of proof. Lastly, the passage addresses a subtle dispute with Imam al-Karkhi: when the property appears and its value is equal to or less than the compensation paid, Imam al-Karkhi says the owner has no choice because he received full market value. But the relied-upon position (al-ṣaḥīḥ) according to Zahir al-Riwayah is that the owner still has a choice, because the reason for the choice is the lack of complete consent, not the insufficiency of value. The owner had claimed a higher amount (either the actual value or what he claimed in court), and he was not given that; so he may still reclaim the property. This is supported by the fact that Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's Al-Mabsut and Imam al-Tahawi's narration state the ruling absolutely, without restriction to cases where the value is different.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایۃ (Zāhir al-Riwāyah): The authoritative transmitted rulings from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.), representing the most reliable Hanafi position.
رضا مندی (Riḍāmandī): Consent or satisfaction; the owner's free acceptance of the compensation. If consent is complete, the owner loses the right to reclaim the property; if incomplete, the right remains.
اختیار (Ikhtiyār): The owner's option to either keep the compensation or reclaim the usurped property upon its reappearance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, when does the owner have the choice to reclaim the usurped property after receiving compensation?
A) Only when the compensation was less than the property's value.
B) Only when the compensation was paid based on the usurper's own oath (not the owner's claim).
C) Whenever the property reappears, regardless of the value, as long as the owner had claimed a higher amount and accepted less only due to lack of proof.
D) Only when the compensation was paid based on the owner's evidence.

Key Takeaway
The owner's right to reclaim usurped property after compensation hinges on the completeness of his consent, not on the sufficiency of the value received.

Hanafi Ruling on Accessories of Usurped Property as Amanah
States the Hanafi ruling on accessories and contrasts with Shafi'i view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the legal status of the accessories (zawā'id) of usurped property, identify the Shafi'i opposing view, and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between the two schools.

Core Idea
The offspring and produce of usurped property are a trust (amānah), not guaranteed, unless the usurper transgresses or refuses to return them.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: the liability for accessories such as offspring and fruit of usurped property. The Hanafi school treats these as a trust (amānah) in the usurper's hands, meaning no liability unless he transgresses or withholds them after demand. The Shafi'i school, however, considers them guaranteed (maḍmūnah) by virtue of being part of the usurped property. Understanding this ruling clarifies the Hanafi principle that possession over accessories does not automatically create liability.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the offspring and fruit of usurped property are an amānah. The usurper is not liable for their loss unless he transgresses (e.g., misuse) or refuses to return them after the owner demands them.
This is a clear statement of the Hanafi view, distinguishing between the original property (guaranteed) and its accessories (trust).
2
Identify the opposing school and its view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that all accessories (zawā'id) of usurped property are guaranteed (maḍmūnah), whether attached or separated. He defines usurpation as placing one's hand on someone else's property without consent, which necessarily includes the accessories.
The Shafi'i view is based on a broader definition of ghaṣb that encompasses all increases.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Al-Shafi'i argues that since the original property is guaranteed, its accessories must also be guaranteed because the hand that usurps the principal is also considered to have usurped its increments. He gives the example of a wild animal taken from the sanctuary that gives birth in the usurper's hand: the offspring is guaranteed.
The proof relies on the principle that the usurper's control over the original extends to its natural increases.
4
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to the Hanafi school, if the offspring of a usurped slave-girl dies without any transgression by the usurper, he pays nothing. According to the Shafi'i school, he must pay its value. This difference can lead to significantly different financial outcomes.
The thamarah shows the real-world impact of the legal categorization.
5
Note the Hanafi basis
The Hanafi ruling is based on the principle that the usurper's possession over the accessories is not the same as his possession over the original. The accessories are not directly usurped; they come into existence after the act of ghaṣb. They are akin to a trust until the usurper's transgression or refusal to return.
This distinction between the original act and subsequent increments is central to the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و ولد المغصوبة ونماؤها وثمرة البستان المغصوب امانة في يد الغاصب ان هلک فلاضمان عليه الا ان يتعدى فيها او يطلبها مالكها فيمنعها اياه، وقال الشافعى زوائد المغصوب مضمونة متصلة كانت او منفصلة الوجود الغصب وهو اثبات اليد على مال الغير بغير ،رضاه، كما فى الطبية المخرجة من الحرم اذا ولدت في يده
He said: 'And the offspring of the usurped (female slave) and its increase and the fruit of the usurped garden are a trust (amānah) in the hand of the usurper. If they are destroyed, there is no liability upon him unless he transgresses regarding them or the owner demands them and he withholds them from him.' And al-Shafi'i said: 'The accessories (zawā'id) of the usurped property are guaranteed (maḍmūnah), whether they are connected (muttasilah) or separated (munfaṣilah). The existence of usurpation is the placing of hand upon the property of another without his consent.' As in the case of the wild animal taken out of the sanctuary (ḥaram) when it gives birth in his hand.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the offspring (walad), increase (namā'), and fruit (thamarah) of usurped property. According to the Hanafi school, these are considered a trust (amānah) in the usurper's possession. Therefore, the usurper is not liable if they are destroyed without his transgression (taʿaddī). However, if he transgresses (e.g., by misuse) or if the owner demands them back and he refuses, then he becomes liable. This is because usurpation (ghaṣb) creates a temporary possession, but the accessories are not automatically guaranteed. The passage then contrasts with the Shafi'i position: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the accessories (zawā'id) of the usurped property are guaranteed (maḍmūnah) regardless of whether they are attached (muttasilah) or separated (munfaṣilah). He defines usurpation as placing one's hand on someone else's property without consent. The example given is of a wild animal taken from the sanctuary (ḥaram) that gives birth in the usurper's hand; the offspring would be guaranteed according to the Shafi'i view. The Hanafi response is not included in this excerpt, but the ruling is clear: the Hanafi position treats the accessories as a trust, while the Shafi'i treats them as guaranteed. The passage appears to be cut off, but it serves as a statement of the two positions.

Key Terms
امانت (Amānah): A trust; the legal status of property held by a person without liability for loss unless they are negligent or transgress. The usurper holds the offspring and produce as an amānah.
زوائد (Zawā'id): Accessories or additions to the principal property, including offspring, produce, and natural increase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, under what condition is the usurper liable for the loss of offspring of a usurped slave-girl?
A) Automatically, because the offspring is part of the usurped property.
B) Only if the usurper failed to pay compensation for the slave-girl.
C) Only if the usurper transgresses (e.g., by misuse) or refuses to return the offspring after the owner demands it.
D) Only if the offspring is born after the usurper has become liable for the compensation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats the accessories (zawā'id) of usurped property as a trust (amānah), not guaranteed, unless the usurper transgresses or refuses to return them after demand.

The Status of Increases of Usurped Property: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Ruling that offspring and increase of usurped property are trust (amana) in usurper's hands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the status of offspring and increase of usurped property and explain the basis of the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Increases of usurped property are trust (amānah), not guaranteed — unless the usurper transgresses or refuses after demand.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the offspring, growth, and fruit of usurped property. While the Shafi'i school considers all increases as guaranteed because they arise from wrongful possession, the Hanafi school distinguishes that the owner never had possession over these separate increases. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the Hanafi principle that liability follows from removal of the owner's hand, not merely from the existence of wrongful possession.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the child, growth, and fruit of usurped property are amānah (trust) in the usurper's hands. They are not guaranteed (maḍmūn) unless the usurper transgresses (taʿaddī) or refuses to return them after the owner's demand (manʿ).
This is the default ruling.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold that all increases of usurped property are guaranteed (maḍmūn), whether they are connected (like beauty) or separate (like offspring).
Their reasoning: usurpation is tortious possession, so its effects extend to all increases.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is based on the definition of usurpation: taking possession of another's wealth without consent. Since the increase arises in that same possession, it inherits the liability. They cite the analogy of a gazelle taken from the sanctuary: if she gives birth, the child is guaranteed.
Consider the analogy carefully.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the owner's hand (yad al-mālik) was never established over the increase separately, so the usurper does not remove it. The gazelle analogy is refuted: the child is not guaranteed before the possibility of release; liability arises only after refusal (manʿ). Thus, the increase is amānah unless the usurper's conduct (taʿaddī or manʿ) triggers liability.
Key: the owner's hand is a prerequisite for liability.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the increase perishes without fault, the Hanafi school says no compensation; the Shafi'i school requires compensation regardless.
This difference affects real-world cases of accidental loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال و ولد المغصوبة ونماؤها وثمرة البستان المغصوب امانة في يد الغاصب ان هلک فلاضمان عليه الا ان يتعدى فيها او يطلبها مالكها فيمنعها اياه، وقال الشافعى زوائد المغصوب مضمونة متصلة كانت او منفصلة الوجود الغصب وهو اثبات اليد على مال الغير بغير ،رضاه، كما فى الطبية المخرجة من الحرم اذا ولدت في يده
ترجمہ: مغصو بہ باندی کا بچہ اور اس کی بڑھوتری اور مغصوب باغ کا پھل امانت ہوتا ہے۔ غاصب کے پاس اگر تلف ہو جائے تو اس پر تاوان نہیں ہے۔ الا یہ کہ غاصب اس میں تعدی کرے یا مالک کے طلب کرنے پر اس کو روکے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ مغصوب کے زوائد مضمون میں متصلہ ہوں یا منفصلہ معنی غصب پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اور وہ قبضہ جما لینا ہے غیر کے مال پر اس کی رضا مندی کے بغیر جیسے اس ہرنی میں جو حرم سے نکالی گئی ہے جب اس کے قبضہ میں بچہ بنے تو وہ اس پر مضمون ہوتی ہے۔
تشریح: قوله وولد المغصوبة.. الخ - اگر کوئی باندی غصب کی اور اس سے بچہ ہوا تو اس کا بچہ اور جو کچھ باندی کی بڑھوتر کی ہو اسی طرح مغصوب باغ کا پھل غاصب کے پاس امانت کے طور پر ہوتے ہیں اگر اس کے قبضہ میں رہتے ہوئے تلف ہو جا ئیں تو غاصب پر تاوان لازم نہ ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر اس میں غاصب کی طرف سے تعدی پائی جائے یا مالک کے طلب کرنے پر وہ اس کو نہ دے تو ضامن ہوگا۔ اسی کے قائل امام مالک بھی ہیں۔
قوله ونماؤها .... الخ - نماء مغصوبہ سے مراد حسن و جمال وغیرہ۔ ہے رہے وہ اکساب جو استغلال غاصب سے حاصل ہوں ۔ سو وہ نماء مغصوب کے قبیل سے نہیں ہیں۔ یہاں تک کہ ان میں تعدی کرنے سے ضامن ہو ورنہ الا ان يتعدى فيها الا استثناء مستقيم نه ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ غاصب پر مضمون نہیں ہوتے گوان کو تلف کر دے اس لئے کہ وہ تو منافع مغصوب کا عوض ہیں اور ہمارے یہاں مغصوب کے منافع مضمون نہیں ہوتے تو ایسے ہی ان کا بدل بھی مغصوب نہ ہو گا ۔ قوله وقال الشافعي .... الخ - امام شافعی اور امام احمد فرماتے ہیں کہ مغصوب مٹی سے جس قسم کی زیادتی حاصل ہو غاصب اس کا ضامن ہوگا خواہ وہ زیادتی متصلہ ہو ۔ جیسے حسن و جمال وغیر ہ یازیادتی منفصلہ ہو۔ جیسے بچہ وغیرہ بنا بر آں کہ ان کے یہاں غصب کی تعریف یہ ہے کہ غیر کے مال پر اس کی رضا مندی کے بغیر قبضہ جمالیا جائے اور یہ بات صورت مذکورہ میں موجود ہے۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا۔ جیسے حرم سے نکالی ہوئی ہرنی اگر اس کے قبضہ میں بچہ بنے تو بچہ اس پر مضمون ہوتا ہے کیونکہ ماں کے حق میں سبب ضمان موجود ہے اس لئے کہ اصل یعنی ماں کا ضمان۔ باطل قبضہ جما لینے کے اعتبار سے ہے اور یہی قبضہ بعینہ بچہ پر بھی ثابت ہے۔ لحدوثها فی ملک الید فتصير مضمونة ضرورة -
احناف کی دلیل: ولنا ان الغصب اثبات اليد على مال الغير على وجه يزيل يد المالك على ما ذكرناه ويد المالك ما كانت ثابتة على هذه الزيادة حتى يزيلها الغاصب ولو اعتبرت ثابتة على الولد لا يزيلها اذ الظاهر عدم المنع حتى لو منع الولد بعد طلبه يضمنه وكذا اذا تعدى فيه كما قال فى الكتاب وذلك بان اتلفه او ذبحه فاکله او باعه وسلمه وفى الظبية المخرجة لا يضمن ولدها اذا هلك قبل التمكن من الارسال لعدم المنع وانما يضمته اذا هلک بعده لوجود المنع بعد طلب صاحب الحق وهو الشرع على هذا اكثر مشايخنا ولو اطلق الجواب فهو ضمان جناية ولهذا يتكرر بتكررها ويجب بالاعانة والاشارة فلان يجب بما هو فوقها وهو اثبات اليد على
He said: And the child of the usurped female slave, and her growth, and the fruit of the usurped garden are a trust (amānah) in the hand of the usurper. If they are destroyed, there is no liability on him, unless he transgresses regarding them, or the owner demands them and he withholds them from him. And al-Shafi'i said: The increases of the usurped property are guaranteed, whether connected or separate, because the meaning of usurpation exists, and it is the taking of possession of another's wealth without his consent. Like the case of the female gazelle brought out of the sanctuary: if she gives birth in his hand, it is guaranteed to him. Translation: The child of the usurped female slave, and her increase, and the fruit of the usurped garden are a trust in the hands of the usurper. If they perish, there is no compensation on him, unless the usurper transgresses regarding them or the owner demands and he refuses. Imam al-Shafi'i says that the increases of the usurped property are guaranteed, whether connected or separate, because the meaning of usurpation exists, and that is taking possession of another's property without his consent. Like the female gazelle taken out of the sanctuary: if she gives birth in his hand, it is guaranteed. Explanation: His statement: 'And the child of the usurped female slave...' etc. If someone usurps a female slave and she gives birth, then her child, and whatever increase she has, and similarly the fruit of the usurped garden, are as a trust in the usurper's hands. If they perish while in his possession, there is no liability on the usurper. Yes, if there is transgression by the usurper or he does not give them when the owner demands, he is liable. Imam Malik also holds the same view. His statement: 'And her increase...' etc. By 'namā' of the usurped property is meant beauty, charm, etc. As for the earnings obtained through the usurper's exploitation, they are not of the category of 'namā' of the usurped property. Thus, even if he transgresses regarding them, he is liable, but the exception 'unless he transgresses' is not a straight exception, because they are not guaranteed to him, and if he destroys them, it is because they are the compensation for the usufruct of the usurped property, and in our school the usufruct of the usurped property is not guaranteed, so similarly their substitute is not usurped. His statement: 'And al-Shafi'i said...' etc. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad say that whatever increase is obtained from the usurped property, the usurper is liable for it, whether it is connected increase like beauty and charm, or separate increase like a child, because in their view the definition of usurpation is taking possession of another's wealth without his consent, and this is present in the mentioned case. So this is like the case of the female gazelle taken out of the sanctuary: if she gives birth in his hand, the child is guaranteed to him because the cause of liability regarding the mother exists, because the original, i.e., the mother's liability, is due to invalid taking of possession, and this same possession is established over the child as well, because it arises in the ownership of the hand, so it becomes guaranteed necessarily. The Hanafi proof: And we have that usurpation is taking possession of another's wealth in a way that removes the owner's hand, as we mentioned. And the owner's hand was not established over this increase that the usurper should remove it. Even if it were considered established over the child, he does not remove it, for apparent is the absence of prevention. Thus, if he prevents the child after demand, he is liable for it, and similarly if he transgresses regarding it, as stated in the book, and that is by destroying it, or slaughtering and eating it, or selling and delivering it. And regarding the gazelle taken out, he is not liable for its child if it perishes before the possibility of release, due to absence of prevention. He is only liable if it perishes after that, due to existence of prevention after the demand of the right-holder. And this is the position of most of our mashāyikh. And if the answer is absolute, it is liability for injury, and for this reason it is repeated with its repetition and is obligatory by assistance and indication. So it is all the more necessary that what is above it, i.e., taking possession of
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the status of offspring, growth, and fruit (zuwaid) of usurped property. The Hanafi position: these are amānah (trust) in the usurper's hands; if they perish without his fault, he is not liable. He becomes liable only if he transgresses (ta'dī) or refuses to return them after the owner's demand. Imam al-Shafi'i (and Imam Ahmad) hold that all increases are guaranteed (maḍmūn) because the usurpation itself is a tortious possession; the original wrongful hand extends to the increases. The commentary provides the Hanafi proof: the owner's hand never extended to the increases separately, so the usurper does not remove the owner's hand over them. The analogy of the gazelle taken from the sanctuary is refuted: there, the child is not guaranteed before the time for release; after that, the 'prevention' (man') creates liability. Thus, the Hanafi view is that the increases are not guaranteed ab initio. The commentary also distinguishes between 'namā' (natural increase like beauty) and 'aksāb' (earnings from exploitation), noting that earnings are not part of the usurped property and are guaranteed if misused.

Key Terms
أمانة (amānah): A trust in the hands of the usurper; no liability for destruction without transgression.
زوائد المغصوب (zawāʾid al-maghṣūb): Increases of the usurped property, including offspring, growth, and fruit.
تعدي (taʿaddī): Transgression or misuse by the usurper that triggers liability for the increase.
منع (manʿ): Refusal to return the increase after the owner's demand, also triggers liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a usurper become liable for the child of a usurped female slave?
A) Immediately, because the child is an increase of usurped property.
B) Only if he commits transgression (taʿaddī) or refuses to return it upon the owner's demand.
C) Only if the child is destroyed while in his possession.
D) He is never liable.

Key Takeaway
The offspring and increase of usurped property are amānah in the usurper's hands; liability arises only upon transgression or refusal after demand.

intermediate
10 min
Offspring and Increase of Usurped Property: Trust or Guaranteed?
Hanafi ruling that offspring and increase are trust; inter-madhhab dispute with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the offspring and increase of usurped property and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the definition of ghasp.

Core Idea
The offspring and increase of usurped property are amanah (trust) not guaranteed, unless the usurper withholds after demand or commits transgression.

This passage presents a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding the legal status of increments (zawa'id) of usurped property. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the original property (guaranteed) and its increments (trust), while the Shafi'i school treats all increments as guaranteed by virtue of being in the usurper's possession. Understanding the basis of this difference requires examining the definition of ghasp and the concept of removal of the owner's possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the Hanafi position
State the precise ruling: the child of a usurped female slave, her increase, and the fruit of a usurped garden are amanah. Identify the two exceptions that make them guaranteed (transgression or withholding after demand).
The Hanafi position is also held by Imam Malik.
2
Understand the Shafi'i position and their proof
State the Shafi'i ruling: all increments are guaranteed. Recognize their proof: the definition of ghasp as taking possession without consent, and the analogy to a gazelle from the Haram whose fawn is guaranteed.
The gazelle analogy is a key point in the dispute.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response based on the definition of ghasp
Explain the Hanafi definition of ghasp: it requires removing the owner's possession. Since the owner never had possession over the increments (they came into existence after usurpation or were not in the owner's control), the usurper does not remove anything. Therefore, increments are trust. Distinguish the gazelle case by noting that the fawn is not guaranteed before the owner demands its return.
The Hanafi response also addresses the objection about a pregnant slave: the fetus before birth is not considered property per some commentaries.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi position
Identify the practical consequence: if increments perish without transgression or refusal after demand, Hanafi says no compensation, Shafi'i says compensation. Confirm that the Hanafi view is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the madhhab.
The dispute is rooted in the definition of ghasp.

احناف کی دلیل
ولنا ان الغصب اثبات اليد على مال الغير على وجه يزيل يد المالك على ما ذكرناه ويد المالك ما كانت ثابتة على هذه الزيادة حتى يزيلها الغاصب ولو اعتبرت ثابتة على الولد لا يزيلها اذ الظاهر عدم المنع حتى لو منع الولد بعد طلبه يضمنه وكذا اذا تعدى فيه كما قال فى الكتاب وذلك بان اتلفه او ذبحه فاکله او باعه وسلمه وفى الظبية المخرجة لا يضمن ولدها اذا هلك قبل التمكن من الارسال لعدم المنع وانما يضمته اذا هلک بعده لوجود المنع بعد طلب صاحب الحق وهو الشرع على هذا اكثر مشايخنا ولو اطلق الجواب فهو ضمان جناية ولهذا يتكرر بتكررها ويجب بالاعانة والاشارة فلان يجب بما هو فوقها وهو اثبات اليد على مستحق الأمن أولى واخرى
ترجمہ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ غصب غیر کے مال پر اس طرح قبضہ جما لینا ہے جو مالک کا قبضہ زائل کر دے۔ جیسا کہ ہم ذکر کر چکے اور اس زیادتی پر مالک کا قبضہ ہی نہیں تھا یہاں تک کہ غاصب اس کو زائل کرے اور اگر بچہ پر اس کا قبضہ ثابت ہی مانا جائے تو غاصب نے اس کو زائل نہیں کیا کیونکہ ظاہر نہ روکنا ہے یہاں تک کہ غاصب اگر بچہ کو رو کے مالک کی طلب کے بعد تو ضامن ہوگا ایسے ہی اگر وہ اس میں تعدی کرے۔ جیسا کہ کتاب میں کہا ہے اور تعدی بایں طور ہے کہ اس کو تلف کر دے یا ذبح کر کے کھا جائے یا فروخت کر کے سپر د کر دے اور حرم سے نکالی ہوئی ہرنی میں اس کے بچہ کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا اگر وہ چھوڑنے پر قابو پانے سے پہلے تلف ہو جائے رو کنانہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے ضامن تو اسی وقت ہوگا جب وہ اس کے بعد تلف ہو۔ صاحب حق یعنی شرع کے مطالبہ کے بعد روکنا پائے جانے کی وجہ سے۔ ہمارے اکثر مشائخ اسی پر ہیں۔ اور اگر جواب مطلق ہی ہو تو یہ جرم کا تاوان ہے اسی لئے جرم متکررہونے سے ضمان متکرر ہوتا ہے اور اعانت اور اشارہ سے بھی واجب ہوتا ہے۔ پس اگر ضمان واجب ہو اس سے جو اس سے بڑھ کر ہے اور وہ مستحق امن پر قبضہ جما لینا ہے تو زیادہ بہتر اور مناسب ہوگا۔
تشریح قوله ولنا ان الغصب .. الخ - ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ غصب کے معنی ہیں غیر کے مال پر اپنا قبضہ اس طرح جمالینا کہ مالک کا قبضہ زائل کر دے جیسا کہ آغاز کتاب الغصب میں بیان ہو چکا اور یہاں زیادتی پر مالک کا قبضہ پہلے سے ثابت ہی نہیں تھا۔ یہاں تک کہ غاصب اس کو زائل کرے۔ پس اختلاف مذکور غصب کی تعریف پر مبنی ہوا۔ اعتراض اب یہاں یہ اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ تعلیل مذکور کے بموجب اگر باندی کو بحالت حمل غصب کیا تو اس کے بچہ کا تاوان واجب ہونا چاہیے۔ کیونکہ اس پر قبضہ ثابت تھا۔ حالانکہ باندی حاملہ غصب کرے یا غیر حاملہ بہر دوصورت غاصب اس کے بچہ کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا۔
جواب ... اس کا جواب عنایہ و بنایہ وغیرہ شروح میں یہ دیا گیا ہے کہ حمل جدا ہونے سے پہلے مال نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ تو باندی کے حق میں عیب شمار ہوتا ہے۔ فلم يصدق اثبات اليد على مال الغير لیکن صاحب نتائج نے اس جواب پر یہ بحث کی ہے کہ حمل اگر قبل از انفصال مال نہ ہو تو حمل کو آزاد یامد بر کر نا میچ نہیں ہونا چاہیے۔ کیونکہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ محل اعتناق و تد بیر ملوک مال ہی ہوتا ہے۔ حالانکہ حمل کا اعتاق و تدبیر درست ہے۔ معلوم ہوا کہ حمل مال ہے اور اگر یہی تسلیم کر لیا جائے کہ محل اعتاق و تدبیر کا مال ہونا ضروری نہیں بلکہ ملک کا ہونا کافی ہے اور ملک کا تحقق غیر مال میں بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ تب بھی مذکورہ جواب عبارت کتاب کے قابل نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ جواب مذکور کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بحالت حمل غصب جاریہ کی صورت میں سنمان ولد واجب نہ ہونے کی وجہ حمل کا قبل از انفصال مال نہ ہونا ہے نہ یہ کہ اس پر مالک کا قبضہ ثابت نہیں تھا۔ حالانکہ کتاب میں یہی کہا ہے۔ وید المالک ماکانت ثابتة على هذه الزيادة قوله ولو اعتبرت ثابتة .... الخ - اور اگر ملک ام کے تابع کرتے ہوئے اولاد پر مالک کا قبضہ تقدیر اثابت بھی مان لیا جائے تب
Translation: The child of a usurped female slave, and her increase, and the fruit of a usurped garden are trust (amanah). If they perish with the usurper, there is no compensation upon him. Unless the usurper commits transgression (ta'addi) in them, or withholds them after the owner's demand. Imam Shafi'i says: The increments of the usurped property are guaranteed (madhmun), whether connected or disconnected, due to the presence of the meaning of ghasp, which is taking possession (qabd) of another's property without their consent, like the gazelle that was taken out of the Haram—when a child is born in his possession, it is guaranteed upon him. Commentary on his saying 'and the offspring of the usurped...' etc. If someone usurps a female slave and she gives birth, her child and whatever increase she has, similarly the fruit of a usurped garden, are trust with the usurper. If they perish while in his possession, compensation is not obligatory. Yes, if there is transgression from the usurper, or he does not give it back after the owner's demand, then he becomes guarantor. Imam Malik also holds this view. Commentary on 'and her growth...' Growth (nama) of the usurped means beauty, grace, etc. As for the earnings acquired through the usurper's exploitation, they are not of the category of growth of the usurped property. So if he transgresses in them, he becomes guarantor; otherwise not. The exception 'unless he transgresses in them' is not a genuine exception because they are not guaranteed upon him even if he destroys them, since they are compensation for the usufruct of the usurped property, and in our school the usufruct of usurped property is not guaranteed, so their substitute is also not usurped. Commentary on 'and al-Shafi'i said...' Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad say: Whatever increase arises from the usurped property, the usurper is guarantor for it, whether it is a connected increase like beauty, etc., or a disconnected increase like a child, etc., because according to them the definition of ghasp is taking possession of another's property without his consent, and this is present in the mentioned case. So it became like the gazelle taken out of the Haram: if a child is born in his possession, the child is guaranteed upon him because the cause of guarantee is present with respect to the mother. Since the original (the mother) is guaranteed due to invalid possession, and this same possession is also established over the child because of its occurrence in the property of the hand (possession), so it becomes necessarily guaranteed. The Hanafi proof: And our proof is that ghasp is establishing possession over the property of another in a manner that removes the owner's possession, as we mentioned. And the owner's possession was not established over this increase for the usurper to remove it. Even if it were considered established over the child, the usurper did not remove it because the default is no withholding; so if he withholds the child after demand, he becomes guarantor, and likewise if he transgresses in it, as stated in the book. Transgression is by destroying it, slaughtering and eating it, or selling and delivering it. And regarding the gazelle taken out, he does not guarantee its child if it perishes before being able to release it, due to absence of withholding. He only guarantees if it perishes after that, due to the presence of withholding after the demand of the rightful person, which is the Shari'ah. Most of our scholars are upon this. And if the answer is absolute, it is a guarantee of injury (jinaayah); therefore, it is repeated with repetition of injuries, and it becomes obligatory through assistance and indication. So if guarantee becomes obligatory for what is above that—namely, establishing possession over one deserving of trust—then it is more appropriate and fitting. Commentary on 'and our proof that ghasp...' Our proof is that ghasp means establishing one's own possession over another's property in a way that removes the owner's possession, as was explained at the beginning of the chapter on ghasp. And here, the owner's possession was not previously established over the increase, for the usurper to remove it. Thus, the mentioned difference of opinion is based on the definition of ghasp. Objection: According to the mentioned reasoning, if a female slave is usurped while pregnant, then the compensation for her child should be obligatory, because possession was established over it. Yet whether the female slave is usurped pregnant or not, in both cases the usurper is not guarantor for her child. Answer: The answer given in 'Inayah, 'Binayah', and other commentaries is that the fetus before separation is not property; rather, it is considered a defect with respect to the female slave. Therefore, 'establishing possession over another's property' does not apply. But the author of Nata'ij has discussed this answer, arguing that if the fetus is not property before separation, then manumitting or mudabbar-ing a fetus should not be valid, because the locus of manumission and tadbir is usually property. Yet manumission and tadbir of a fetus are valid. So it is known that the fetus is property. And if we concede that the locus of manumission and tadbir does not necessarily have to be property, rather ownership is sufficient, and ownership can exist in non-property, then too the above answer is not befitting the text of the book, because the gist of the answer is that in the case of usurping a pregnant female slave, the non-obligation of compensation for the child is due to the fetus not being property before separation, not that the owner's possession was not established over it, while the book says: 'and the owner's possession was not established over this increase.'
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the status of offspring and increase of usurped property. The Hanafi school holds that the child of a usurped female slave, her growth (like beauty), and the fruit of a usurped garden are amanah (trust) in the hands of the usurper. If they perish without the usurper's transgression or refusal after the owner's demand, no compensation is due. This is also the view of Imam Malik. In contrast, Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold that all increments (zawa'id) of usurped property are guaranteed (madhmun) because the definition of ghasp according to them is simply taking possession of another's property without consent, regardless of whether the owner's prior possession is removed. They analogize to a gazelle taken from the Haram: if a fawn is born in the usurper's possession, it is guaranteed because the mother is already guaranteed due to unlawful possession, and the fawn is born into that same possession. The Hanafi rebuttal is based on their specific definition of ghasp: it requires the removal of the owner's possession. Since the owner never had possession over the increments (they did not exist at the time of usurpation or were not in the owner's control), the usurper does not remove anything. The increments are therefore trust until the usurper withholds them after demand or commits transgression. The commentator then addresses an objection: if a pregnant female slave is usurped, why is the child not guaranteed even though the owner had possession over the fetus? The answer from earlier commentaries is that the fetus before birth is not considered property; it is a defect in the slave. However, a later scholar (author of Nata'ij) criticizes this because manumission and tadbir of a fetus are valid, suggesting it is property. He offers an alternative: perhaps the locus of manumission need not be property but merely owned. The passage ends by noting that the book's statement 'the owner's possession was not established over this increase' applies to increments arising after usurpation, not the fetus which existed before.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasp): Taking possession of another's property without right, with the condition of removing the owner's possession (per Hanafi).
زائد / زيادة (za'id / ziyadah): Increments of usurped property, whether connected (like beauty) or disconnected (like offspring or fruit).
امانت (amanah): Trust; property held by another without liability for loss unless negligence.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability for compensation in case of loss or damage.
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression beyond proper bounds; in this context, destroying, slaughtering, selling, or any misuse of the trust property.
مضمون (madhmun): Guaranteed; subject to compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, under what condition does a usurper become liable (daman) for the offspring of a usurped female slave?
A) Immediately upon the birth of the child.
B) Only if the child is destroyed by the usurper.
C) If the usurper withholds the child after the owner's demand or commits transgression in it.
D) The usurper is never liable for the child.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the increments of usurped property are trust until the usurper withholds after demand or transgresses; the school's definition of ghasp as removing the owner's possession is decisive.

intermediate
15 min
Liability for Offspring of Usurped Property: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Hanafi refutes Shafi'i's analogy on liability for offspring of usurped slave-girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on liability for offspring of usurped property and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the distinction between dhaman ghasb and dhaman jinayat.

Core Idea
A usurper is not liable for offspring unless he detains it after demand — the offspring is not property before separation.

This passage tackles a classic inter-madhhab dispute: must a usurper compensate for the offspring of a usurped slave-girl or animal? The Hanafi school distinguishes between guarantee for usurpation (dhaman ghasb) and penalty for crime (dhaman jinayat), rejecting the Shafi'i analogy to a gazelle taken from the Haram. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping the Hanafi definition of ghasb and the limits of analogical reasoning in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and Hanafi position
Identify the contested ruling: is the usurper liable for the offspring of a usurped pregnant slave-girl or animal? The Hanafi position: not liable unless he detains after the owner's demand or commits transgression.
The ruling is not about the act but about the liability (dhaman).
2
Identify the Shafi'i/Zufar analogy
The opposing school analogies the case to a gazelle taken from the Haram, where both mother and offspring are liable. Understand the basis of their qiyas.
The analogy relies on the apparent similarity of offspring following the mother.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: definition of ghasb and non-property status of fetus
Examine the Hanafi argument: ghasb requires removal of the owner's hand; the owner's hand was never established over the offspring (before separation). Also, the fetus is not considered property until birth.
This is based on istihsan and the definition of ghasb from Kitab al-Ghasb.
4
Examine the distinction between dhaman ghasb and dhaman jinayat
The gazelle case is dhaman jinayat (penalty for violating sanctity of the Haram), not property usurpation. In jinayat, liability arises from detention after the Lawgiver's claim and can be triggered by assistance or indication—features absent in ghasb.
This is the crucial refutation of the analogy.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Hanafi, the usurper does not owe compensation for offspring unless specific conditions occur. Under Shafi'i, he owes it automatically. This affects real cases of stolen or wrongfully taken animals.
The ikhtilaf is a legitimate difference based on usul principles.

ترجمہ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ غصب غیر کے مال پر اس طرح قبضہ جما لینا ہے جو مالک کا قبضہ زائل کر دے۔ جیسا کہ ہم ذکر کر چکے اور اس زیادتی پر مالک کا قبضہ ہی نہیں تھا یہاں تک کہ غاصب اس کو زائل کرے اور اگر بچہ پر اس کا قبضہ ثابت ہی مانا جائے تو غاصب نے اس کو زائل نہیں کیا کیونکہ ظاہر نہ روکنا ہے یہاں تک کہ غاصب اگر بچہ کو رو کے مالک کی طلب کے بعد تو ضامن ہوگا ایسے ہی اگر وہ اس میں تعدی کرے۔ جیسا کہ کتاب میں کہا ہے اور تعدی بایں طور ہے کہ اس کو تلف کر دے یا ذبح کر کے کھا جائے یا فروخت کر کے سپر د کر دے اور حرم سے نکالی ہوئی ہرنی میں اس کے بچہ کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا اگر وہ چھوڑنے پر قابو پانے سے پہلے تلف ہو جائے رو کنانہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے ضامن تو اسی وقت ہوگا جب وہ اس کے بعد تلف ہو۔ صاحب حق یعنی شرع کے مطالبہ کے بعد روکنا پائے جانے کی وجہ سے۔ ہمارے اکثر مشائخ اسی پر ہیں۔ اور اگر جواب مطلق ہی ہو تو یہ جرم کا تاوان ہے اسی لئے جرم متکررہونے سے ضمان متکرر ہوتا ہے اور اعانت اور اشارہ سے بھی واجب ہوتا ہے۔ پس اگر ضمان واجب ہو اس سے جو اس سے بڑھ کر ہے اور وہ مستحق امن پر قبضہ جما لینا ہے تو زیادہ بہتر اور مناسب ہوگا۔ تشریح قوله ولنا ان الغصب .. الخ - ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ غصب کے معنی ہیں غیر کے مال پر اپنا قبضہ اس طرح جمالینا کہ مالک کا قبضہ زائل کر دے جیسا کہ آغاز کتاب الغصب میں بیان ہو چکا اور یہاں زیادتی پر مالک کا قبضہ پہلے سے ثابت ہی نہیں تھا۔ یہاں تک کہ غاصب اس کو زائل کرے۔ پس اختلاف مذکور غصب کی تعریف پر مبنی ہوا۔ اعتراض اب یہاں یہ اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ تعلیل مذکور کے بموجب اگر باندی کو بحالت حمل غصب کیا تو اس کے بچہ کا تاوان واجب ہونا چاہیے۔ کیونکہ اس پر قبضہ ثابت تھا۔ حالانکہ باندی حاملہ غصب کرے یا غیر حاملہ بہر دوصورت غاصب اس کے بچہ کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا۔ جواب ... اس کا جواب عنایہ و بنایہ وغیرہ شروح میں یہ دیا گیا ہے کہ حمل جدا ہونے سے پہلے مال نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ تو باندی کے حق میں عیب شمار ہوتا ہے۔ فلم یصدق اثبات اليد على مال الغير لیکن صاحب نتائج نے اس جواب پر یہ بحث کی ہے کہ حمل اگر قبل از انفصال مال نہ ہو تو حمل کو آزاد یامد بر کر نا میچ نہیں ہونا چاہیے۔ کیونکہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ محل اعتناق و تد بیر ملوک مال ہی ہوتا ہے۔ حالانکہ حمل کا اعتاق و تدبیر درست ہے۔ معلوم ہوا کہ حمل مال ہے اور اگر یہی تسلیم کر لیا جائے کہ محل اعتاق و تدبیر کا مال ہونا ضروری نہیں بلکہ ملک کا ہونا کافی ہے اور ملک کا تحقق غیر مال میں بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ تب بھی مذکورہ جواب عبارت کتاب کے قابل نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ جواب مذکور کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بحالت حمل غصب جاریہ کی صورت میں سنمان ولد واجب نہ ہونے کی وجہ حمل کا قبل از انفصال مال نہ ہونا ہے نہ یہ کہ اس پر مالک کا قبضہ ثابت نہیں تھا۔ حالانکہ کتاب میں یہی کہا ہے۔ وید المالک ماکانت ثابتة على هذه الزيادة قوله ولو اعتبرت ثابتة .... الخ - اور اگر ملک ام کے تابع کرتے ہوئے اولاد پر مالک کا قبضہ تقدیر اثابت بھی مان لیا جائے تب بھی غاصب نے تقدیری قبضہ کو زائل نہیں کیا اس لئے کہ ظاہر حال یہی ہے کہ غاصب اس کو مالک سے نہ روکتا۔ یہاں تک کہ وہ اگر مالک کی طلب کے بعد اس کو روکے تو ضامن ہوگا پھر زوائد پر تعدی کی صورت یہ ہے کہ غاصب اس کو تلف کر دے یا ذبح کر کے کھا جائے یا فروخت کر کے سپرد کر دے۔ قوله وفى الظبية المخرجة ... الخ - امام شافعی کے قیاس " كما في الظبية المخرجة من الحرم “ کا جواب ہے کہ یہ مسیح نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ قیاس اگر چھوڑنے پر قابو پانے سے پہلے کی حالت پر ہے، تب تو یہ ظاہر الفساد ہے کیونکہ قابو پانے سے پہلے اگر بچہ تلف ہو جائے تو اس پر ضمان ہی نہیں اس واسطے کہ اس کی طرف سے رو کنا نہیں پایا گیا اور اگر قیاس مذکور قابو پانے کے بعد کی حالت پر ہے تو یہ بھی صحیح نہیں کیونکہ اس صورت میں ضمان کا وجوب رو کنے کی وجہ سے ہے کہ اس نے صاحب حق یعنی شرع کے مطالبہ کے بعد روکا ہے اس لئے کہ صید حرم میں حق شارع کا ہے اور شارع کا مطالبہ یہ ہے کہ اصل یعنی ہرنی کو اس کے بچہ کے ساتھ چھوڑا جائے۔ ہمارے اکثر متقدمین مشائخ کے یہاں جواب اسی طور پر ہے۔ قوله ولو اطلق الجواب .... الخ - اور اگر جواب مطلق ہو۔ یعنی بہر صورت ضامن ہونے کا حکم مان لیا جائے تب بھی کوئی اعتراض نہیں ہو سکتا۔ کیونکہ یہ ضمان جنایت یعنی جرم کا تاوان ہے نہ کہ ضمان غصب اس لئے جرم اگر متکر رہو تو جرمانہ متکرر ہوتا ہے۔ مثلاً ایک مرتبہ ہرنی کو نکال لایا تو مجرم ہوا اگر دوبارہ نکالے تو پھر جرمانہ لازم ہو گا۔ نیز یہ جرمانہ اعانت اور اشارہ سے بھی واجب ہوتا ہے یعنی اگر نکالنے میں کسی نے اس کی مدد کی یا اس کو اشارہ سے بتلا دیا تو معین و مشیر بھی مجرم ہوتا ہے۔ حالانکہ یہ غصب نہیں بلکہ جرم ہے اور جب یہ جرمانہ اعانت واشارہ جیسے امور سے بھی واجب ہوتا ہے تو جو فعل اس سے بڑھ کر ہے یعنی مستحق امن ہرنی پر اپنا قبضہ جمالینا۔ اس سے بطریق اولی واجب ہوگا۔ حاصل یہ کہ ہرنی کے مسئلہ میں اگر مان لیا جائے کہ اس کے بچہ پر تعدی سے تاوان واجب ہوتا ہے۔ تو وہ ضمان جنایت اور تاوان واجب ہے وہ ضمان غصہ نہیں ہے۔ پس ضمان غصب کو ضمان جنایت پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ باندی میں ولادت سے جو نقصان آئے وہ غاصب کے ضمان میں ہوگا اگر بچہ کی قیمت سے نقصان پورا ہو سکتا ہو تو غاصب سے ضمان ساقط ہو جائے گا قال وما نقصت الجارية بالولادة فى ضمان الغاصب فان كان فى قيمة الولد وفاء به جبر النقصان بالولد وسقط ضمانه عن الغاصب وقال زفر والشافعى لا ينجبر النقصان بالولد لان الولد ملكه فلا يصلح جابرًا لملكه كما في ولد الظبية وكما اذا هلك الولد قبل الردّ او ماتت الام وبالولد وفاء وصار كما اذا جز صوف شاة غيره او قطع قوائم شجر غیره او خصی عبد غيره او علمه الحرفة فاضناه ،التعليم ولنا ان سبب الزيادة والنقصان واحد وهو الولادة او العلوق على ما عرف وعند ذلك لا يعد نقصانا فلا يوجب ضمانا وصار كما اذا غصب جارية سمينة فهزلت ثم سمنت او سقطت ثنيتها ثم نبتت او قطع يد المغصوب في يده واخذ ارشها واداه مع العبد يحتسب عن نقصان القطع وولد الظبية ممنوع ، وكذا اذا ماتت الام وتخريج
Translation: Our proof is that ghasb is taking possession of another's property in a way that removes the owner's possession. As we have mentioned, and over this increase the owner did not have possession at all such that the usurper could remove it. And if one were to consider that his possession over the child is established, then the usurper did not remove it because apparently he did not detain it, until the usurper detains the child after the owner's demand, then he will be liable. Similarly, if he commits transgression against it, as stated in the book. Transgression is like destroying it, slaughtering and eating it, or selling and delivering it. As for the gazelle taken out of the Haram, he is not liable for its offspring if it perishes before gaining control over releasing it; he is liable only due to detention when it perishes after that, after the claim of the right-holder, i.e., the Shari'ah, due to detention. Most of our shaykhs hold this. And if the answer is absolute, then it is a penalty for a crime; therefore, if the crime is repeated, the penalty repeats. And it is also wajib by assistance and indication. So if dhaman is wajib for that which is less than this, and that is taking possession of the one entitled to security, then it is more appropriate. Explanation of 'Wa lana inna al-ghasb' etc. - Our proof is that the meaning of ghasb is to take possession of another's property in a way that removes the owner's possession, as mentioned at the beginning of Kitab al-Ghasb. And over this increase, the owner's possession was not previously established, such that the usurper could remove it. So the mentioned difference is based on the definition of ghasb. Objection: According to the mentioned reasoning, if a slave-girl is usurped while pregnant, then compensation for her child should be wajib, because possession over it was established, whereas whether the slave-girl is usurped pregnant or not, the usurper is not liable for her child. Answer: The answer given in Anayah, Binayah and other commentaries is that the fetus, before separation, is not property; rather, it is considered a defect in the slave-girl. So it does not constitute establishing a hand over another's property. However, the author of Nata'ij has discussed this answer, stating that if the fetus is not property before separation, then emancipating or making tadbir over the fetus should not be valid, because it is apparent that the subject of emancipation and tadbir is owned property. Yet emancipation and tadbir of the fetus are valid. This indicates that the fetus is property. And even if we accept that the subject of emancipation and tadbir need not be property, rather it is sufficient that it be owned (milk), and ownership can be realized in non-property, then too the mentioned answer is not befitting the text of the book. Because the essence of the answer is that in the case of usurping a pregnant slave-girl, the reason for the non-liability of the child is that the fetus is not property before separation, not that the owner's possession over it was not established. While the book said that the owner's hand was not established over this increase. 'And if it were considered established' etc. - And if, considering the ownership through the mother, one assumes that the owner's possession over the offspring is established by estimation, then too the usurper did not remove that estimable possession because the apparent situation is that the usurper does not detain it from the owner. Until after the owner's demand, if he detains it, then he will be liable. As for transgression over the increase, it is when the usurper destroys it, slaughters and eats it, or sells and delivers it. 'And regarding the gazelle taken out' etc. - The response to Imam Shafi'i's analogy 'like the gazelle taken out of the Haram' is that this is not correct because if this analogy applies to the state before gaining control over releasing, then it is obviously invalid because if the offspring perishes before gaining control, there is no dhaman because detention was not found on its part. And if the analogy applies to the state after gaining control, then it is also not correct because in this case, the obligation of dhaman is due to detention; he detained after the claim of the right-holder, i.e., the Shari'ah, because hunting in the Haram involves a right of the Lawgiver, and the Lawgiver's claim is that the original (the mother) should be released along with her offspring. Most of our early shaykhs have this answer. 'And if the answer is absolute' etc. - And if one accepts the answer absolutely, i.e., that he is liable in any case, then there is no objection. Because this dhaman is the penalty for a crime (jinayat), not dhaman of ghasb. Therefore, if the crime is repeated, the penalty repeats. For example, if he brought out the gazelle once, he became a criminal; if he brings it out again, the penalty becomes necessary. Furthermore, this penalty is also wajib by assistance and indication; i.e., if someone helped him in bringing it out or indicated it, then the assistant and the indicator are also criminals. Whereas this is not ghasb but a crime. And when this penalty is wajib by things like assistance and indication, then the act which is greater than that, i.e., taking possession of a gazelle entitled to security, it is all the more wajib. The conclusion is that if it is accepted in the case of the gazelle that transgression over its offspring necessitates a penalty, that penalty is dhaman jinayat and not dhaman ghasb. Therefore, it is not correct to analogize dhaman ghasb to dhaman jinayat. As for the slave-girl, any depreciation caused by birth is under the dhaman of the usurper. If the value of the child covers that depreciation, then the depreciation is compensated by the child and the dhaman is dropped from the usurper. He said: 'And what the slave-girl depreciates due to birth is under the dhaman of the usurper. If the value of the child suffices to cover it, the depreciation is compensated by the child and his dhaman is dropped.' Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: 'The depreciation is not compensated by the child because the child is his property, so it cannot serve as compensation for his property, as in the case of the gazelle's offspring, and as when the child perishes before return, or the mother dies and the child suffices, and it becomes like when someone shears the wool of another's sheep, or cuts off the limbs of another's tree, or castrates another's slave, or teaches him a craft and thereby damages him - the instruction (is not compensation).' Our proof: The cause of the increase and the depreciation is one, i.e., birth or conception, as is known. So then it is not considered a depreciation, and hence does not obligate dhaman. It becomes like when someone usurps a fat slave-girl and she becomes thin then becomes fat again, or her front tooth falls out and then grows back, or he cuts off the hand of the usurped property in his hand and takes its compensation (arsh) and returns it with the slave - it offsets the depreciation of the cut. And the case of the gazelle's offspring is rejected. Similarly, if the mother dies and the child suffices, etc.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage addresses the liability (dhaman) for the offspring of a usurped property, specifically a pregnant slave-girl or an animal. The central dispute is between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i (and Zufar). The Hanafi position, stated clearly, is that the usurper is not liable for the offspring unless he detains it after the owner's demand or commits a direct transgression (e.g., killing, selling). The reasoning is rooted in the definition of ghasb: it requires the usurper to remove the owner's established possession over the property. Since the offspring is not a separate property before birth, the owner's hand (yad) was never established over it; thus, there is no possession to remove. The opposite view analogizes to the case of a gazelle taken from the Haram, where the offspring is liable. The Hanafi response provides a crucial distinction: the gazelle case falls under dhaman jinayat (penalty for a crime against the sanctity of the Haram), not dhaman ghasb. In jinayat, liability arises from detention after the claim of the Lawgiver, and it can be repeated, and even assistance or indication triggers liability. Therefore, it is not analogous to ghasb. The passage also discusses the scenario where the offspring covers the depreciation caused by birth to the mother; the Hanafi view holds that the depreciation is compensated by the child, and the usurper's liability is discharged, unlike Shafi'i who argues the child is already the usurper's property and cannot compensate. The commentary follows the author's sequence: first presenting the Hanafi proof based on definition, then addressing objections and refinements, and finally the inter-madhhab debate. All examples are from Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Taking possession of another's property in a way that removes the owner's possession.
ضمان (dhaman): Liability or guarantee to compensate for loss or damage.
حمل (haml): The fetus or offspring in the womb before separation.
جنایت (jinayat): A crime or tort, especially in the context of violating sanctity (e.g., hunting in the Haram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, when is a usurper liable for the offspring of a usurped slave-girl?
A) Always, because the offspring is part of the property.
B) Only if he detains the offspring after the owner's demand or commits a direct transgression.
C) Only if the owner demands compensation.
D) Never, because the offspring is not property.

Key Takeaway
The usurper is not liable for offspring automatically because the offspring is not property before separation and the owner's hand was never established over it; liability arises only upon detention after demand or direct transgression.

Compensating the Decrease: Unity of Cause in Ghasb
Hanafi ruling and inter-madhhab dispute on compensating value loss from childbirth of usurped slave-girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the child's value compensates the decrease in the usurped slave-girl's value due to childbirth, and evaluate the Shafi'i and Zufar counter-argument.

Core Idea
If the same cause produces both a loss and a gain, the gain compensates the loss—unity of cause eliminates separate liability.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in the law of usurpation (ghasb): when a usurped slave-girl gives birth, causing a drop in her market value. The Hanafi school rules that the value of the newborn child automatically compensates that loss. This ruling is based on a key principle: ittihad al-sabab (unity of cause). The debate with Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar hinges on whether the child, which belongs to the usurper, can serve as compensation. By analyzing their proofs, you will understand how the Hanafi school prioritizes causal unity over ownership.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: the child's value compensates the decrease in the mother's value, and the usurper's liability for that decrease is discharged.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State that Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar hold that the child cannot compensate the decrease because it is the usurper's own property.
Zufar is a Hanafi jurist who often disagrees with Abu Hanifa on ghasb issues.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the analogies (shearing wool, cutting branches, castration, etc.) that the opponent uses to argue that an increase cannot offset a loss when the increase belongs to the person compensating.
These analogies are designed to show that ownership of the increase prevents it from serving as compensation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand that the Hanafi school rejects these analogies because they lack unity of cause. In the slave-girl case, both the decrease and the increase arise from childbirth—the same cause. In the opponent's analogies, the loss and gain have different causes.
The Hanafi response also points out that the gazelle analogy is invalid because the fawn is not the usurper's property.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: under the Hanafi view, if the child's value suffices, no extra payment is needed. Under the Shafi'i/Zufar view, the full decrease must be paid in addition to returning mother and child.
This difference matters in cases where the child's value is less than the decrease, or where the child dies before return.

قال وما نقصت الجارية بالولادة فى ضمان الغاصب فان كان فى قيمة الولد وفاء به جبر النقصان بالولد وسقط ضمانه عن الغاصب وقال زفر والشافعى لا ينجبر النقصان بالولد لان الولد ملكه فلا يصلح جابرًا لملكه كما في ولد الظبية وكما اذا هلك الولد قبل الردّ او ماتت الام وبالولد وفاء وصار كما اذا جز صوف شاة غيره او قطع قوائم شجر غیره او خصی عبد غيره او علمه الحرفة فاضناه التعليم ولنا ان سبب الزيادة والنقصان واحد وهو الولادة او العلوق على ما عرف وعند ذلك لا يعد نقصانا فلا يوجب ضمانا وصار كما اذا غصب جارية سمينة فهزلت ثم سمنت او سقطت ثنيتها ثم نبتت او قطع يد المغصوب في يده واخذ ارشها واداه مع العبد يحتسب عن نقصان القطع وولد الظبية ممنوع ، وكذا اذا ماتت الام وتخريج الثانية ان الولادة ليست بسبب لموت الام اذ الولادة لا تفضى اليه غالبا وبخلافيما اذا مات الولد قبل الرد لانه لابد من رد اصله للبرائة فكذا لابد من رد خلفه والخصاء لا يعد زيادة لانه غرض بعض الفسقة، ولا اتحاد في السبب فيما وراء ذلك من المسائل لان سبب النقصان القطع والجز وسبب الزيادة النمو وسبب النقصان التعليم وسبب الزيادة فهمه
He said: And what the slave-girl decreases in value due to childbirth, that is in the guarantee of the usurper. So if the value of the child suffices to cover it, the decrease is compensated by the child, and the guarantor's liability falls from the usurper. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: The decrease is not compensated by the child, because the child is his property, so it cannot serve as a compensator for his property, as in the case of the fawn of a gazelle (taken from the Haram), and as when the child dies before return, or the mother dies while the child's value suffices, and it becomes like when one shears the wool of another's sheep, or cuts the branches of another's tree, or castrates another's slave, or teaches him a craft and the teaching weakens him. Our proof: The cause of both increase and decrease is one, namely childbirth or conception, as is known. In that case, it is not considered a decrease, so it does not necessitate liability. And it becomes like when one usurps a fat slave-girl, then she becomes thin, then becomes fat again, or her front teeth fall out then grow back, or when the hand of a usurped slave is cut off while in his (the usurper's) possession and he takes the blood-money and returns it with the slave, it counts against the decrease of the hand. And the case of the fawn of a gazelle is rejected. Likewise, when the mother dies, the second derivation: childbirth is not a cause for the mother's death, because childbirth does not normally lead to it. Contrary to when the child dies before return, because it is necessary to return its origin for discharge, so likewise it is necessary to return its substitute. And castration is not considered an increase because it is the desire of some wicked people. And there is no unity of cause in the issues beyond that, because the cause of decrease is cutting and shearing, and the cause of increase is growth, and the cause of decrease is teaching, and the cause of increase is understanding.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on a specific case in the law of usurpation (ghasb): if a usurped slave-girl gives birth, causing a drop in her market value, the child's value is used to compensate that loss. The ruling is attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa and forms part of the Zahir al-Riwayah. The opposing view is held by Imam Zufar (a Hanafi jurist who often disagrees) and Imam al-Shafi'i. They argue that since the child belongs to the usurper (because the offspring of a usurped slave-girl is owned by the usurper in Hanafi law, though the mother is returned), it cannot be used to compensate a loss in the usurper's own property; that would be like paying oneself. They draw analogies: (1) a gazelle fawn taken from the Haram—if the mother gazelle is taken and gives birth, the fawn is not used to compensate any loss because the fawn is also sacred; (2) if the child dies before return, the full value of the child is still due; (3) if the mother dies, the child's value is similarly insufficient; (4) shearing wool, cutting branches, castrating a slave, or teaching a craft that weakens—none of these are compensated by the resulting increase. The Hanafi response is built on the concept of 'unity of cause' (ittihad al-sabab). Both the decrease in the mother's value and the value of the child arise from the same cause: childbirth. Therefore, the decrease is not treated as a compensable loss because it is accompanied by a corresponding increase. This is similar to cases where a fat slave-girl becomes thin then fat again, or teeth fall out then regrow, or a hand is cut off and the blood-money is paid—the loss is considered offset. The Hanafis reject the gazelle analogy because the gazelle case involves a sacred right of the Lawgiver (the Haram), not private property, and the fawn is not owned by the usurper. In the slave-girl case, the child is owned by the usurper, so it can serve as compensation. The passage also distinguishes other analogies: castration is not an increase because it is a defect; teaching does not create a unity of cause because the loss and gain have different causes.

Key Terms
الضمان (al-daman): Liability or guarantee to compensate for loss or damage.
الجابر (al-jabir): Compensator; that which makes up for a deficiency.
الولادة (al-wilada): Childbirth; the act of giving birth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what compensates the decrease in value of a usurped slave-girl due to childbirth?
A) The usurper pays the full decrease in cash.
B) The value of the child born to her compensates the loss.
C) No compensation is due because childbirth is natural.
D) The owner receives both mother and child and must pay the difference.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the child's value compensates the decrease in the mother's value from childbirth because the cause (childbirth) is the same, so the loss is not independent.

intermediate
6 min
Compensation for Childbirth of a Usurped Slave
Ruling on depreciation from childbirth and inter-school dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on depreciation from childbirth of a usurped female slave and evaluate the opposing proof based on unity of cause.

Core Idea
The child compensates the loss because the cause of increase and decrease is one.

When a usurped female slave gives birth, her value depreciates. The Hanafi school holds that the child itself compensates this loss, discharging the usurper. This ruling is contested by Imam Zufar (within the Hanafi school) and by Imam Shafi'i. Their objection is that the child is owned by the same owner, so it cannot compensate a loss to its own property. In this lesson, we dissect the Hanafi proof of 'unity of cause' (ittihad al-sabab) and see why the majority Hanafi view prevails.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the usurper is liable for the depreciation of the female slave caused by childbirth, but this liability is satisfied by the child itself. If the child's value equals or exceeds the depreciation, the usurper pays nothing additional; if it is less, the shortfall is deducted.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Zufar (a Hanafi) and Imam Shafi'i hold that the child does not compensate the loss. They argue that since the child belongs to the owner, it cannot be used to compensate a loss to the owner's own property—it would be like taking from one pocket to fill another.
Imam Ahmad is also reported to hold this view.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponents invoke analogical reasoning (qiyas): they compare this case to several situations where an increase does not compensate a loss—e.g., a doe's fawn (the fawn is separate property), the child dies before return, the mother dies, shearing wool, cutting branches, castration, teaching a profession. In all these, the loss is not canceled by the increase.
These are seven specific analogies cited in the text.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is based on the principle of unity of cause (ittihad al-sabab): the same event (childbirth or settling of sperm) produces both the increase (the child) and the decrease (the depreciation). Since the cause is one, the decrease is not a separate compensable loss; it is 'absorbed' by the increase. The opponent's analogies are invalid because in those cases the causes are not unified: the loss arises from one action (e.g., cutting) and the increase from another (e.g., growth).
The Hanafis support their position with counter-analogies: a fat slave becomes thin then fat again; teeth fall out then regrow; a hand is cut and compensation is paid with the slave.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under the Hanafi view, if the child's value covers the depreciation, the owner receives both the slave and the child, and the usurper pays nothing. Under the opposing view, the usurper must pay the full depreciation amount in addition to returning the slave and child.
This difference directly affects the financial liability of the usurper.

The second [point] is that childbirth is not a cause of the mother's death, because childbirth does not usually lead to it. And contrary to when the child dies before return, because it is necessary to return its origin for acquittal, so likewise it is necessary to return its successor. Castration is not considered an increase because it is the desire of some immoral people. There is no unity of cause in the cases beyond that, because the cause of decrease is cutting and shearing, and the cause of increase is growth... (followed by Urdu commentary explaining the rulings, the dispute with Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i, the Hanafi proof of unity of cause, and the refutation of analogies).
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf Ul Hadaya is an expansion of a ruling from Al-Hidayah on the compensation for the depreciation of a usurped female slave due to childbirth. The ruling states that the child itself compensates for the loss: if the child's value covers the depreciation, the usurper is discharged; otherwise, the shortfall is deducted. Imam Zufar (a Hanafi) and Imam Shafi'i disagree, arguing that since the child belongs to the owner, it cannot compensate for a loss to its own property. They analogize to cases like a doe's fawn, or where the child dies before return, or the mother dies, or shearing wool, cutting branches, castration, or teaching a profession. The Hanafi response (attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) is that the cause of both the increase (the child) and the decrease (the depreciation) is one and the same: either childbirth (according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) or the settling of the sperm (according to Abu Hanifa). When the cause is unified, the decrease is not considered a separate compensable loss. They support this with analogous cases: a fat slave becomes thin then fat again; front teeth fall out then regrow; a slave's hand is cut and the usurper pays compensation and returns the slave with the compensation. In these three cases, the loss is considered compensated because the cause of loss and return is the same. The author then addresses an objection that in those cases the causes are not truly unified (the cause of emaciation is different from the cause of fattening), and notes that Al-Hidayah itself rebuts Imam Shafi'i's analogy on the basis that the cause is not unified in the analogies they propose. Thus, the Hanafi position remains that the childbirth depreciation is compensated by the child.

Key Terms
جبر نقصان (jabr nuqsan): Compensation of a loss; here, paying for the depreciation of the slave's value.
ولادت (wiladat): Childbirth; the event that causes both increase (the child) and decrease (depreciation of the mother).
اتحاد سبب (ittihad sabab): Unity of cause; the idea that one cause produces both the increase and the decrease, so they cancel out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, if a usurped female slave gives birth and depreciates by 20, and the child is worth 20, what happens?
A) The usurper must pay 20 to the owner.
B) The usurper gives the slave and child to the owner and owes nothing.
C) The usurper keeps the child as compensation.
D) The owner must pay the usurper for the child.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on childbirth depreciation relies on the principle that when a single cause produces both a gain and a loss, the loss is offset by the gain.
