The Principle of Ittihad al-Sabab: Offsetting Damage in Usurpation of a Pregnant Slave (Inter-Madhhab Dispute)
Hanafi defense of ittihad al-sabab with seven refutations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle of ittihad al-sabab (unity of cause) and apply it to distinguish when a concurrent increase offsets damage in ghasb cases.

Core Idea
When the same cause produces both increase and damage, the increase offsets the damage.

Is a usurper liable for damage caused to a pregnant slave-girl when she gives birth, or does the child's value compensate the loss? This lesson unpacks a classic inter-madhhab dispute where the Hanafi school defends the principle of ittihad al-sabab (unity of cause) to exonerate the usurper. By tracing the Hanafi proofs and responses to opposing analogies, you will learn how causation analysis overrides the simple fact that the child belongs to the owner.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the precise ruling: the child's value offsets the damage caused by birth because the cause (birth or pregnancy) is unified for both increase and damage.
Note the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa considers the cause as 'settling of sperm', Sahibayn as 'birth'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Zufar, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad hold that the child cannot offset damage as it is the owner's property. They cite seven analogical examples.
These examples are meant to show that increase does not automatically offset damage.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand each analogy: doe's fawn not offsetting, child dying before return, mother dying, shearing wool, cutting tree, castrating slave, teaching a craft.
These analogies rely on the idea that increase and damage have separate causes.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine how the Hanafis distinguish each analogy: (1) non-Zahir al-Riwayah allows offset for doe; (2) mother's death usually not caused by birth, so cause not unified; (3) if child dies, mother not returned in original state; (4-5) causes are separate; (6) castration is forbidden, not a valid increase; (7) cause of increase (understanding) differs from cause of damage (physical exertion).
The key is whether the cause of increase and damage is one and the same.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, Hanafis hold no liability if mother and child are returned alive (cause unified). Opposing schools require compensation. The Zahir al-Riwayah position is that if mother dies, no offset, but the author of Hidayah inclines toward offset under non-Zahir al-Riwayah.
This shows how the same event can yield different rulings across schools based on causation theory.

مشقت ہے جس کی وجہ سے کمزوری آجاتی ہے اور زیادتی کا سبب اس کی فہم یعنی جو رتِ ذہن ہے۔ سوال بچہ تو غاصب کے پاس امانت ہوتا ہے تو یہ مضمون کا خلیفہ کیسے ہو سکتا ہے؟ جواب ... صاحب ہدایہ نے اس کی طرف اپنے عَنِ المحصلين خيرا
His statement: 'And Zufar said...' - Imam Zufar, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad (may Allah have mercy on them) say that the damage is not compensated by the child, because the child is also the property of the owner, so it cannot be that his property compensates the damage of his own property. For example: 1. The damage of a doe taken out of the sanctuary is not compensated by its fawn. 2. Similarly, if before return the child dies, or 3. Due to birth the mother dies and the value of the child is sufficient to cover the indemnity, then in these cases also by consensus the damage is not compensated, and this is analogous to (4) shearing the wool of another's goat, or (5) cutting the trunk of another's tree, or (6) castrating another's slave, or (7) teaching a slave a craft and in learning he becomes weak and emaciated - in all seven cases he is liable for the damage even if the value increases. His statement: 'And for us the cause of increase...' - Our proof is that here the cause of both increase and damage is unified, and that is birth (according to the Sahibayn) or the settling of the sperm (according to Imam Abu Hanifa). And when the cause of increase and damage is a single thing, then birth is considered damage. So it will not be a cause for liability, and this is like: a plump slave-girl was usurped and she became thin, then later became plump again; or her front teeth fell out later regrew; or a usurped slave's hand was cut and the usurper paid compensation and returned the slave with the compensation - in these three cases the damage is compensated. His statement: 'Then she became thin, then fat...' - On this, one may say that in these two cases the cause is not unified. Because the cause of damage - in the first case thinness and in the second case loss of the central incisor - is different from the cause of increase - in the first case fatness and in the second case growth of the central incisor. However, later the author of Hidayah rejects the analogy of Imam Shafi'i on the same basis that in the analogized case the cause is not unified. So then how can it be correct for that person to analogize to the mentioned two cases when they also lack unity of cause? His statement: 'And the fawn of the doe...' - From here begins the response to the seven examples of Imam Zufar and Shafi'i. The response to (1) is that it is not accepted that the damage of the doe is not compensated by the value of the fawn, because in non-Zahir al-Riwayah the damage is compensated by the value of the fawn (the author of Hidayah inclines to this view, so the mentioned analogy is incorrect). The response to (2) is that in the case of the mother's death, regarding compensation by the value of the child, there are two narrations: one that compensation occurs, provided the child's value is sufficient (this is non-Zahir al-Riwayah); under this narration the mentioned analogy is not against us. But Zahir al-Riwayah is that compensation does not occur. Under this narration the analogy is against us. The answer is that the cause of the slave-girl's death is not the birth, because usually birth does not cause death. Thus birth is the cause of increase, while death occurred due to some other cause, so the cause is not unified. And our discussion is only when the cause of increase and damage is unified. (3) The meaning of 'and as when the child dies before return' - The response is that here for exoneration it is necessary to return the original (the mother) in the same condition as she was usurped, so returning the substitute (the child) also becomes necessary, but he did not return the mother in that condition; rather he returned her deficient due to birth. Since before return the child died, what was obligatory (returning with the child) was not done, so he is liable. Because the discussion is only when he returns the mother with her child. (6) 'Or castrates another's slave' - The response is that castrating a slave, which you considered an increase, is not an increase. It is only the desire of some perverts, so it has no consideration in Shari'ah because Shari'ah has declared this act forbidden. (7,5,2) The response is that in these issues, although there is increase, the cause is not unified, because in cutting tree branches and clipping wool, the cause of damage is the cutting/trimming, and the cause of increase is the growing; and in teaching a craft, the cause of damage is the teaching which causes exertion resulting in weakness, and the cause of increase is his understanding, i.e., sharpness of mind. Question: The child is a trust (amanah) with the usurper, so how can it be a substitute for the principal? Answer: The author of Hidayah has indicated towards this by his statement 'and in that case it is not far to consider it damage', which repels the question. May Allah reward the author for his precise writing, how pure his intellect, how deep his insight, and how delicate his understanding. May Allah reward him well on behalf of students.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning a usurped pregnant slave-girl who gives birth. The passage presents the Hanafi position against Imam Zufar, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad. The core issue is whether the value of the child can offset the damage caused to the mother by the birth. The opposing scholars argue that since the child belongs to the owner, it cannot compensate for the owner's own loss; they cite seven analogous cases where damage is not offset despite an increase in value. The Hanafis respond that the cause of both the increase (the child) and the damage (the birth or pregnancy) is unified, so the birth is legally treated as damage, not as an increase that creates liability. They also distinguish each of the seven examples individually: some are based on non-reliable narrations, some lack unity of cause, and some involve forbidden acts. The passage also addresses a potential objection about the child being a trust (amanah) and explains why it can still serve as a substitute. The discussion highlights the Hanafi principle that khiyana (breach of trust) is not established if the damage is due to the same cause that produced the increase. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to the author of Hidayah leans toward compensation in non-Zahir al-Riwayah, but the Zahir al-Riwayah position is that damage is not compensated when the mother dies in birth, as the cause is not unified.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation or wrongful appropriation of another's property without their consent.
جبر نقصان (jabr nuqsan): Compensation of damage by offsetting it against an increase or benefit that accrued to the damaged property.
سبب (sabab): Cause; the event or action that legally produces an effect (increase or damage).
اتحاد سبب (ittihad al-sabab): Unity of cause; when the same event or action gives rise to both an increase and a damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi view, why does the value of the child offset the damage caused to a usurped pregnant slave-girl?
A) Because the child is not considered property
B) Because the cause of the increase and the damage is unified
C) Because the child belongs to the usurper
D) Because the damage is less than the increase

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that when a single cause produces both an increase and a damage, the increase offsets the damage, a principle called ittihad al-sabab, which overrides the mere fact that the increase belongs to the owner.

intermediate
8 min
Condition for Offsetting Decrease with Increase in Usurpation (Ittihad al-Sabab)
Defends the condition of unified cause for offsetting decrease with increase in usurpation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of ittihad al-sabab for offsetting decrease with increase in usurpation, apply it to scenarios involving childbirth, death, castration, and other mixed increases and decreases, and distinguish between unified and separate causes.

Core Idea
In usurpation, a decrease is offset by an increase only if both arise from the same cause; separate causes require independent compensation.

This passage from Al-Hidayah defends the Hanafi rule that when a usurped item suffers both an increase and a decrease, the decrease may be compensated by the increase only if both share a single cause (ittiḥād al-sabab). The author, Al-Marghinani, answers several objections that challenge this condition, clarifying its application in cases like a doe giving birth and dying, a slave-girl dying after childbirth, castration, and shearing wool. Understanding this condition is crucial for correctly determining liability in usurpation cases.

Guided Path
1
State the General Rule
Recall the Hanafi rule: when a usurper returns an item that has both increased and decreased, if the cause of both is the same, the decrease is compensated by the increase. If the causes are separate, the usurper must compensate the decrease independently.
This rule is the axis around which the objections revolve.
2
Identify the Objections
List the objections raised: 1) Doe gives birth and dies, 2) Slave-girl dies after childbirth, 3) Child dies before return, 4) Castration of a slave, 5) Cutting branches and shearing wool, 6) Teaching a craft. For each, the objector claims that the increase (child, wool, etc.) should offset the decrease, but Al-Marghinani explains why the condition is not met.
The passage responds sequentially; follow the author's order.
3
Analyze the Cause in Each Objection
For each objection, determine whether the increase and decrease share a single cause. For example, in the doe case: childbirth (increase) and death (decrease) are not necessarily caused by the same event; death may have an independent cause. In castration, the act is forbidden and not a valid increase. In cutting branches, the decrease is from cutting, increase from growth – separate causes.
The key is distinguishing between the immediate physical change and the underlying cause.
4
Apply the Condition to the Slave-girl's Death
When the slave-girl (mother) dies after childbirth, there are two narrations: one (non-Zahir al-Riwayah) allows compensation if the child's value suffices, the other (Zahir al-Riwayah) denies it because death is likely from a separate cause. Al-Marghinani leans toward the Zahir al-Riwayah view, emphasizing that the cause is not unified.
This shows the practical impact of the condition and the tarjih mechanism.
5
Conclude with the Child as Substitute
If the mother is returned deficient (after childbirth) and the child dies before return, the usurper is liable because he failed to return the substitute (child) as required. The child is an amana, but the obligation is to return both mother and child in their original state.
The ruling is consistent: the increase (child) is not a substitute when causes are separate.

كتاب الغصب
۳۷۰
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲
ا کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ولادت کی وجہ سے ہرنی کے نقصان کا بچہ کی قیمت سے پورانہ ہونا تسلیم نہیں ہے کیونکہ غیر ظاہر الروایۃ میں بچہ کی قیمت سے جبر نقصان ہو جائے گا ( صاحب ہدایہ اسی طرف مائل ہیں ، پس اس پر قیاس مذکور غلط ہوا ) ۔ -۲- کا جواب یہ ہے کہ موت ام کی صورت میں بچہ کی قید سے جبر نقصان کی بابت دو روایتیں ہیں ایک یہ کہ جبر نقصان ہو جائے گا، جب کہ بچہ کی قیمت وافی ہو ( یہ غیر ظاہر روایت ہے ) اس روایت پر تو قیاس مذکور ہمارے خلاف نہیں ہے۔ اور ظاہر الروایۃہ یہ ہے کہ جبر نقصان نہیں ہوگا۔ اس روایت پر قیاس مذکور ہمارے خلاف ہے۔ سو جواب یہ ہے کہ باندی کے مرنے کا سبب ولادت نہیں ہے کیونکہ اکثر اوقات ولادت سے موت واقع نہیں ہوتی ۔ گویا ولادت تو زیادتی کا سبب ہے، رہی موت سودہ کسی دوسرے سبب سے واقع ہوئی ہے، پس سبب متحد نہیں رہا۔ حالانکہ ہماری گفتگو اسی صورت میں ہے جب زیادتی ونقصان کا سبب متحد ہو۔
- معنی و كما اذا هلک الولد قبل الرد " کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں بری ہونے کے لئے اصل یعنی ماں کو جس ٣- صفت پر غصب کیا تھا اسی صفت پر واپس کرنا ضروری ہے تو اس کے خلیفہ یعنی بچہ کو واپس کرنا بھی ضروری ہوا حالانکہ اس نے ماں کو اسی صفت پر واپس نہیں کیا بلکہ ولادت سے ناقص کر کے واپس کیا۔ ادھر واپسی سے پہلے بچہ مر چکا تو بچہ کے ساتھ واپس کرنا جو واجب تھا وہ نہ ہوا لہذا ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ گفتگو اسی صورت میں ہے جب ماں کو اس کے بچہ کے ساتھ واپس کرے۔
۶
- لینی’ او خصی عبد غیرہ " کا جواب یہ ہے کہ غلام خصی کرنا جس کو تم نے زیادتی شمار کیا ہے یہ زیادتی نہیں ہے،
یہ تو بعض مشاق کی غرض ہوتی ہے، تو شرع میں اس کا کوئی اعتبار نہ ہوگا کیونکہ شریعت نے اس فعل کو حرام قرار دیا ہے۔ ۷،۵،۲- کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ان مسائل میں اگر چہ زیادتی ہے لیکن سبب متحد نہیں ہے، اس لئے کہ قطع قوائم شجر اور جو صوف میں نقصان کا سبب پیڑی کاٹنا اور اون تراشنا اور زیادتی کا سبب اس کا بڑھنا ہے اور تعلیم حرفت میں نقصان کا سبب تعلیم ہے کہ یہ موجب مشقت ہے جس کی وجہ سے کمزوری آجاتی ہے اور زیادتی کا سبب اس کی فہم یعنی جو رتِ ذہن ہے۔
سوال بچہ تو غاصب کے پاس امانت ہوتا ہے تو یہ مضمون کا خلیفہ کیسے ہو سکتا ہے؟
جواب ... صاحب ہدایہ نے اس کی طرف اپنے قول وعند ذلك لا بعد نقصاناً " سے اشارہ کیا ہے کہ اس سے سوال کا دفعیہ ہو جاتا ہے۔ فَاللَّهِ دَرُ الْمُصَفِ عالمًا أدق تحريرهُ وَ مَا أَزْکى قريحته و ما امعن نظرهُ وَ مَا الطف ذَهَبَهُ، جَزَاهُ اللَّهُ عَنِ
المحصلين خيرا
Book of Usurpation. 370. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume 12. Answer to the first: That the compensation of the doe's loss by the value of the young is not accepted because in non-Zahir al-Riwayah, the loss is compensated by the value of the young (the author of Hidayah leans towards this, so the mentioned analogy is incorrect). Answer to the second: Regarding the death of the mother, there are two narrations concerning compensation by the young: one is that it will compensate if the young's value is sufficient (this is non-Zahir al-Riwayah), so the mentioned analogy does not go against us. The Zahir al-Riwayah is that it does not compensate. This narration goes against us. The answer is that the cause of the slave-girl's death is not childbirth, because most times death does not occur from childbirth. Childbirth is a cause of increase, while death occurred from some other cause, so the cause is not unified, whereas our discussion is specifically when the cause of increase and decrease is unified. Meaning: 'As if the young dies before return': The answer is that here for exoneration, it is necessary to return the original (the mother) in the same condition as when usurped, so returning her substitute (the child) is also necessary. However, he did not return the mother in that condition but returned her deficient by childbirth. Since the child died before return, the obligation to return the child was not fulfilled, so he is liable. Because the discussion concerns the case where the mother is returned with her child. 'Or castrating another's slave': The answer is that castrating a slave, which you considered an increase, is not an increase; it is merely the desire of some perverts, so it has no validity in Shari'ah because the Shari'ah has declared this act forbidden. For issues 2,5,7: The answer is that in these issues, although there is increase, the cause is not unified. For cutting branches and wool, the cause of decrease is cutting and shearing, while the cause of increase is growth. In teaching a craft, the cause of decrease is the teaching (which causes weakness), and the cause of increase is understanding (sharpness of mind). Question: The child is an amana with the usurper, so how can it be a substitute for the mother? Answer: The author of Hidayah indicated by his saying 'And then there is no harm in deficiency' that this answers the question. So excellent is the author (al-Musannif), how precise his writing, how noble his mind, how deep his insight, how subtle his understanding. May Allah reward him well for the scholars.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a set of responses (جواب) to objections raised against the ruling that when a usurper returns a usurped item with both an increase (زيادة) and a decrease (نقصان), if the cause is unified, the decrease may be compensated by the increase. The commentary explains that in the case of a doe (ہرنی) that gives birth and dies, the cause of death is not necessarily childbirth, so the causes are separate; thus, the ruling does not apply. Similarly, the objection that if the child dies before return, the usurper should be liable is answered by stating that the obligation was to return the mother with her child; since the child died, the obligation was not fulfilled, so liability remains. The objection about castration is dismissed because castration is not a legitimate increase in Shari'ah. Finally, the objection that the child is an amana and cannot be a substitute is answered by referring to the author's statement that deficiency (نقصان) is not harmed by the presence of a substitute. The passage emphasizes that the key condition for compensation by increase is the unity of cause (اتحاد السبب).

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyādah): Increase or addition to the usurped property, such as growth of wool or offspring.
نقصان (nuqsān): Decrease or defect in the usurped property, such as cutting branches or shearing wool.
اتحاد السبب (ittiḥād al-sabab): Unification of the cause for both increase and decrease, a condition for offsetting decrease with increase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key condition for a decrease in usurped property to be compensated by an increase, according to the Hanafi school?
A) The increase must be greater in value than the decrease.
B) The cause of both increase and decrease must be the same (ittiḥād al-sabab).
C) The usurper must intend to compensate the decrease.
D) The original owner must approve the offset.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a decrease in usurped property is only offset by an increase if both arise from the same cause; separate causes require independent compensation, and forbidden acts (like castration) are not recognized as valid increases.

8 min
Liability of Usurper for Slave-Girl's Death in Postpartum
Presents the legal dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions on this case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the liability of a usurper who returns a pregnant slave-girl who later dies in postpartum and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A valid return ends liability for new causes, but Abu Hanifa holds the usurper liable for death caused by the pregnancy he initiated.

The following passage from Al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute. A usurper commits zina with a slave-girl, she becomes pregnant, he returns her to the owner, and she dies in postpartum. Is the usurper liable for her full value? Abu Hanifa says yes, for her value on the day she conceived. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say no, because the return was valid and death was from a new cause (childbirth) in the owner's hand. This lesson will dissect the arguments and the practical difference between the two views.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify what Abu Hanifa rules in this case: the usurper is liable for the slave-girl's value on the day she became pregnant. Note the exception for a free woman (no liability).
The value is determined at the time of conception (يوم علقت), not at the time of death or usurpation.
2
Identify the opposing Sahibayn position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that even for a slave-girl, the usurper is not liable for her value upon death after return. They only accept liability for the defect (loss of pregnancy).
The Sahibayn are joined by the three Imams (including Shafi'i and Malik) on this point.
3
Explain the Sahibayn's proof (dalil)
Their key premise: the return was valid (الرد قد صح). Death after return occurred from a new cause (childbirth) that arose in the owner's hand. Thus, the usurper's liability ends. They analogize to cases of fever or flogging after return.
This is a dalil naqli based on the principle that valid return transfers risk back to the owner.
4
Explain Abu Hanifa's response (istihsan)
Abu Hanifa sees the pregnancy as a defect created by the usurper's act. The death in postpartum is a direct consequence of that pregnancy, not a new independent cause. Therefore, liability for the value at conception remains.
This is an istihsan (juristic preference) overriding the general analogy.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa's view, the usurper pays the full value on day of conception. Under the Sahibayn, he only pays compensation for the defect (the loss of the slave-girl's virginity or the value of the pregnancy).
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school follows Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text

تشریح قوله و من غصب جارية ... الخ - غاصب نے مغصو بہ باندی کے ساتھ ( طوعاً وکر با ) زنا کیا اور اس کو حالتِ حمل میں واپس کر دیا۔ باندی مالک کے پاس آکر نفاس میں مرگئی تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک غاصب پر باندی کی اس قیمت کا تاوان ہو گا جو حاملہ ہونے کے دن تھی اور اگر غاصب نے حرہ مغصوبہ کے ساتھ زناء کر کے حمل کی حالت میں واپس کی اور وہ نفاس میں مرگئی تو ضامن نہ ہو گا ۔ صاحبین اور ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک باندی کی صورت مین بھی ضامن نہ ہو گا (البتہ نقصان حمل کا ضامن ہوگا ) ۔ قوله لهما ان الرد.... الخ - صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سبب تلف ولادت ہے جس کا وجود مالک کے یہاں ہوا ہے ۔ پس غاصب کی طرف سے باندی کی واپسی صحیح ہوئی۔ کیونکہ اس نے مستحق کو اس کا حق پہنچا دیا اور ایصال حق ضمان سے برأت کا موجب ہے (صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ غائب نے اس کو معیوب کر دیا۔ لہذا عیب کا تاوان لے گا ) پھر صاحبین نے اس کو چند جزئیات پر قیاس کیا ہے۔
۔ اگر باندی کو غاصب کے پاس بخار آ گیا پھر غاصب نے باندی واپس کر دی اور وہ مالک کے قبضہ میں آکر مرگئی تو وہ ضامن نہیں ہوتا ۔
۲۔ باندی نے غاصب کے قبضہ میں زنا کر یا پھر غاصب نے اس کو واپس کر دیا اور مالک کے قبضہ میں اس کو زنا کی وجہ سے حد ماری گئی اور وہ مر گئی تو غاصب ضامن نہ ہوگا۔
۳۔ کسی نے ایسی باندی خریدی جو بائع کے قبضہ میں حاملہ ہوگئی تھی پھر اس نے مشتری کے پاس بچہ جنا اور حال یہ کہ مشتری کو مل کا علم
A usurped slave-girl, he committed zina with her, she became pregnant, he returned her, she died in postpartum. He will be liable for her value on the day she became pregnant. He said: Whoever usurps a slave-girl and commits zina with her so she becomes pregnant, then returns her, and she dies in her postpartum, he guarantees her value on the day she conceived, and there is no liability upon him regarding a free woman. This is according to Abu Hanifa. They (the two) said: He is not liable even for the slave-girl. Their proof: The return was valid, and the destruction after that was due to an incident that occurred in the owner's hand, which is childbirth, so the usurper is not liable, just as if she had a fever in the usurper's hand, then he returned her, and she died; or if she committed zina in his hand, then he returned her, and she was flogged and died from that; and like the one who bought a slave-girl who had become pregnant in the seller's hand, she gave birth at the buyer's, and died in her postpartum, he cannot recover the price from the seller by agreement. Explanation of the language: 'habit' - to become pregnant; 'allaqat' - to conceive, semen to settle; 'hammat' - to have fever; 'julidat' - to be flogged. Translation: Someone usurped a slave-girl and committed zina with her, so she became pregnant, then he returned her, and she died in her postpartum. Then the usurper is liable for her value on the day she became pregnant. In the case of a free woman, he is not liable. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The two companions say: Even in the case of a slave-girl, he is not liable. Their proof: The return was valid, and death after that occurred due to a cause that arose in the owner's possession, which is childbirth. So the usurper is not liable, just as if she had a fever in the usurper's hand, then he returned her, and she died; or like if the slave-girl committed zina in his hand, then he returned her, then she was flogged and died from that; or like someone bought a slave-girl who had become pregnant in the seller's hand, she gave birth at the buyer's, and died in her postpartum, then by agreement he cannot recover the price from the seller. Explanation of his saying 'and whoever usurps a slave-girl...': The usurper committed zina with the usurped slave-girl (willingly or unwillingly) and returned her in a state of pregnancy. The slave-girl came to the owner and died in her postpartum. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the usurper is liable for the value of the slave-girl on the day she became pregnant. If the usurper committed zina with a free woman who was usurped and returned her in a state of pregnancy, and she died in postpartum, he is not liable. According to the two companions and the three Imams, even in the case of a slave-girl, he is not liable (although he is liable for the loss of the pregnancy). His saying 'their proof...': The proof of the two companions is that the cause of destruction is childbirth, which occurred at the owner's place. So the return of the slave-girl by the usurper was valid. Because he delivered to the owner his right, and delivering a right is the cause of exoneration from liability (the only thing is that the usurper made her defective, so he will pay compensation for the defect). Then the two companions analogized this to several particulars: 1. If the slave-girl had a fever at the usurper's place, then the usurper returned her, and she died at the owner's possession, he is not liable. 2. The slave-girl committed zina at the usurper's possession, then the usurper returned her, and she was flogged for zina at the owner's possession and died, the usurper is not liable. 3. Someone bought a slave-girl who had become pregnant at the seller's possession, then she gave birth at the buyer's, and died in her postpartum, and the buyer had no knowledge...
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of a usurper who makes a slave-girl pregnant and returns her, after which she dies in postpartum. The passage includes the Arabic text of Al-Hidayah (the matn), a glossary of terms, an Urdu translation, and a detailed commentary (tashrih). The ruling: Abu Hanifa holds the usurper liable for the slave-girl's value on the day she became pregnant, but not if she is a free woman. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the usurper is not liable even for a slave-girl. Their proof (dalil) is that the return was valid, and the death occurred from childbirth, a cause arising in the owner's hand. They analogize to cases where a returned slave-girl dies from a fever or flogging after return, where the usurper is not liable. The commentary explains that the only liability remaining is for the defect (the loss of virginity or pregnancy). The lesson underscores the principle that once the usurped item is validly returned to the owner, the usurper's liability for subsequent destructions ends, unless the cause of destruction existed during the usurpation.

Key Terms
غصب (ghaṣb): Unlawful taking of someone's property without their consent, entailing liability for return or compensation.
رد (radd): Return of the usurped property to its owner; if valid, it may end the usurper's liability for future incidents.
نفاس (nifās): Postpartum bleeding period after childbirth; here, the time during which the slave-girl died.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what value must the usurper pay if a slave-girl he made pregnant dies in postpartum after return?
A) The full market value at the time of usurpation
B) The value on the day she became pregnant
C) No value, only compensation for the pregnancy loss
D) The value at the time of death

Key Takeaway
The usurper's liability for defects caused during his possession persists even after valid return, as per Abu Hanifa, because the death was a direct consequence of his own act (pregnancy).

Dispute on Liability of Usurper for Slave-Girl Dying in Postpartum
Intra-Hanafi dispute on guarantor liability for returned slave-girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on usurper liability and distinguish between the proofs of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The validity of the return determines liability: a returned defective item does not discharge the usurper if the defect existed at return.

In this passage, we examine a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of a usurper who returns a slave-girl after causing her pregnancy. The disagreement centers on whether the return was valid given the defect (pregnancy) caused by the usurper. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the principle that a return must put the property back in the same condition as when taken.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa)
What is the ruling according to Abu Hanifa? He holds the usurper liable for the full value of the slave-girl on the day she became pregnant because the return is invalid due to the pre-existing cause of death.
The key is that the defect (pregnancy) existed at the time of return.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's opposing view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the usurper is not liable for the full value, only for the defect. They argue the return is valid because the cause of death (childbirth) arose in the owner's possession.
They analogize to fever and zina cases where the cause arose after return.
3
Follow the Sahibayn's proof and analogies
The Sahibayn cite three analogies: (1) slave-girl with fever returned and dies, (2) slave-girl who committed zina returned and flogged to death, (3) purchased slave-girl pregnant before sale dies in postpartum. In all, the usurper/buyer is not liable because the cause of death occurred after return/delivery.
These analogies rely on the cause of death being in the owner's possession.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response and distinction
Abu Hanifa distinguishes: in the analogies, the cause of death (fever, flogging) did not exist at the time of return, but here pregnancy (the cause) did exist. Therefore the return is invalid, and the usurper remains liable as if no return occurred.
He further analogizes to a slave-girl who commits a crime in the usurper's hand and is killed in the owner's hand: the usurper pays full value.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the usurper pays full value of the slave-girl. Under the Sahibayn, only compensation for the defect (pregnancy). Later Hanafi practice often follows the Sahibayn.
The text notes a contradiction in Hidayah regarding whether childbirth is a cause of death, indicating ongoing scholarly consideration.

امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل
وله انه غصبها وما انعقد فيها سبب التلف ورُدَّت وفيها ذلك فلم يوجد الرد على الوجه الذى اخذه فلم يصح الرد وصار كما اذا جنت فى يد الغاصب جناية فقتلت بها فى يد المالک او دفعت بها بان كانت الجناية خطأ يرجع على الغاصب بكل القيمة، كذا هذا بخلاف الحرة لانها لا تضمن بالغصب ليبقى ضمان الغصب بعد فساد الردّ وفى فصل الشراء الواجب ابتداء التسليم وما ذكرناه شرط صحة الرد والزناء سبب لجلد مولم لا جارح ولا متلف فلم يوجد السبب في يد الغاصب
توضیح اللغة تلف (س) تلفاً ہلاک ہونا، برباد ہونا ، جنت (ض) جنایہ گناہ کرنا، جرم کرنا ، جلد کوڑے مارنا۔ مولم دردناک۔ جارح زخمی کرنے والا ۔ متلف مہلک ۔
ترجمہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے ایسی حالت میں غصب کیا کہ باندی میں سبب تلف موجود نہیں تھا اور وہ ایسی حالت میں واپس کی گئی کہ اس میں سبب تلف موجود ہے تو واپسی اس طور پر نہیں ہوئی جس طور پر اس نے لی تھی پس واپسی صحیح نہ ہوئی اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے باندی نے غاصب کے قبضہ میں کوئی جرم کیا اور مالک کے قبضہ میں قتل کی گئی یا وہ اس جرم کے عوض میں دے دی گئی ۔ بایں طور کہ جرم خطاء تھا تو وہ غاصب سے پوری قیمت واپس لیتا ہے۔ ایسے ہی یہاں ہے بخلاف حرہ کے ۔ کیونکہ حرہ مخصب سے مضمون نہیں ہوتی ۔ یہاں تک کہ واپسی فاسد ہونے کے بعد بھی غصب کا تاوان باقی رہے اور خرید کے مسئلہ میں ابتداء سپرد کرنا واجب ہے اور جو ہم نے یہاں ذکر کیا وہ واپسی سیح ہونے کی شرط ہے۔ اور زنا ایسی ضرب کا سبب ہے جو دکھ پہنچانے والی ہو نہ آنکہ زخمی یا تلف کنندہ ہو۔ پس غاصب کے قبضہ میں سبب نہیں یا یا گیا۔
تشريح ... قوله وله انه غصبها ... الخ - امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب غاصب نے باندی غصب کی تھی اس وقت اس میں تلف ہونے کا کوئی سبب نہیں تھا۔ اور جب اس نے واپس کی ہے اس وقت اس میں سبب تلف یعنی حمل موجود ہے تو واپسی صحیح نہ ہوئی اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے باندی نے غاصب کے قبضہ میں کوئی جرم (قتل) کیا پھر اسی جرم کی وجہ سے وہ مالک کے قبضہ میں قتل کی گئی یا اگر اس کا جرم خطاء تھا تو اس کے عوض میں باندی دے دی گئی تو وہ غاصب سے پوری قیمت واپس لیتا ہے۔ پس ایسے ہی زیر بحث مسئلہ میں ہوگا۔ بخلاف آزاد عورت کے کہ آزاد عورت غصب سے مضمون نہیں ہوتی ( کیونکہ وہ مال نہیں ہے ) یہاں تک کہ واپسی فاسد ہونے کے بعد بھی غصب کا تاوان باقی رہے۔
Book of Ghasp, Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume 12. [Arabic matn:] The hand of the owner is childbirth, so the usurper is not liable, just as if she suffered fever in the usurper's hand then he returned her and she died, or she committed zina in his hand then he returned her and she was flogged and died from it, and like one who bought a slave-girl who had become pregnant in the seller's hand, she gave birth at the buyer's and died in her postpartum, he does not seek return of the price from the seller by agreement. [Urdu translation:] Someone usurped a slave-girl and committed zina with her, and she became pregnant, then he returned her, and she died in her postpartum; then the usurper is guarantor for that value which was on the day she became pregnant. In the case of a free woman, he is not liable. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say that even in the case of a slave-girl he will not be liable. Their proof is that the return is valid, and death occurred after due to a cause that arose in the owner's possession, which is childbirth. So the usurper is not liable, just as if the slave-girl suffered fever in the usurper's hand then he returned her and she died, or the slave-girl committed zina in the usurper's hand and he returned her and then she was flogged and died from it, or one bought a slave-girl who had become pregnant in the seller's hand, she gave birth at the buyer's and died in postpartum, then by agreement he cannot claim the price from the seller. [Commentary:] Explanation of the statement 'and whoever usurps a slave-girl...': The usurper committed zina with the usurped slave-girl willingly or unwillingly, then returned her in a state of pregnancy. The slave-girl came to the owner and died in postpartum. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the usurper is liable for the value of the slave-girl on the day she became pregnant. If the usurper committed zina with a free woman and returned her in pregnancy and she died in postpartum, he is not liable. According to the two companions and the three imams, even in the case of a slave-girl he is not liable (however he is liable for the injury to the pregnancy). Their proof is that the cause of death is childbirth which occurred in the owner's possession. So the return was valid because he delivered her right to the one entitled, and delivery of right causes release from liability (only that he made her defective, so he will pay compensation for the defect). Then they analogized this to several cases: 1. If the slave-girl suffered fever at the usurper's, then he returned her and she died at the owner's, he is not liable. 2. The slave-girl committed zina in the usurper's hand, then he returned her and she was flogged for zina at the owner's and died, the usurper is not liable. 3. Someone bought a slave-girl who had become pregnant in the seller's hand, then she gave birth at the buyer's and died in postpartum, he cannot get the price back from the seller by agreement. It should be noted that the restriction 'and she died in her postpartum' is because if her death occurred due to childbirth, then by agreement he would be liable. Warning: The author of Hidayah presented this proof from the two companions, and upon it there is an objection that earlier he stated on page 368 that childbirth is not a cause of death, he said: 'and the second issue is that childbirth is not a cause of death of the mother, for it is not decreed by Allah predominantly', and here he made childbirth a cause of death. So there is contradiction. Let one reflect on the resolution. [Abu Hanifa's proof:] Arabic: And his proof is that he usurped her and there was no cause of death in her at that time, and she was returned while it was in her, so the return was not done in the manner in which he took her, so the return became invalid, and it became like if she committed a crime in the usurper's hand and was killed for it in the owner's hand, or if she was given in exchange for a crime that was unintentional, then he recovers full value from the usurper; similarly here. In contrast to a free woman, because she is not guaranteed by usurpation, so the guarantee of ghasp remains after the invalidity of return. In the chapter of purchase, the beginning of delivery is obligatory, and what we mentioned is a condition of valid return. And zina is a cause for a painful flogging, not injuring or causing death, so the cause did not exist in the usurper's hand. [Urdu translation of proof:] Abu Hanifa's proof is that he usurped her in a state where there was no cause of death in the slave-girl, and she was returned in a state where the cause of death existed, so the return did not happen in the way he took her, so the return is invalid. This is like if a slave-girl committed a crime in the usurper's hand and was killed for it in the owner's hand, or if the crime was unintentional and she was given as compensation, then the full price is taken from the usurper. Similarly here. In contrast to a free woman, because a free woman is not guaranteed by usurpation, so the guarantee of ghasp remains even after the return becomes invalid. In the purchase case, initial delivery is obligatory, and what we mentioned is a condition of valid return. And zina is a cause for a painful flogging, not for injury or death, so the cause did not exist in the usurper's hand. [Commentary:] Explanation of his statement 'and his proof is that he usurped her...': Abu Hanifa's proof is that when the usurper usurped the slave-girl, at that time there was no cause of death in her. And when he returned her, at that time the cause of death, i.e., pregnancy, existed, so the return was not valid. It became like if the slave-girl committed a crime (murder) in the usurper's hand, then she was killed for that crime in the owner's hand, or if the crime was unintentional and the slave-girl was given as compensation, then he takes full value from the usurper. So similarly in the issue under discussion. In contrast to a free woman, because a free woman is not guaranteed by usurpation (as she is not property), so the guarantee of ghasp remains even after the return becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of a usurper (ghasib) for a slave-girl he misappropriated, committed zina with, causing pregnancy, then returned to the owner, after which she died in postpartum. The core issue is whether the return of the slave-girl is valid, thus transferring liability to the owner, or invalid due to the defect (pregnancy) caused by the usurper, making him liable. The passage opens with the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: the usurper is liable for the value of the slave-girl on the day she became pregnant. In the case of a free woman, he is not liable because free persons are not subject to ghasp. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree and hold the usurper not liable even for a slave-girl, because the return was valid since the cause of death (childbirth) arose in the owner's possession. They support their view by analogies to cases where a slave-girl suffers fever or commits zina at the usurper's, then is returned and later dies in the owner's possession – in all such cases the usurper is not liable. Similarly, by analogy to a purchase case where a slave-girl becomes pregnant before sale and dies after delivery; the buyer cannot claim the price back by consensus. The commentary then notes a caution from the author of Hidayah that the Sahibayn's proof appears contradictory to an earlier statement that childbirth is not a cause of death. The passage then presents Imam Abu Hanifa's proof. He argues that the usurper took the slave-girl without any cause of death, but returned her with a cause of death (pregnancy). Therefore the return is not valid because it was not in the same condition as when taken. This is analogous to a case where a slave-girl commits a crime in the usurper's hand and is killed for it in the owner's hand – then the usurper must pay full value. The key distinction for Abu Hanifa is that the pregnancy was caused by the usurper's action and existed at the time of return, invalidating the return. For a free woman, no liability arises because free persons are not guaranteed. The passage ends with the reason that zina is only a cause for a painful flogging, not for death, so the cause did not originate in the usurper's hand. This is a classic example of qiyas (analogy) in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasp): Usurpation – taking another's property without right, with the intention of ownership or control.
غاصب (ghasib): The usurper – one who commits ghasp.
حمل (haml): Pregnancy – the condition of being with child.
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum period – bleeding after childbirth.
ضمان (daman): Liability, guarantee – the obligation to compensate for loss or damage.
صاحبین (sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is the return of the slave-girl invalid?
A) Because the usurper committed zina, which is a sin.
B) Because the cause of death (pregnancy) existed at the time of return.
C) Because the slave-girl died in the owner's possession.
D) Because the owner did not accept the return.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a return in ghasp depends on whether the cause of loss existed at the time of return, a point of ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

advanced
8 min
Liability for Usurped Slave Girl Dying in Postpartum: Abu Hanifa's Proof
Imam Abu Hanifa's proof and rebuttals in an intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's position on the validity of return in usurpation, explain his analogical proof and distinctions, and evaluate the Sahibayn's counter-arguments.

Core Idea
A usurped object must be returned in the same condition as taken; any change invalidates the return and maintains liability.

This lesson dives into an intra-Hanafi dispute over the liability of a usurper who returns a pregnant slave girl who later dies in childbirth. Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the return was invalid due to a change in condition, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that the physical return ends liability. You will examine Abu Hanifa's analogical proof and his responses to the Sahibayn's qiyas, sharpening your ability to distinguish valid from invalid return in ghasb cases.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the usurper remains liable for the full value because the return was invalid. The slave girl was taken without the cause of destruction (pregnancy) and returned with it, so the condition changed.
The key is that the attribute (pregnancy) was not present at the time of usurpation.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's opposition
The Sahibayn argue that the physical return of the slave girl extinguishes liability, regardless of the pregnancy. They support this with two qiyas: the purchase case and the zina case.
Their qiyas aims to show that later-added attributes do not affect the validity of delivery.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's analogical proof
Abu Hanifa draws an analogy: if a slave girl commits a crime in the usurper's hand and is then killed in the owner's hand, the usurper pays full value. Similarly, here the cause of destruction (pregnancy) developed during usurpation, so the return is invalid.
The 'illa is the existence of a cause of destruction that was not present at the time of taking.
4
Evaluate the response to the purchase qiyas
Abu Hanifa distinguishes purchase from usurpation: in sale, delivery is of the specific object regardless of attributes; in usurpation, the return must undo the wrongful act in the exact condition it was taken.
Attributes are part of the ghasb obligation, but not part of the sale contract.
5
Evaluate the response to the zina qiyas
Abu Hanifa argues that the prescribed flogging for zina is only painful, not destructive. The flogging that caused death was not the prescribed punishment, so the cause of death was not present in the usurper's hand.
This breaks the analogy because the zina case involves a non-destructive cause, whereas pregnancy is inherently destructive.

امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل
وله انه غصبها وما انعقد فيها سبب التلف ورُدَّت وفيها ذلك فلم يوجد الرد على الوجه الذى اخذه فلم يصح الرد وصار كما اذا جنت فى يد الغاصب جناية فقتلت بها فى يد المالک او دفعت بها بان كانت الجناية خطأ يرجع على الغاصب بكل القيمة، كذا هذا بخلاف الحرة لانها لا تضمن بالغصب ليبقى ضمان الغصب بعد فساد الردّ وفى فصل الشراء الواجب ابتداء التسليم وما ذكرناه شرط صحة الرد والزناء سبب لجلد مولم لا جارح ولا متلف فلم يوجد السبب في يد الغاصب
توضیح اللغة تلف (س) تلفاً ہلاک ہونا، برباد ہونا ، جنت (ض) جنایہ گناہ کرنا، جرم کرنا ، جلد کوڑے مارنا۔ مولم دردناک۔ جارح زخمی کرنے والا ۔ متلف مہلک ۔
ترجمہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس نے ایسی حالت میں غصب کیا کہ باندی میں سبب تلف موجود نہیں تھا اور وہ ایسی حالت میں واپس کی گئی کہ اس میں سبب تلف موجود ہے تو واپسی اس طور پر نہیں ہوئی جس طور پر اس نے لی تھی پس واپسی صحیح نہ ہوئی اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے باندی نے غاصب کے قبضہ میں کوئی جرم کیا اور مالک کے قبضہ میں قتل کی گئی یا وہ اس جرم کے عوض میں دے دی گئی ۔ بایں طور کہ جرم خطاء تھا تو وہ غاصب سے پوری قیمت واپس لیتا ہے۔ ایسے ہی یہاں ہے بخلاف حرہ کے ۔ کیونکہ حرہ مخصب سے مضمون نہیں ہوتی ۔ یہاں تک کہ واپسی فاسد ہونے کے بعد بھی غصب کا تاوان باقی رہے اور خرید کے مسئلہ میں ابتداء سپرد کرنا واجب ہے اور جو ہم نے یہاں ذکر کیا وہ واپسی سیح ہونے کی شرط ہے۔ اور زنا ایسی ضرب کا سبب ہے جو دکھ پہنچانے والی ہو نہ آنکہ زخمی یا تلف کنندہ ہو۔ پس غاصب کے قبضہ میں سبب نہیں یا یا گیا۔
تشريح ... قوله وله انه غصبها ... الخ - امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب غاصب نے باندی غصب کی تھی اس وقت اس میں تلف ہونے کا کوئی سبب نہیں تھا۔ اور جب اس نے واپس کی ہے اس وقت اس میں سبب تلف یعنی حمل موجود ہے تو واپسی صحیح نہ ہوئی اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے باندی نے غاصب کے قبضہ میں کوئی جرم (قتل) کیا پھر اسی جرم کی وجہ سے وہ مالک کے قبضہ میں قتل کی گئی یا اگر اس کا جرم خطاء تھا تو اس کے عوض میں باندی دے دی گئی تو وہ غاصب سے پوری قیمت واپس لیتا ہے۔ پس ایسے ہی زیر بحث مسئلہ میں ہوگا۔ بخلاف آزاد عورت کے کہ آزاد عورت غصب سے مضمون نہیں ہوتی ( کیونکہ وہ مال نہیں ہے ) یہاں تک کہ واپسی فاسد ہونے کے بعد بھی غصب کا تاوان باقی رہے۔ قوله وفي فصل الشراء.. الخ - صاحبین کے قیاسیات ثالث کا جواب ہے قیاس سوم یعنی صاحبین کے قول و کمن اشترى جارية قد حبلت في يد البائع یہ قول کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اول تو ہمارے بعض مشائخ نے اس کو تسلیم نہیں کیا بلکہ یہ کہا ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک وہ پوراشن واپس لے گا اور بعض دیگر مشائخ نے گوحکم مذکور تسلیم کیا ہے تاہم انہوں نے مسئلہ غصب اور مسئلہ شراء میں فرق کیا ہے ۔ وہ یہ کہ فصل شراء میں بائع پر واپسی واجب نہیں بلکہ اس پر تسلیم ( سپرد کرنا ) واجب ہے کہ ابتداء مبیع کو اسی طریقہ پر سپر د کرتا ہے جس طور پر عقد واقع ہوا ہے اور یہ بات اس کی طرف سے پائی گئی اسلئے کہ عقد عین شی ، پر واقع ہوتا ہے نہ کہ اوصاف پر ۔ اس لئے اوصاف کے مقابلہ میں کچھ نہیں ہوتا اور باندی کے نفاس میں مر جانے سے تسلیم معدوم نہیں ہوئی ۔
بخلاف غاصب کے کہ اس کے ذمہ اپنے فعل کو فسخ کرنا واجب ہے اور یہ اسی وقت ہوگا جب وہ اسی حالت میں واپس کرے جس حالت پر قبضہ کیا تھا کیونکہ غصب میں اوصاف بھی داخل ہیں۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر فربہ باندی غصب کی اور وہ غاصب کے پاس کمزور ہوگئی اور اس کو کمزوری کی حالت میں واپس کیا تو وہ نقصان کا ضامن ہوتا ہے۔ جب اوصاف داخل غصب ہوئے تو بلا اوصاف واپس کرنا فاسد واپسی ہوئی حالانکہ ہم نے جو ذ کر کیا ہے کہ واپسی اسی طریقہ پر ہو جس طریقہ پر اس نے باندی کو لیا تھا یہ صحت واپسی کیلئے شرط ہے اور ایسی واپسی یہاں نہیں پائی گئی اسلئے کہ جب اس نے باندی غصب کی تھی اس وقت اس میں سبب تلف ( حمل ) نہیں تھا اور جب اس نے واپس کی ہے اس وقت اس میں یہ سبب موجود ہے۔
قوله والزناء سبب ..... الخ - قیاس دوم یعنی صاحبین کے قول اوزنت فی یدہ اھ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جوز نا غاصب کے قبضہ میں پایا گیا وہ ایسی ضرب کا موجب ہے جو صرف مولم ہو (یعنی دکھ پہنچائے ) نہ یہ کہ جارح اور مختلف ہو کر ہلاک کر ڈالے اسی لئے ایسا کوڑا اختیار کیا جاتا ہے جس میں گانٹھ نہ ہو اور جب اس کو مالک کے قبضہ میں ایسی مارلگائی گئی جس کی وجہ سے وہ ہلاک ہو گئی تو یہ اس کے موجب کے علاوہ ہوئی جو غاصب کے قبضہ میں واجب ہوا تھا۔ پس تلف کا سبب غاصب کے قبضہ میں نہیں پایا گیا۔ لہذا ضامین نہ ہوگا
Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence: He said: He usurped her while there was no cause of destruction within her, and she was returned with that cause, so the return did not occur in the manner in which he took her, so the return is invalid, and it is as if she committed a crime in the usurper's hand and was killed for it in the owner's hand, or was handed over as compensation, if the crime was unintentional, he pays the full value to the usurper. Similarly here, unlike the free woman because she is not guaranteed by usurpation, so the guarantee of usurpation remains after the return becomes invalid. In the chapter of purchase, initial delivery is obligatory, and what we mentioned is a condition for the validity of return. And fornication is a cause for painful flogging, not for wounding or destruction, so the cause was not found in the usurper's hand. (Urdu translation and commentary: The proof is that when he usurped the slave girl, there was no cause of destruction; when he returned her, the cause (pregnancy) existed, so the return was invalid. This is like a slave girl who committed a crime in the usurper's hand and was killed in the owner's hand, or was given as compensation. Unlike a free woman. The purchase case is distinguished because in sale, delivery is of the specific item not attributes; in usurpation, the return must be in the same condition. Regarding the zina qiyas: the prescribed flogging is only painful, not destructive, so the cause of death was not present at the usurper's hand.)
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the liability of a usurper who returns a pregnant slave girl who then dies in postpartum. Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the return was invalid because the condition of the object changed (the pregnancy developed during the usurpation), so the usurper remains liable for the value. He supports this with an analogy: if a slave girl commits a crime in the usurper's hand and is subsequently killed or handed over as compensation in the owner's hand, the usurper bears the loss. He distinguishes the case of a free woman (who is not a commodity) and the case of a purchase (where delivery is of the specific item, not its attributes). He also refutes the Sahibayn's qiyas based on zina (fornication) by arguing that the prescribed punishment is only painful, not destructive, so the cause of death was not present in the usurper's hand. The commentary explains each point clearly, following the author's order.

Key Terms
سبب التلف (sabab al-talaf): The cause of destruction, here referring to the pregnancy of the slave girl which leads to childbirth and potential death.
رد (radd): Return of the usurped object to its owner.
غصب (ghasb): Unlawful seizure and possession of someone else's property without right.
مولم (mu'lim): Painful, causing pain but not injury or destruction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa's position in this passage, under what condition is the return of a usurped object considered valid?
A) The object is returned in the same condition as when it was taken, including all attributes.
B) The object is returned in a better condition than when taken.
C) The object is returned at all, regardless of condition.
D) The object is returned with a decrease in value compensated.

Key Takeaway
A usurper must return the object in the exact condition it was taken; otherwise, liability persists.

Usurper's Liability for Usufruct: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i and Maliki
States Hanafi ruling on non-liability for benefits and refutes opposing schools

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a usurper's liability for usufruct, explain the proofs of Hanafi and opposing schools, and evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the three positions.

Core Idea
Benefits are accidents (a'rad) created in the usurper's possession, so he is not liable for them unless the property depreciates.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute: is a usurper liable for the usufruct (benefits) of the property he took? The Hanafi school's answer is no—unless the property's value decreased due to use. The Shafi'i and Maliki schools disagree. Let's examine the proofs and the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the usurper is not liable for the benefits themselves, but if the property decreases in value due to use, he must pay that decrease.
This distinguishes between the benefit (usufruct) and the physical depreciation.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their positions
Shafi'i holds liability for full rental value whether used or idle; Maliki holds liability only if inhabited.
Note the difference between unconditional liability (Shafi'i) and conditional liability (Maliki).
3
Examine the opponent's proof
The opponent (Shafi'i and Maliki) argue that benefits are valuable property (mutaqawwim) and are guaranteed in contracts, so by analogy they are guaranteed in usurpation.
This is a qiyas to lawful contracts.
4
Analyse the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response is that benefits are accidents (a'rad) that come into being in the usurper's hand; they did not exist in the owner's possession, so they are not property that was taken.
The key distinction: benefits are not existing at the time of usurpation; they are created anew.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi pays only depreciation, Shafi'i pays full rental value, Maliki pays rental value only if he used the property.
This affects real-world compensation calculations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غاصب منافع مغصوب کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا
قال ولا يضمن الغاصب منافع ما غصبه الا ان ينقص باستعماله فيغرم النقصان، وقال الشافعي يضمنها فيجب اجر المثل، ولا فرق فى المذهبين بينما اذا عطلها او سكنها ، وقال مالك ان سکنها يجب اجر المثل وان عطّلها لا شيء عليه له ان المنافع اموال متقومة حتى تضمن بالعقود فكذا بالغصوب، لنا انها حصلت على ملك الغاصب لحدوثها في امكانها اذ هى لم تكن حادثة في يد المالك لانها اعراض لا . وبخلاف الحمى فان الهلاك لم يكن بالسبب الذى كان عند الغاصب بل الضعف الطبيعة عن دفع آثار الحمى المتوالية واذا لا يحصل باوّل الحمى عند الغاصب وهي غير موجبة لما كان بعده اما الحمل فيوجب انفصال الولد وانفصال الولد يوجب للام الولادة فما يحدث به يكون مضافاً إلى السبب الاول ١٣ كفايه
The usurper is not liable for the benefits of what he usurped unless there is a decrease due to use, then he pays the decrease. Al-Shafi'i said he is liable and must pay the rental value. There is no difference in the two schools between if he left it idle or inhabited it. Malik said if he inhabited it, he must pay the rental value; if he left it idle, nothing on him. Their evidence: Benefits are valuable properties, so they are guaranteed by contracts, similarly by usurpation. Our evidence: They come into being in the usurper's ownership because they occur in his possession, as they were not occurring in the owner's hand because they are accidents that do not persist. And unlike fever, because destruction was not by the cause that was with the usurper, but natural weakness to repel successive effects of fever, and if the first fever does not occur with the usurper and it does not necessitate what came after it. As for pregnancy, it necessitates the delivery of the child and the delivery necessitates postpartum, so what happens due to it is attributed to the first cause. (Kifaya 13)
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage presents a three-way inter-madhhab dispute regarding the liability of a usurper for the usufruct (benefits) of the usurped property. The Hanafi school holds that the usurper is not liable for the benefits (e.g., rental value) unless the property actually depreciates in value due to use, in which case he pays only the decrease. Al-Shafi'i holds that the usurper is liable for the full rental value of the benefits, whether he used the property or left it idle. Imam Malik makes a distinction: if the usurper inhabited the property, he owes the rental value; if he left it idle, nothing is due. The Hanafi proof is that benefits are not independently existing property; they are accidents (a'rad) that come into being only in the hands of the person in possession. Therefore, they are not owned by the original owner at the time of usurpation. The text then offers a distinction regarding fever: the fever itself is not a cause of death; rather, death results from the weakness of the body to resist successive fevers, which is not attributable to the original fever that occurred in the usurper's possession. This contrasts with pregnancy, where the initial cause (pregnancy) necessarily leads to childbirth and postpartum, so subsequent events are attributed to that cause.

Key Terms
منافع (manafi): Benefits/usufruct, the usufruct or use value of a property.
أعراض (a'rad): Accidents; non-permanent attributes that do not persist over time.
متقوم (mutaqawwim): Valuable property that is legally recognized and compensable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, when is a usurper liable to pay compensation for the use of a usurped property?
A) He is always liable for the rental value of the property.
B) He is only liable if the property has decreased in value due to his use.
C) He is liable only if he inhabited the property.
D) He is never liable under any circumstances.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between physical depreciation and use value; only actual loss to the owner's property is compensable, not hypothetical rental value.

Liability in Usurpation vs Purchase: Rebutting the Sahibayn's Qiyas
Commentator rebuts Sahibayn's analogy between purchase and usurpation regarding return of a pregnant slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school distinguishes liability in usurpation from sale regarding the return of a pregnant slave who dies in childbirth.

Core Idea
Attributes like pregnancy are compensable in usurpation but not in sale because the legal obligations differ.

This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The Sahibayn analogize the return of a pregnant slave in usurpation to a sale, arguing that if a seller is not liable for a slave who dies after delivery, a usurper should similarly be absolved. The commentator explains why this analogy fails: sale only requires delivering the specific item ('ayn'), while usurpation requires restoring the exact state including attributes, because the usurper must undo his wrongful act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
State the two positions: Abu Hanifa holds the usurper liable; the Sahibayn analogize to purchase where the seller is not liable.
The Sahibayn's position is based on qiyas (analogy).
2
Understand the Sahibayn's qiyas
The Sahibayn compare the usurper's return to a seller's delivery: if a seller is not liable when a pregnant slave dies after delivery, the usurper should not be liable either.
Their argument assumes the legal effect of return/delivery is the same in both contexts.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The commentator distinguishes the two cases: in sale, the obligation is delivery (taslim) of the specific thing, not its attributes; in usurpation, the obligation is to undo the wrong (naqd al-fil) by returning the property in the exact state as taken, including attributes.
This is why returning a pregnant slave with the pregnancy is defective under usurpation but valid under sale.
4
Apply to the second qiyas
The second analogy involves a slave who commits zina in the usurper's possession and later dies from lashing after return. The commentator argues that the lashing prescribed for zina is not intended to kill, so the death is caused by the owner's excessive blow, not the usurper's act.
This further illustrates that causation determines liability.
5
Derive the practical consequence
Conclude that under Hanafi law, a usurper remains liable for the value of the slave if he returns her with a latent defect (like pregnancy) that causes death. In contrast, a seller is not liable for such defects after delivery.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference).

کا تاوان باقی رہے۔ قوله وفي فصل الشراء.. الخ - صاحبین کے قیاسیات ثالث کا جواب ہے قیاس سوم یعنی صاحبین کے قول و کمن اشترى جارية قد حبلت في يد البائع یہ قول کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اول تو ہمارے بعض مشائخ نے اس کو تسلیم نہیں کیا بلکہ یہ کہا ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک وہ پوراشن واپس لے گا اور بعض دیگر مشائخ نے گوحکم مذکور تسلیم کیا ہے تاہم انہوں نے مسئلہ غصب اور مسئلہ شراء میں فرق کیا ہے ۔ وہ یہ کہ فصل شراء میں بائع پر واپسی واجب نہیں بلکہ اس پر تسلیم ( سپرد کرنا ) واجب ہے کہ ابتداء مبیع کو اسی طریقہ پر سپر د کرتا ہے جس طور پر عقد واقع ہوا ہے اور یہ بات اس کی طرف سے پائی گئی اسلئے کہ عقد عین شی ، پر واقع ہوتا ہے نہ کہ اوصاف پر ۔ اس لئے اوصاف کے مقابلہ میں کچھ نہیں ہوتا اور باندی کے نفاس میں مر جانے سے تسلیم معدوم نہیں ہوئی ۔
بخلاف غاصب کے کہ اس کے ذمہ اپنے فعل کو فسخ کرنا واجب ہے اور یہ اسی وقت ہوگا جب وہ اسی حالت میں واپس کرے جس حالت پر قبضہ کیا تھا کیونکہ غصب میں اوصاف بھی داخل ہیں۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر فربہ باندی غصب کی اور وہ غاصب کے پاس کمزور ہوگئی اور اس کو کمزوری کی حالت میں واپس کیا تو وہ نقصان کا ضامن ہوتا ہے۔ جب اوصاف داخل غصب ہوئے تو بلا اوصاف واپس کرنا فاسد واپسی ہوئی حالانکہ ہم نے جو ذ کر کیا ہے کہ واپسی اسی طریقہ پر ہو جس طریقہ پر اس نے باندی کو لیا تھا یہ صحت واپسی کیلئے شرط ہے اور ایسی واپسی یہاں نہیں پائی گئی اسلئے کہ جب اس نے باندی غصب کی تھی اس وقت اس میں سبب تلف ( حمل ) نہیں تھا اور جب اس نے واپس کی ہے اس وقت اس میں یہ سبب موجود ہے۔
قوله والزناء سبب ..... الخ - قیاس دوم یعنی صاحبین کے قول اوزنت فی یدہ اھ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جوز نا غاصب کے قبضہ میں پایا گیا وہ ایسی ضرب کا موجب ہے جو صرف مولم ہو (یعنی دکھ پہنچائے ) نہ یہ کہ جارح اور مختلف ہو کر ہلاک کر ڈالے اسی لئے ایسا کوڑا اختیار کیا جاتا ہے جس میں گانٹھ نہ ہو اور جب اس کو مالک کے قبضہ میں ایسی مارلگائی گئی جس کی وجہ سے وہ ہلاک ہو گئی تو یہ اس کے موجب کے علاوہ ہوئی جو غاصب کے قبضہ میں واجب ہوا تھا۔ پس تلف کا سبب غاصب کے قبضہ میں نہیں پایا گیا۔ لہذا ضامین نہ ہوگا ۔
...remains as compensation. [Commentary on] his saying 'And in the chapter of purchase...' etc. - This is the response to the third analogy of the Sahibayn. The third analogy is the statement of the Sahibayn: 'And if someone purchases a slave girl who is pregnant in the hand of the seller.' The response to this statement is that, firstly, some of our shaykhs did not accept it; rather, they said that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, he will take back the full price. And some other shaykhs accepted the mentioned ruling; nevertheless, they distinguished between the case of usurpation and the case of purchase. That is, in the chapter of purchase, the seller is not obliged to take back (the slave); rather, he is obliged to deliver (taslim) because initially he delivers the sold item in the same manner in which the contract was made, and this (delivery) was found from his side because the contract pertains to the specific thing itself, not to attributes. Therefore, nothing is (compensated) for attributes, and the delivery is not nullified by the slave dying in childbirth.
Unlike the usurper, for whom it is obligatory to undo his own act, and that will only happen when he returns (the property) in the same state in which he took possession, because in usurpation, attributes are also included. This is why if a fat slave girl is usurped and she becomes thin with the usurper, and he returns her in a thin state, he is liable for the loss. When attributes are included in usurpation, returning without attributes is a defective return, while what we mentioned — that the return must be in the same manner in which he took the slave — is a condition for the validity of the return, and such a return is not found here because when he usurped the slave, there was no cause of destruction (pregnancy) in her, and when he returned her, this cause was present.
[Commentary on] his saying 'And zina is a cause...' etc. - This is the response to the second analogy, i.e., the statement of the Sahibayn: 'And she committed zina in his hand.' The response is that the zina that occurred in the usurper's possession is a cause for a lashing that is merely painful, not one that is injurious and causes death. That is why a whip without knots is chosen. When the owner struck her such a blow that caused her death, this was beyond what was required from the usurper's possession. Therefore, the cause of destruction was not found in the usurper's possession; thus, he will not be liable.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute where the commentator responds to two qiyas (analogies) of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) against Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling. The issue is whether a usurper is liable for the loss of a pregnant slave who dies after being returned. The Sahibayn analogized to a purchase case where a pregnant slave is sold and dies; in purchase, the seller is not liable for the loss. The commentator explains that some Hanafi shaykhs did not accept the analogy, while others accepted it but distinguished: in purchase, the seller's obligation is merely to deliver the specific thing (ayn), not its attributes; thus, if the slave dies in childbirth after delivery, the seller is not liable. In usurpation, however, the usurper must return the property in the exact condition (including attributes) as taken; if he returns her pregnant and she dies, the return is defective because the cause of death (pregnancy) existed at the time of return, so he remains liable. The second qiyas involves a slave who commits zina and is lashed to death after return. The commentator argues that the lashing prescribed for zina is not meant to kill, and the death occurred due to the owner's excessive blow, not the usurper's act, so the usurper is not liable. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that the usurper's liability is determined by the state of the property at the time of return and the causation of loss.

Key Terms
غصب (ghaṣb): Unlawful taking and possession of another's property without consent, entailing liability for return and compensation.
تسلیم (taslīm): Delivery of a sold item to the buyer; in purchase, it does not require returning attributes.
اوصاف (awṣāf): Attributes or qualities of a property; in usurpation, they are included in the liability for return.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn, why is a seller in a purchase case not liable if a pregnant slave dies after delivery, while a usurper is liable?
A) Because in purchase, the seller only guarantees the price, not the slave.
B) Because purchase contracts transfer ownership completely, while usurpation does not.
C) Because in purchase, the seller's obligation is to deliver the specific thing (ayn), not its attributes; in usurpation, the usurper must return the property exactly as taken, including attributes.
D) Because the Sahibayn's analogy is based on a weak hadith.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the liability for return in usurpation includes attributes, whereas in sale only the specific object is owed—this distinction explains why a usurper remains liable for a pregnant slave who dies after return.

Usurper Not Liable for Benefits: Hanafi Position with Shafi'i and Maliki Views
Matn states ruling; commentator expands on inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on usurper liability for benefits, explain the Hanafi proof based on benefits as accidents, and evaluate the Shafi'i and Maliki counter-arguments.

Core Idea
Benefits are accidents that vanish; you cannot usurp what does not exist in the owner's hand.

The question of whether a usurper must pay for using someone else's property without permission may seem straightforward, but classical jurists differed sharply. The Hanafi school holds that benefits (manafi') are not compensable in tort because they are transitory accidents that cannot be independently possessed. This lesson unpacks the inter-madhhab dispute, the underlying proofs, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the exact ruling from the matn: the usurper is not liable for benefits unless the property physically decreases.
The exception for physical decrease shows the Hanafi emphasis on tangible harm.
2
Identify the opposing positions
Note the Shafi'i position (liable for market rent regardless of use) and the Maliki position (liable only if used).
The Maliki position is a middle ground.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i proof
Examine the argument that benefits are valuable property (amwal mutaqawwima) and thus should be compensated in tort as in contract.
This analogizes ghasb to lease.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Understand that benefits are accidents (a'rad) that come into existence in the usurper's possession; they did not exist in the owner's hand. The usurper owns them by necessity, and one is not liable for one's own property.
Emphasize ontological difference between benefits and physical objects.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario: usurper lives in a house for a month without damage. Hanafi: no rent; Shafi'i: rent due; Maliki: rent due if used.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

غاصب منافع مغصوب کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا
