ترجمہ اور ضامن نہیں ہوتا غاصب اس چیز کے منافع کا جس کو اس نے غصب کیا ہے الا یہ کہ ناقص ہو جائے اس کے استعمال سے ، پس وہ نقصان کا تاوان دے گا ۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ منافع کا ضامن ہو گا ۔ پس اجر مثل واجب ہو گا اور دونوں مذہبوں میں اس کا فرق نہیں کہ غاصب نے اس کو بے کار چھوڑا ہو یا اس کو سکونت میں استعمال کیا ہو ۔ امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر غاصب اس میں رہا ہو تو اجر مثل واجب ہوگا اور اگر بیکار چھوڑا ہو تو اس پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منافع بھی قیمتی مال ہیں ۔ یہاں تک کہ عقود سے ان کی ضمانت واجب ہوتی ہے تو ایسے ہی غصوب سے بھی واجب ہوگی ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ منافع ملک غاصب پر حاصل ہوئے ہیں اس کے امکان میں پیدا ہونے کی وجہ سے کیونکہ مالک کے قبضہ میں ان کا وجود نہیں تھا۔ اسلئے کہ منافع اعراض ہوتے ہیں جو باقی نہیں رہ سکتے تو غاصب ان کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ اپنی ضرورت دور کرنے کیلئے اور انسان اپنی ملک کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا اور کیسے ضامن ہوگا حالانکہ منافع کو غصب کرنا اور ان کو تلف کر نا متحقق نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ ان کیلئے بقا نہیں ہے اور اسلئے کہ منافع کو اعیان کے ساتھ کوئی مماثلت نہیں ہے۔ ان کے جلد فنا ہو جانے اور اعیان کے باقی رہنے کی وجہ سے اور یہ مآخذ مختلف میں مفصل معلوم ہیں اور ہم یہ تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ وہ بذات خود قیمتی ہیں بلکہ درود عقد کے وقت ضرورۃ قیمتی ٹھہرا لئے جاتے ہیں۔ حالانکہ یہاں کوئی عقد نہیں پایا گیا۔ مگر جو کچھ اس کے استعمال کی وجہ سے ناقص ہو جائے وہ اس پر مضمون ہے مال عین کے بعض اجزاء، تلف کرنے کی وجہ سے ۔
تشریح قوله ولا يضمن الغاصب .. الخ ۔ ہمارے یہاں غاصب شی ، مغصوب کی واپسی تک اس کے منافع کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا۔ خواہ اس نے وہ منافع بالفعل حاصل کر لئے ہوں یا مغصوب بشی کو برکا رکھ چھوڑا ہو۔ مثلاً ایک شخص نے کسی کا غلام غصب کیا اور اس کو ایک ماہ تک روکے رکھا یہاں تک کہ وہ غاصب منافع ہو گیا۔ یا اس نے غلام سے خدمت کی یہاں تک کہ وہ مستبلک منافع ہو گیا تو ہمارے نزدیک وہ ان منافع کا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔
صدر الاسلام بزدوی کی شرح کافی میں ہے۔ لیس على الغاصب في ركوب الدابة وسكنى الدار اجر وهو مذهب علمائنا ہاں اگر اس کے استعمال سے مغصوب میں کوئی نقصان آ گیا۔ تو نقصان کا ضامن ہوگا۔
قوله و قال الشافعي الخ- امام شافعی اور امام احمد کے نزدیک منافع کا بھی ضامن ہوگا۔ پس اتنی مدت اس چیز کا جوا جرش وہ غائب کے ذمہ واجب ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حکم کے حق میں ان دونوں مذہبوں کے درمیان تحصیل و تعطیل کا کوئی فرق نہیں۔ یعنی امام شافعی کے نزدیک غاصب بہر صورت ضامن ہوگا۔ استعمال کرے یا معطل چھوڑے اور ہمارے نزدیک بہر صورت ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ قوله قال مالك.... الخ - امام امالک کے قول کی بابت اصحاب مالک کا اختلاف ہے بعض نے کہا ہے کہ منافع کا ضامن نہ ہو
The usurper is not liable for the benefits of what he usurped unless it decreases through use; then he pays the decrease. Al-Shafi'i said: He is liable for them, so the equivalent rent is obligatory. There is no difference between the two madhhabs whether he left it idle or occupied it. Malik said: If he occupied it, the equivalent rent is obligatory; if he left it idle, nothing is upon him. His (Shafi'i's) proof is that benefits are valuable property (amwal mutaqawwima) such that liability for them is established through contracts, so likewise through usurpation. Our proof is that these benefits came into existence in the usurper's ownership due to their occurrence in his capacity, because they did not come into existence in the owner's hand, for they are accidents (a'rad) that do not persist, so the usurper owns them to fulfill his need, and a person is not liable for his own property. How can he be liable when usurping and destroying them is not actualized, because they have no permanence, and because benefits are not analogous to physical objects (a'yan) due to their quick perishing and the permanence of physical objects. These principles are known in al-Mukhtalaf. And we do not concede that they are valuable in themselves; rather, they become valuable by necessity when a contract is made, and no contract exists here. However, whatever decreases due to his use is guaranteed upon him because he consumed some parts of the physical object.
Translation: The usurper is not liable for the benefits of what he usurped unless it becomes defective due to his use; then he will pay compensation. Imam Shafi'i says that he will be liable for benefits, so the equivalent rent is obligatory, and in both madhhabs there is no difference whether he left it idle or used it for residence. Imam Malik says that if he resided in it, the equivalent rent is obligatory, and if he left it idle, nothing is upon him. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that benefits are valuable property; since liability for them is established through contracts, it is likewise through usurpation. Our proof is that these benefits came into existence in the usurper's ownership because they occur in his capacity, since they did not exist in the owner's hand because benefits are accidents that cannot persist; thus the usurper owns them to fulfill his need, and a person is not liable for his own property. How can he be liable when usurping and destroying them is not actualized because they have no permanence, and because benefits have no similarity to physical objects due to their quick perishing and the permanence of physical objects. These principles are known in detail in al-Mukhtalaf. We do not concede that they are valuable in themselves; rather, they become valuable necessarily when a contract is made, and here no contract exists. However, whatever becomes defective due to his use is guaranteed upon him because he consumed some parts of the physical object.
Commentary on his saying 'and he does not guarantee...' etc. According to us, the usurper is not liable for the benefits of the usurped property until its return, whether he actually obtained those benefits or left the property idle. For example, if a person usurps someone's slave and detains him for a month such that the usurper makes profit, or he takes service from the slave such that he enjoys the benefits, then according to us he will not be liable for those benefits. In Sadr al-Islam al-Bazdawi's Sharh al-Kafi: 'There is no rent upon the usurper for riding an animal or residing in a house, and this is the madhhab of our scholars.' However, if some defect occurs in the usurped property due to use, then he is liable for the defect.
His saying 'and al-Shafi'i said...' etc. According to Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad, he will also be liable for benefits; thus the rent for that period will be due from the usurper. The author of al-Hidayah says that regarding the ruling, there is no difference between these two madhhabs in terms of use or non-use; i.e., according to Imam Shafi'i, the usurper is liable in any case, whether he uses it or leaves it idle, and according to us, he is not liable in any case. His saying 'Malik said...' etc. Regarding the statement of Imam Malik, there is disagreement among the Malikis; some said that he is not liable for benefits...
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on whether a usurper is liable for the benefits (manafi') of the usurped property. The text begins with the Hanafi ruling from the matn: the usurper is not liable for benefits unless the property decreases in value due to use, in which case he compensates the decrease. Three positions are presented: (1) Shafi'i: The usurper is liable for the market rent (ujr al-mithl) regardless of whether he actually used the property or left it idle. (2) Maliki: Liability only if he actually used the property; if left idle, no liability. (3) Hanafi: No liability for benefits at all, only for physical decrease. The Shafi'i proof is that benefits are valuable property (amwal mutaqawwima) and since contracts (like lease) establish liability for them, wrongful taking (ghasb) should also. The Hanafi proof is that benefits are accidents (a'rad) that come into existence in the usurper's possession; they did not exist in the owner's hand. The usurper owns them by necessity to fulfill his need, and one is not liable for one's own property. Moreover, benefits cannot be physically usurped or destroyed because they are transient. The commentator adds that benefits are not intrinsically valuable; they become valuable only through a contract, and no contract exists here. The exception for physical decrease is because that is a consumption of the actual substance of the property. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Key Terms
منافع (manāfiʿ): Usufruct or benefits derived from property, such as rent, service, or use.
اجر المثل (ujr al-mithl): The equivalent market rent or hire of a similar property.
اعراض (aʿrāḍ): Accidents; non-permanent attributes or benefits that do not persist over time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person usurps a car and uses it for a week without causing any physical damage. According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the usurper's liability for the benefits?
A) He must pay the market rent for the week.
B) He must pay only if he caused the car's value to decrease.
C) He is not liable for any benefits.
D) He is liable for both benefits and any decrease.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a usurper is not liable for benefits of the usurped property because benefits are transient accidents owned by the usurper by necessity; only physical decrease is compensable.

Liability for Usufruct in Ghasb: Hanafi vs Shafi'i vs Maliki
Inter-madhhab dispute on usurper's liability for usufruct

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on usurper's liability for usufruct, explain the Shafi'i and Maliki positions, and evaluate the proofs for each school.

Core Idea
Usufructs are accidents that become the usurper's property; one is not liable for one's own property.

This lesson explores a classic inter-madhhab dispute: if someone wrongfully takes another's property (ghasb) and uses it without permission, does he owe compensation for the benefit (manfa'ah) he obtained? The Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki schools diverge sharply. We will examine each position, trace the proofs, and understand the practical consequences. By the end, you will grasp why the Hanafi school distinguishes between damage to the substance ('ayn) and the usufruct (manafi'), and how this affects real-world cases.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: the usurper is not liable for the usufruct, only for any physical diminution of the property. Note that this applies whether he uses the property or leaves it idle.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the usurper is liable for the usufruct in all cases, requiring payment of ajr al-mithl (equivalent rent). Imam Malik holds a middle position: liability only if the usurper actually used the property.
Some Malikis differ; the text mentions multiple views within the Maliki school.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i argument: usufructs are valuable property (mal mutaqawwim) because they are compensable in contracts (ijarah) and can be dower. Therefore, they should be compensable in torts like ghasb.
The Shafi'i also argue that property status of 'ayn depends on usufructs, so usufructs are even more deserving of being considered property.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that usufructs are accidents (a'rad) that perish instantly; they arise in the usurper's possession, so he becomes their owner. One cannot be liable for one's own property. Moreover, liability in torts requires similarity (mumathalah) as per Quran 2:194 and 42:40, and usufructs cannot be similar to material objects.
The Hanafi also argue that usufructs are not valuable in themselves but only become valuable through contract out of necessity.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: if a person usurps a house and lives in it for a month without causing damage, Hanafi says nothing is owed, Shafi'i says full rental value, Maliki says rental value only if he actually lived there.
The same applies to animals, slaves, etc.

اس کا جواب صاحب غایۃ البیان نے دیا ہے کہ اجرت ہمارے نزدیک منافع کے مقابلہ میں واجب نہیں ہوتی بلکہ مالک کی
Book of Usurpation. Ashraf al-Bidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 12. It remains, so he owns it to fulfill his need, and a person is not liable for his own property. How can it be that usurpation and destruction of them are not realized? Because they have no permanence, and because they are not similar to material objects due to their rapid perishing and the permanence of material objects. These points are known in detail in Al-Mukhtalaf. And we do not concede that they (usufructs) are valuable in themselves; rather, they become valuable out of necessity when a contract occurs, but no contract has occurred here. However, any diminution caused by use is guaranteed upon him because he has consumed some parts of the material object. Translation: And the usurper is not liable for the usufruct of the thing he has usurped unless it becomes diminished due to his use, so he shall compensate the loss. Imam Shafi'i says that he is liable for the usufruct, so an equivalent rent is obligatory. And there is no difference between the two schools regarding whether the usurper left it idle or used it for dwelling. Imam Malik says that if the usurper dwelt in it, equivalent rent is obligatory; if he left it idle, nothing is obligatory. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that usufructs are valuable property, such that liability for them is obligatory through contracts, so likewise liability becomes obligatory through usurpation. Our proof is that these usufructs accrue to the usurper's ownership due to their arising in his possession, because they did not exist in the owner's possession. Because usufructs are accidents that cannot remain, so the usurper becomes their owner to fulfill his need, and a person is not liable for his own property. And how could he be liable when usurpation and destruction of usufructs are not realized? Because they have no permanence, and because usufructs have no similarity to material objects due to their rapid perishing and the permanence of material objects. And these points are known in detail in Al-Mukhtalaf. And we do not concede that they are valuable in themselves; rather, they become valuable out of necessity when a contract occurs, but no contract has occurred here. However, any diminution caused by use is guaranteed upon him because he has consumed some parts of the material object. Commentary on his saying "And the usurper is not liable..." etc. According to us, the usurper of a thing is not liable for its usufruct until the return of the usurped item, regardless of whether he actually obtained the usufruct or left the usurped thing idle. For example, a person usurps someone's slave and keeps him for a month until he becomes a usurper of usufruct, or he takes service from the slave until he becomes a user of usufruct; according to us, he is not liable for those usufructs. In Sadr al-Islam al-Bazdawi's Sharh al-Kafi: "The usurper is not liable for riding the animal or dwelling in the house, and this is the madhhab of our scholars. However, if his use causes a defect in the usurped item, he is liable for the loss." His saying "And al-Shafi'i said..." etc. According to Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad, he is also liable for the usufruct, so the rent for that period is obligatory on the usurper. The author of Al-Hidayah states that there is no difference between the two schools regarding the ruling on use and idleness, meaning according to Imam Shafi'i, the usurper is liable in both cases, and according to us, he is not liable in both cases. His saying "Malik said..." etc. Regarding Imam Malik's statement, the Malikis differ: some said he is not liable for usufruct, as per our view, i.e., not liable in case of usurpation nor in case of destruction. And it is narrated from Ibn al-Qasim that he is liable for the proceeds of houses and goats/camels, but not for the usufruct of slaves and animals. And some said that if he dwelt in the usurped house, he is liable for equivalent rent; if he left it idle, nothing is obligatory. His saying "His proof is that usufructs..." etc. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that usufructs are valuable property, such that liability for them is obligatory through contracts like ijarah etc., by consensus, whether the contracts are valid or invalid. So, like material objects, compensation for them is also obligatory due to usurpation. Because a contract does not make something non-valuable valuable (like if it is upon a carcass). The reason is that property (mal) is that which is other than us and created for our benefits, and usufructs share this characteristic; therefore, they are eligible to be dower. And the property status of material objects is also by virtue of their usufructs that pertain to benefits. This is why when usufructs of a thing are few, the value of the substance is also low. And when material objects become property by virtue of usufructs, then usufructs themselves being property is even more evident. Moreover, taking a countervalue in exchange for usufruct is valid in Sharia, whereas taking a countervalue for something non-valuable is impermissible, like taking a countervalue for wine or a grain of sesame. As for the valuation of usufructs, it is because valuation is based on desirability, and usufructs are desirable to people; thus they give up material objects for them. His saying "And our proof is that they accrued..." etc. Our proof is that when the usurper became liable for the usurped object, whether by value or by similar item, then these usufructs arose, so they accrued to the usurper's ownership because they came into existence through his capacity, disposal, and power, and through his acquisition and action. And acquisition belongs to the acquirer, due to the Prophet's saying: "Every person is more entitled to his acquisition." Because the existence of these usufructs was not in the owner's possession. Because usufructs are not material objects but accidents that cannot remain, so to fulfill necessity, the usurper becomes their owner. And it is obvious that a person is not liable for his own property. And even if we concede that these usufructs arise in the owner's ownership, still he cannot be liable because usurping or destroying usufructs is inconceivable since their remaining is impossible. Also, because usufructs cannot be similar to material objects, as they perish quickly while material objects remain, whereas liability for transgression is based on similarity. Allah Almighty says: "So whoever has assaulted you, then assault him in the manner similar to what he assaulted you." And: "And the retribution for an evil act is an evil one like it." His saying "And a person is not liable..." etc. The author of Al-Nata'ij has objected to this proof, saying that its implication is that in the ijarah of land and animals, the lessee would not be liable for rent when usufructs accrue in his possession, because just as a person is not liable for his own property, similarly rent is not obligatory in exchange for his property? But in ijarah, rent is obligatory by consensus. The author of Ghayat al-Bayan has answered that according to us, rent is not obligatory in exchange for usufructs, but rather in exchange for the owner's [ability].
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the liability of a usurper (ghasib) for the usufruct (manafi') of the usurped property. The Hanafi position, as stated in the matn, is that the usurper is not liable for the usufruct unless the property itself is diminished. The Shafi'i position is that he is liable for the usufruct, requiring payment of equivalent rent (ajr al-mithl) regardless of whether he used the property or left it idle. The Maliki position is intermediate: liability only if he actually used the property. The text provides proofs for each school. The Shafi'i argue that usufructs are valuable property (mal) because they are compensable in contracts like ijarah, and thus should be compensable in torts like ghasb. The Hanafi respond that usufructs are accidents (a'rad) that perish instantly; they arise in the usurper's possession because the owner had no control over them, so they become the usurper's property. Since one is not liable for one's own property, no compensation is due. However, any physical damage to the substance ('ayn) is compensable because that is a tangible loss. The Hanafis further argue that usufructs cannot be usurped or destroyed because they have no permanence, and liability in torts is based on similarity (mumathalah), which is impossible with usufructs. The passage also addresses an objection: if usufructs become the usurper's property, then in ijarah (hire), the lessee would also own the usufruct and not owe rent. The Hanafi response is that in ijarah, the rent is paid for the owner's making the usufruct available, not for the usufruct itself. This distinction preserves the validity of ijarah. The authority weight of this ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, as the Hanafi position is the established madhhab.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Wrongful seizure and wrongful possession of another's property without consent.
منافع (manafi'): The benefits or usufructs arising from a property, such as the use of a house or the service of a slave.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage; in this context, whether the usurper must pay for the usufruct.
متقوم (mutaqawwim): Valuable property recognized by Sharia; something that can be lawfully sold and compensated.
عین (ayn): A physical, tangible object with enduring existence, as opposed to manfa'ah (usufruct).
عرض (arad): An accident; a non-enduring attribute that perishes quickly, such as usufruct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a usurper not liable for the usufruct of the usurped property?
A) Because usufructs are not considered property in any context.
B) Because usufructs are accidents that become the usurper's property and one is not liable for one's own property.
C) Because the owner has abandoned the usufruct.
D) Because the usurper had permission to use the property.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a usurper is not liable for the usufruct of usurped property because usufructs are accidents that become his property; only physical diminution of the substance is compensable.

Liability for Usufruct in Usurpation: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on daman manafi' in ghasb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on liability for usufruct in usurpation, explain the Hanafi proof, and compare it to the Shafi'i position, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
The usurper owns the usufruct by acquisition, so he is not liable for them—liability only for damage to the corpus.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding whether a usurper (ghasib) must compensate the owner for the usufruct (manafi') of the property he has used. The Shafi'i school argues that usufruct are valuable property, so their usurpation entails liability. The Hanafi school refutes this with three key arguments, relying on the maxim that acquisition belongs to the acquirer and the principle that liability requires similitude.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school holds regarding liability for usufruct in ghasb. Note that they distinguish between liability for the corpus and liability for usufruct.
Hanafi: no liability for usufruct; only for damage to the 'ayn.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that the Shafi'i school is the opponent and that they hold the usurper liable for usufruct as well, analogizing to contracts like ijarah.
Shafi'i: usufruct are amwal mutaqawwima, so ghasb triggers daman.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: usufruct are valuable by nature, as seen in contracts, compensation, and people's valuation. Therefore, by qiyas on 'ayn, usurpation of usufruct must entail liability.
Shafi'i uses qiyas jali: manafi' like 'ayn in being property.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school rebuts with three arguments: (1) usufruct arise in the usurper's possession and become his property by acquisition; (2) usufruct are accidents that cannot be usurped or destroyed; (3) liability requires similitude, but usufruct are not like 'ayn. Also, the Shafi'i analogy to ijarah fails because ijarah is based on istihsan, not qiyas.
Hanafi response is multi-pronged: ownership, impossibility of ghasb of accidents, and lack of similitude.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference between the two positions: Hanafi says no compensation for use unless damage to the corpus; Shafi'i says the usurper must pay the rental value (ujrat al-mithl) even if the property is returned intact.
This affects real-world cases of unauthorized use of property.

قوله له ان المنافع .... الخ - امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منافع بھی قیمتی مال ہیں ۔ یہاں تک کہ عقود یعنی اجارہ وغیرہ کے ذریعہ سے بالا جماع ان کا ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے۔ خواہ عقود صحیحہ ہوں یا فاسدہ ۔ پس اعیان کی طرح غصب کی وجہ سے ان کا بھی تاوان واجب ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ عقد کسی غیر متقوم کو متقوم نہیں کر دیتا (كما لو ورد على الميتة ) وجہ یہ ہے کہ مال اس کو کہتے ہیں جو ہمارے سوا ہو اور ہمارے مصالح کیلئے مخلوق ہو اور منافع کی یہی شان ہے اسی لئے وہ مہر ہونے کے قابل ہوتے ہیں اور اعیان کا اموال ہونا بھی انہیں منافع کے لحاظ سے ہوتا ہے جو المفا سے متعلق ہوتے ہیں۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ جب کسی شی ء کے منافع کم ہوں تو عین کی مالیت بھی کم ہوتی ہے اور جب منافع کے اعتبار سے اعیان اموال ہوئیں تو منافع کا بذات خود اموال ہونا بطریق اولی ہوگا۔ علاوہ ازیں منافع کی طرف سے مال عوض لینا شرعاً صحیح ہے۔ جبکہ غیر متقوم کا عوض لینا نا جائز ہے۔ جیسے شراب اور تل کے ایک دانہ کا عوض لینا۔ رہا منافع کا قیمتی ہونا سو ا سلئے کہ تقوم عزت سے عبارت ہے اور منافع بھی لوگوں کے نزدیک عزیز ہوتے ہیں۔ ولهذا يبذلون الاعيان لاجلها
قوله ولنا انها حصلت .... الخ - ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب غاصب منصوب کا ضامن ہو گیا خواہ قیمت ہو یا بمثل تب یہ منافع پیدا ہوئے ہیں تو یہ منافع غاصب کی ملکیت پر پیدا ہوئے۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کے امکان اور تصرف و قدرت میں اس کے کسب و فعل سے حاصل ہوئے ہیں والكسب للكاسب لقوله عليه السلام كل الناس احق بكسبه اس واسطے کہ ان منافع کا وجود مالک کے قبضہ میں نہیں تھا۔
اسلئے کہ منافع اعیان نہیں بلکہ اعراض ہیں جو باقی نہیں رہ سکتے تو دفع ضرورت کی خاطر غاصب ان کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ انسان اپنی ملک کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا۔ اور اگر ملک مالک پر ان منافع کا حدوث ہی تسلیم کر لیں تب بھی وہ ضامن نہیں ہوسکتا کیونکہ منافع کو غصب کرنا یا تلف کرنا غیر متصور ہے اسلئے کہ ان کا باقی رہنا ناممکن ہے۔ نیز اسلئے بھی کہ منافع اعیان کے مثل نہیں ہو سکتے ۔ کیونکہ وہ جلد فنا ہو جاتے ہیں اور اعیان باقی رہتی ہیں۔ حالانکہ مضمان عدوان مماثلت پر ہی بنی ہے۔ قال اللہ تعالیٰ فمن اعتدي عليكم فاعتدوا عليه بمثل ما اعتدى، وجزاء سيئة سيئة مثلها -
قوله والانسان لا يضمن ... الخ - صاحب نتائج نے اس پر یہ اعتراض کیا ہے کہ اس دلیل کا مختصیٰ یہ ہے کہ استیجار ڈورو اراضی اور استیجار دواب وغیرہ میں مستاجر پر اجرت واجب نہ ہو جبکہ منافع اس کے قبضہ میں حاصل ہوں اسلئے کہ جس طرح آدمی اپنی ملک کا منامن نہیں ہوتا۔ ایسے ہی اس کی ملک کے مقابلہ میں اجرت بھی واجب نہیں ہوتی ۔ حالانکہ اجارہ میں بالا جماع اجرت واجب ہوتی ہے۔
اس کا جواب صاحب غایۃ البیان نے دیا ہے کہ اجرت ہمارے نزدیک منافع کے مقابلہ میں واجب نہیں ہوتی بلکہ مالک کی طرف سے قابو دینے کے مقابلہ میں ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے کہ جب مالک کی طرف سے قابو دئیے بغیر مستاجر اس کے منافع حاصل نہیں کر سکتا تو مالک کا قابو دینا استیفاء منافع تک رسائی کا ایک وسیلہ اور طریقہ ہوا۔ پس بغرض حاجت وجوب اجرت میں وسیلہ کو خود منفعت کا حکم دے دیا گیا۔ صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ یہ جواب گو یہاں مخلص تو ہو گیا۔ لیکن کتاب الاجارت میں جو امور مذکور ہیں ظاہرا ان کا ترک لازم آتا ہے۔ مثلاً
a الاجارة تملیک المنافع بعوض
ب والقياس يأبى جواز هالان المعقود عليه المنفعة وهى معدومة
ج تنعقد الاجارة ساعة فساعة على حسب حدوث المنافع لان المعاوضة تقتضى التسارى والملك في المنفعة التى هي المعقود عليه يقع ساعة فساعة على حسب حدوثها فكذالک فى بدلها وهو الاجرة
d الدار له قيمت مقام المنفعة في حق اضافة العقود اليها ليرتبط الايجاب بالقبول ثم عمله يظهر في حق المنفعة ملكا واستحقاقا حال وجود المنفعة الى غير ذلك
یہ تمام اقوال اسی پر دال ہیں کہ اجرت منافع کے مقابلہ میں ہوتی ہے۔
پس بہتر جواب یہ ہے کہ دلیل مذکور کا اقتضاء جو عدم وجوب اجرت ہے یہ بنا بر موجب قیاس ہے اور جب اجارہ کا جواز ہی خلاف قیاس اور بطریق استحسان ہے تو مستاجر پر منافع کے مقابلہ میں اجرت کا وجوب بھی موجب استحسان کے طور پر ہوسکتا ہے بخلاف غصب کے کہ یہ بالکل جائز نہیں نہ قیا سانہ استحسانا فلا يترك فيه ما يخالف القياس
قوله هذه الماخذ.... الخ - ماخذ سے مراد وہ عمل ہیں جو مناط حکم ہیں جن کو صاحب ہدایہ نے اولاً لانها حصلت فی ملک الغاصب سے اور ثانیاً انها لا يتحقق غصبها واتلافها سے اور ثالثاً لانها لا تماثل الاعیان ھ سے ذکر کیا ہے۔ اور امختلف سے مراد بقول انزاری و صاحب عنایہ فقیہ ابواللیث کی کتاب المختلف ہے۔ لیکن محقق بدرالدین عینی فرماتے ہیں:
لم لا يجوز ان يكون اراد به مختلف الطريقه بيننا وبين الشافعى فان هذه المسالة من جملة المسائل المذكورة في علم الخلاف
قوله ولا نسلم .... الخ - امام شافعی کے قول المنافع اموال متقومہ کا جواب ہے کہ منافع کا بذات خود متقوم ہو ناتسلیم نہیں بلکہ جب ان پر عقد اجارہ وغیرہ وارد ہوتا ہے تو بوجہ ضرورت خلاف قیاس ان کو قیمتی ٹھہرالیا جاتا ہے اور یہاں غاصب کے ساتھ کوئی عقد نہیں پایا کیا لہذا ضامن نہ ہو گا۔ البتہ عین مغصوب میں سے جو کچھ اس کے استعمال سے ناقص ہو جائے اس کا ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس نے مال سین کے بعض اجزاء تلف کر دئیے۔ پھر استعمال کی قید صرف باعتبار غالب ہے ورنہ حکم یہی ہے کہ اگر اس کے استعمال کے بغیر بھی ناقص ہو جائے تب بھی نقصان کا ضامن ہو گا۔
Book of Usurpation. His saying: 'Indeed, usufruct...' - The proof of Imam Shafi'i is that usufruct are also valuable property, to the extent that their liability is obligatory by consensus through contracts like ijarah, whether valid or void. So, like corporeal property, their compensation is also obligatory. Because contract does not make non-valuable things valuable (as if it occurred on carrion). The reason is that property is that which is other than us and created for our needs, and usufruct have this quality; therefore they are eligible to be dower, and corporeal property being property is also due to usufruct that are connected to benefits. This is why when the usufruct of something are few, its value decreases, and when corporeal property are considered property due to usufruct, then usufruct being property in themselves is even more primary. Moreover, taking compensation for usufruct is valid in Sharia, while taking compensation for non-valuable things is impermissible, like wine and a single grain of sesame. As for usufruct being valuable, it is because valuableness (taqawwum) is honor, and usufruct are honored by people, hence they give up corporeal property for them. His saying: 'And for us, they arose...' - Our proof is that when the usurper became liable for the usurped property, whether by value or by like, then these usufruct arose, so they arose in the ownership of the usurper, because they are obtained from his capacity, disposal, and power, through his acquisition and action; and acquisition belongs to the acquirer, based on the Prophet's saying: 'Every person has more right to his acquisition.' Because the existence of these usufruct was not in the owner's possession. Since usufruct are not corporeal but accidents that cannot persist, so out of necessity the usurper becomes their owner. And it is clear that a person is not liable for his own property. And even if we admit that these usufruct occurred in the owner's ownership, still he would not be liable because it is inconceivable to usurp or destroy usufruct, since their remaining is impossible. Also because usufruct cannot be like corporeal property, as they perish quickly while property remains. Liability for transgression is based on similitude. Allah says: 'So whoever transgresses against you, then transgress against him with the like of that which he transgressed.' His saying: 'And a person is not liable...' - The author of Nata'ij objected that the implication of this proof is that in the rent of lands and animals, the lessee would not owe rent while usufruct arise in his possession, because just as a person is not liable for his own property, similarly rent would not be obligatory in exchange for his property, while in ijarah rent is obligatory by consensus. The author of Ghayat al-Bayan replied that in our view rent is not obligatory for usufruct but for the owner's enabling (tamkin), because without the owner's enabling the lessee cannot obtain usufruct, so the owner's enabling becomes a means and way to obtain usufruct. Thus out of necessity, the means is given the ruling of the benefit. The author of Nata'ij says that this reply is a way out here, but it necessitates abandoning what is mentioned in the Book of Ijarah, for example: (a) Ijarah is the transfer of ownership of usufruct for compensation. (b) Qiyas prohibits its permissibility because the contracted thing (usufruct) is non-existent. (c) Ijarah is concluded moment by moment according to the occurrence of usufruct, because exchange requires mutual exchange, and ownership of usufruct (which is the contracted thing) occurs moment by moment according to its occurrence, and similarly for its substitute, rent. (d) The house has value in place of usufruct in the context of adding contracts to it to link offer and acceptance, then its effect appears regarding usufruct in ownership and entitlement at the time of existence of usufruct, etc. All these statements indicate that rent is for usufruct. The better answer is that the implication of the mentioned proof (non-obligation of rent) is according to qiyas, and since the permissibility of ijarah itself is contrary to qiyas and by way of istihsan, the obligation of rent for usufruct on the lessee can also be by way of istihsan, unlike usurpation, which is completely impermissible neither by qiyas nor istihsan, so what contradicts qiyas is not left in it. His saying: 'These makhadh...' - Makhadh refers to the actions that are the criteria (manat) of the ruling, which the author of Hidayah mentioned firstly from 'because they arose in the usurper's ownership', secondly from 'their usurpation and destruction cannot be realized', and thirdly from 'they are not similar to corporeal property'. And 'mukhtalif' refers, according to al-Ansari and the author of 'Inayah, to the book al-Mukhtalif of Faqih Abu al-Layth. But al-Muhaqqiq Badr al-Din al-Ayni says: Why is it not permissible that he meant by it the difference of method between us and al-Shafi'i? For this issue is among those mentioned in the science of disputation. His saying: 'And we do not accept...' - This is the answer to Imam Shafi'i's statement that usufruct are valuable property: their being valuable in themselves is not accepted; rather, when a contract like ijarah occurs on them, they are deemed valuable by way of necessity contrary to qiyas, and here there is no contract with the usurper, so he will not be liable. However, he will be liable for any deficiency in the usurped property due to his use, because he destroyed some parts of the property. Then the condition of use is only with regard to the usual, otherwise the ruling is that if it becomes deficient even without his use, he will still be liable for the loss.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding whether a usurper (ghasib) is liable for the usufruct (manafi') of the usurped property that he has used or that have accrued during his possession. The Shafi'i position, attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i, argues that usufruct are valuable property (amwal mutaqawwima) just like corporeal property ('ayn), because people value them, they can be the subject of contracts (like ijarah), and they are exchangeable for compensation. Therefore, by analogy to usurpation of corporeal property, the usurper should be liable for them. The Hanafi position, which is the relied-upon view in the madhhab, refutes this with three core arguments: (1) The usufruct arise in the possession of the usurper and are acquired by his own action; based on the hadith 'Every person has more right to his acquisition,' they become his property, and a person is not liable for his own property. (2) Usufruct are accidents that cannot persist, so they cannot be subject to usurpation or destruction in a legally meaningful way. (3) Liability for transgression (daman bi al-'udwan) is based on similitude (mumathalah) as indicated by the Quranic verse, but usufruct are not similar to corporeal property because they perish instantly. The text then addresses an objection: if the Hanafi logic were applied, a lessee would not owe rent for usufruct that arise in his possession, but rent is obligatory by consensus. The first response distinguishes between usurpation and ijarah: rent is for the owner's enabling (tamkin), not for the usufruct themselves. However, this is challenged by statements from the Book of Ijarah that define ijarah as the transfer of ownership of usufruct for compensation. The better response is that ijarah is permitted by istihsan (juristic preference) contrary to qiyas, so rent is obligatory by istihsan. Usurpation, however, is impermissible both by qiyas and istihsan, so qiyas is not abandoned. Finally, the passage refutes the Shafi'i claim that usufruct are inherently valuable; rather, they become valuable only by contract (like ijarah) out of necessity, and in usurpation there is no contract. The usurper is liable only for any reduction in the corporeal property caused by his use, not for the usufruct themselves.

Key Terms
منافع (manāfiʿ): Usufruct or benefits arising from the use of property, such as the dwelling of a house or the ride of an animal.
غصب (ghaṣb): Unlawful usurpation and taking possession of another's property without right and without permission.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability or responsibility to compensate for loss or damage, either by returning the property or paying its value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, why is the usurper not liable for the usufruct of the usurped property?
A) Because usufruct are not considered property in any case.
B) Because the usufruct arise in the usurper's own possession and become his property by acquisition.
C) Because the owner has abandoned his right to the usufruct.
D) Because the usurper has a contract with the owner.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between liability for the corporeal property and usufruct: the usurper owns the usufruct by acquisition and is not liable for them, only for damage to the corpus.

Usurper's Liability for Rent: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Commentary explaining why usurper does not pay rent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a usurper's liability for rent and distinguish between the application of qiyas and istihsan in ijarah versus ghasp.

Core Idea
A usurper does not pay rent because ijarah's istihsan does not extend to unlawful acts.

A usurper (ghasib) who uses another's property without permission clearly benefits from that use. Common sense suggests he should pay rent, just like a lessee. Yet the Hanafi school rules that no rent is due for the mere use. The reasoning hinges on the nature of ijarah: it is a contract that is valid only by istihsan (juristic preference) overriding qiyas, and that relaxation does not apply to the unlawful act of usurpation. This lesson unpacks the analytical steps behind this ruling and differentiates it from the Shafi'i position, offering you a clear framework for applying qiyas and istihsan in similar cases.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Begin by identifying the precise ruling: the usurper is not obligated to pay rent for the period of use, even though he benefited. He is only liable for any physical damage he caused.
This is the mufta bihi position from the Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the qiyas that would suggest liability
Analogy to ijarah: since ijarah involves using usufruct in exchange for rent, and the usurper also uses usufruct, qiyas would require rent. Understand why this analogy is rejected.
The object of ijarah is the usufruct, which is non-existent at contract formation.
3
Explain why ijarah itself is valid despite qiyas
Ijarah is valid only by istihsan, because necessity requires treating the means (owner's permission) as the usufruct itself. This exception is limited to lawful transactions.
Remember: istihsan overrides qiyas only where the law itself is permissible.
4
Explain why istihsan does not apply to ghasp
Ghasp is inherently unlawful (lā jā'iz) – neither by qiyas nor by istihsan. Therefore, the exception that validates ijarah cannot be extended to a forbidden act.
This is the core distinction: lawfulness of the underlying act matters.
5
Respond to the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i considers usufruct as valuable property (amwal mutaqawwimah), making the usurper liable for rent. The Hanafi response: usufruct are not inherently valuable; they become valuable only through a contract (istihsan). No contract exists with the usurper.
This is a dispute over the very nature of usufruct as property.

كتاب الغصب ۳۷۶
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۲
طرف سے قابو دینے کے مقابلہ میں ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے کہ جب مالک کی طرف سے قابو دئیے بغیر مستاجر اس کے منافع حاصل نہیں کر سکتا تو مالک کا قابو دینا استیفاء منافع تک رسائی کا ایک وسیلہ اور طریقہ ہوا۔ پس بغرض حاجت وجوب اجرت میں وسیلہ کو خود منفعت کا حکم دے دیا گیا۔ صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ یہ جواب گو یہاں مخلص تو ہو گیا۔ لیکن کتاب الاجارت میں جو امور مذکور ہیں ظاہرا ان کا ترک لازم آتا ہے۔ مثلاً
a الاجارة تملیک المنافع بعوض
-٢- والقياس يأبى جواز هالان المعقود عليه المنفعة وهى معدومة
تنعقد الاجارة ساعة فساعة على حسب حدوث المنافع لان المعاوضة تقتضى التسارى والملك في المنفعة التى هي المعقود عليه يقع ساعة فساعة على حسب حدوثها فکذالک فى بدلها وهو الاجرة
الدار له قيمت مقام المنفعة في حق اضافة العقود اليها ليرتبط الايجاب بالقبول ثم عمله يظهر في حق المنفعة ملكا واستحقاقا حال وجود المنفعة الى غير ذلك
یہ تمام اقوال اسی پر دال ہیں کہ اجرت منافع کے مقابلہ میں ہوتی ہے۔
پس بہتر جواب یہ ہے کہ دلیل مذکور کا اقتضاء جو عدم وجوب اجرت ہے یہ بنا بر موجب قیاس ہے اور جب اجارہ کا جواز ہی خلاف قیاس اور بطریق استحسان ہے تو مستاجر پر منافع کے مقابلہ میں اجرت کا وجوب بھی موجب استحسان کے طور پر ہوسکتا ہے بخلاف غصب کے کہ یہ بالکل جائز نہیں نہ قیا سانہ استحسانا فلا يترك فيه ما يخالف القياس
قوله هذه الماخذ.... الخ - ماخذ سے مراد وہ عمل ہیں جو مناط حکم ہیں جن کو صاحب ہدایہ نے اولاً لانها حصلت فی ملک الغاصب سے اور ثانیاً انها لا يتحقق غصبها واتلافها سے اور ثالثاً لانها لا تماثل الاعیان ھ سے ذکر کیا ہے۔ اور امختلف سے مراد بقول انزاری و صاحب عنایہ فقیہ ابواللیث کی کتاب المختلف ہے۔ لیکن محقق بدرالدین عینی فرماتے ہیں:
لم لا يجوز ان يكون اراد به مختلف الطريقه بيننا وبين الشافعى فان هذه المسالة من جملة المسائل المذكورة في علم الخلاف
قوله ولا نسلم .... الخ - امام شافعی کے قول المنافع اموال متقومہ کا جواب ہے کہ منافع کا بذات خود متقوم ہو ناتسلیم نہیں بلکہ جب ان پر عقد اجارہ وغیرہ وارد ہوتا ہے تو بوجہ ضرورت خلاف قیاس ان کو قیمتی ٹھہرالیا جاتا ہے اور یہاں غاصب کے ساتھ کوئی عقد نہیں پایا کیا لہذا ضامن نہ ہو گا۔ البتہ عین مغصوب میں سے جو کچھ اس کے استعمال سے ناقص ہو جائے اس کا ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس نے مال سین کے بعض اجزاء تلف کر دئیے۔ پھر استعمال کی قید صرف باعتبار غالب ہے ورنہ حکم یہی ہے کہ اگر اس کے استعمال کے بغیر بھی ناقص ہو جائے تب بھی نقصان کا ضامن ہو گا۔
Book of Ghasp. 376. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume 12. ... It is in exchange for giving control. Because when the lessee cannot obtain the usufruct without the owner giving control, the owner's giving control becomes a means and way to access the usufruct. Thus, out of necessity, the means was given the ruling of the usufruct itself regarding the obligation of rent. The author of Nata'ij says that this answer is a way out here, but it necessitates abandoning what is mentioned in Kitab al-Ijarah, e.g.: (1) Ijarah is the transfer of ownership of usufruct for compensation. (2) Qiyas precludes its permissibility because the object of contract is usufruct, which is non-existent. The ijarah contract is concluded moment by moment according to the occurrence of usufruct, because exchange requires symmetry, and ownership of the usufruct, which is the object of contract, occurs moment by moment according to its occurrence, similarly in its substitute, which is the rent. The house has value standing in place of the usufruct regarding attaching contracts to it to link offer and acceptance, then its effect appears regarding ownership and entitlement of usufruct at the time of its existence, etc. All these statements indicate that rent is in exchange for usufruct. So the better answer is that the implication of the mentioned evidence, which is non-obligation of rent, is based on qiyas, and since the permissibility of ijarah itself is against qiyas and by way of istihsan, then the obligation of rent on the lessee in exchange for usufruct can also be by way of istihsan, unlike ghasp, which is absolutely impermissible, neither by qiyas nor by istihsan, so what is contrary to qiyas is not left therein. His statement: 'hādhihi al-mākhadh...' The 'mākhadh' refer to the acts that are the basis of the ruling, which the author of Hidayah mentioned: first, 'because they occur in the possession of the usurper'; second, 'because their usurpation and destruction cannot be verified'; third, 'because they are not similar to physical assets'. And 'al-mukhtalaf' refers to the book 'al-Mukhtalaf' by Faqih Abu al-Layth, according to al-Ansari and Sahib al-'Inayah. But Muhaqqiq Badr al-Din al-'Ayni says: Why can it not be that he intends by it the difference between us and al-Shafi'i, for this issue is among those mentioned in the science of ikhtilaf? His statement: 'wa lā nusallim...' This is a response to Imam al-Shafi'i's statement that usufruct are valuable properties: that usufruct are not inherently valuable; rather, when a contract of ijarah etc. is entered upon them, out of necessity and against qiyas, they are considered valuable. Here, no contract exists with the usurper, so he will not be liable. However, for any part of the usurped property that is diminished due to his use, he will be liable because he has destroyed some parts of the property. Then the restriction of use is only in consideration of the majority; otherwise, the ruling is that if it becomes deficient even without his use, he will still be liable for the deficiency.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This is a commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah on a passage from Hidayah regarding the liability of a usurper (ghasib) for rent. The passage begins by addressing the issue of whether a usurper must pay rent for using the usurped property. The commentator explains that the obligation of rent in a valid ijarah contract is derived from istihsan (juristic preference), not from qiyas (analogy). In ijarah, rent is due even though the usufruct is created progressively, because necessity requires treating the means (owner's permission) as the usufruct itself. However, this reasoning does not apply to ghasp, which is inherently unlawful and cannot be regularized by istihsan. The passage then addresses objections from the author of Nata'ij and clarifies that the principles of ijarah do not require rent in ghasp. Finally, it responds to the Shafi'i position that usufruct are valuable property (amwal mutaqawwimah), stating that usufruct are not intrinsically valuable; they become valuable only through a contract out of necessity. Since there is no contract with the usurper, no rent is due.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Unlawful taking and use of property without owner's consent; the usurper is called ghasib.
اجارة (ijarah): A contract for the transfer of ownership (tamlik) of usufruct for a known compensation (ujrah).
منفعة (manfa'ah): Usufruct; the benefit or service derived from using an asset (e.g., living in a house).
تقوم (taqawwum): The quality of being considered legally valuable property (mal mutaqawwim) for which compensation is due if destroyed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a usurper not required to pay rent for using the usurped property, even though a lessee must pay rent for similar use?
A) Because usufruct has no value in Islamic law.
B) Because ijarah is based on istihsan and is lawful, while ghasp is unlawful and cannot be analogized.
C) Because the usurper's use is considered a gift from the owner.
D) Because the owner has the right to evict the usurper at any time.

Key Takeaway
A usurper does not pay rent because the istihsan that validates ijarah (and its rent) does not apply to the absolutely unlawful act of usurpation.

Liability for Destroying Dhimmi's Wine or Pig: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on liability for destroying a dhimmi's wine or pig and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Wine and pigs are valuable property for dhimmis, so destroying them incurs liability in Hanafi law.

This passage from the chapter on usurpation of non-fungible items presents a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether a Muslim who destroys a dhimmi's wine or pig must compensate. The ruling hinges on the concept of 'taqawwum' (legal value). We will examine both arguments and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its scope
Identify the ruling: If a Muslim destroys a dhimmi's wine or pig, he is liable (wajib). If he destroys a Muslim's, he is not. This also applies when a dhimmi destroys another dhimmi's.
The text also mentions sale of these items between dhimmis is valid per Hanafi.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold that no liability exists even for a dhimmi's wine or pig, because these items lack value for Muslims and dhimmis are followers of Muslims in rulings.
Imam Malik agrees with the Hanafi position.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is based on qiyas: wine for a dhimmi is like vinegar for a Muslim. Both are permissible and valuable in their respective laws, so destroying them requires compensation.
The analogy relies on the effective cause ('illa) of permissibility and value in the owner's religious law.
4
Examine the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i argument: since these items have no taqawwum in Islamic law (they are impure and prohibited), and dhimmis are subject to the same legal rulings as Muslims in transactions, they also lack value, hence no liability.
The Shafi'i view treats taqawwum as absolute rather than relative.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis require the destroyer to pay compensation; Shafi'is do not. This affects judicial decisions in cases involving dhimmi property.
The dispute also extends to sales: Hanafis permit sale of wine/pig between dhimmis; Shafi'is do not.

Chapter on the usurpation of that which is not valuable property. He said: If a Muslim destroys the wine or pig of a dhimmi, he is liable; if he destroys them from a Muslim, he is not liable. Al-Shafi'i said: He is not liable for them for the dhimmi either. And upon this difference is (the case) if a dhimmi destroys them from a dhimmi, or a dhimmi sells them to a dhimmi. Translation: Chapter on the usurpation of that which is not valuable property. If a Muslim destroys a dhimmi's wine or his pig, he will be liable; and if he destroys these things from a Muslim, he will not be liable. Imam al-Shafi'i says that for a dhimmi also he will not be liable for them. And upon this difference is when a dhimmi destroys these things of a dhimmi, or a dhimmi sells them to another dhimmi. Commentary: His statement 'wa idha atlaf...' etc. This issue has four scenarios: (1) A Muslim destroys a Muslim's wine. (2) A dhimmi destroys a Muslim's wine (this case is not mentioned in the book). (3) A dhimmi destroys a dhimmi's wine. (4) A Muslim destroys a dhimmi's wine. In the first two scenarios, by consensus there is no liability; in the last two, according to us liability is wajib, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i. His statement 'fa in atlafahuma...' etc. The pronoun 'huma' refers to wine and pig. In some copies it is 'atlafaha', which according to Taj al-Shari'ah means the same, and its parallel is the divine saying: 'And when they see a transaction or a diversion, they rush to it' and Allah the Exalted says 'And those who hoard gold and silver and do not spend them in the way of Allah'. The issue: if a Muslim destroys a dhimmi's wine or his pig, he is liable; if a Muslim destroys a Muslim's wine or pig, he is not liable. Imam Malik also holds this. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad say that if a Muslim destroys these things of a dhimmi, he is not liable. And the same difference is when a dhimmi destroys another dhimmi's things, or a dhimmi sells them to another dhimmi: according to us, liability is wajib and the sale is permissible, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof: for him, their value (taqawwum) has fallen with respect to a Muslim, so similarly with respect to a dhimmi, because they are followers of us in rulings, so destroying them does not require a valuable property, i.e., liability. Our proof: the value remains with respect to them, because wine for them is like vinegar for us, and pig for them...
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling (mas'ala) from the chapter on usurpation of non-fungible items (ghasp ma la yataqawwam). The matn states: If a Muslim destroys a dhimmi's wine or pig, he is liable; if he destroys a Muslim's, he is not. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, saying no liability even for dhimmi. The commentary elaborates four scenarios: (1) Muslim destroys Muslim's – no liability by ijma. (2) Dhimmi destroys Muslim's – implied no liability. (3) Muslim destroys dhimmi's – Hanafi: liability, Shafi'i: no. (4) Dhimmi destroys dhimmi's – same ikhtilaf. The Hanafi proof: wine and pigs are considered valuable property (mutaqawwam) for dhimmis, as they are permissible for them, like vinegar for Muslims. Hence, destroying them incurs liability. The Shafi'i proof: since these items have no value for Muslims, and dhimmis are subject to the same rulings as Muslims in legal matters (being followers), they also should not have value, so no liability. The commentary also notes that Imam Malik agrees with the Hanafi position, while Imam Ahmad agrees with al-Shafi'i.

Key Terms
خمر (khamr): Wine; a beverage from grapes that is intoxicating.
خنزير (khinzir): Pig; swine.
تقوم (taqawwum): Being legally considered as valuable property (mal mutaqawwim) that carries liability if destroyed.
ضمان (daman): Liability; obligation to compensate for loss or destruction of property.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim subject of an Islamic state who is protected under a pact (dhimma), allowed to practice his religion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a Muslim destroys a dhimmi's pig, what is the ruling?
A) No liability because pigs are impure.
B) The Muslim is liable (must pay compensation).
C) Only if the pig was used for farming.
D) The Muslim must pay only if the dhimmi is a relative.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, property value is relative to the owner's religious law: what is valueless for a Muslim may be valuable for a dhimmi, so destroying it incurs liability.

Muslim's Destruction of Dhimmi's Wine or Pig: Liability and Dispute with Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on liability for destroying dhimmi's wine/pig

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a Muslim's liability for destroying a dhimmi's wine or pig and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A Muslim is liable for destroying a dhimmi's wine or pig because they remain property in the dhimmi's religion.

How does Islamic law treat property that is sacred to non-Muslims but forbidden to Muslims? This lesson examines a classical inter-madhhab dispute: whether a Muslim must compensate a dhimmi for destroying his wine or pig. The Hanafi school holds that liability exists, while the Shafi'i school denies it. We will trace the proofs and understand the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
A Muslim who destroys a dhimmi's wine or pig is liable for compensation (wajib). This is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling.
There is no intra-Hanafi disagreement on this point.
2
Identify the opposing school and its position
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold that no liability arises, because wine and pigs are not considered property in Islamic law.
Imam Malik agrees with the Hanafi view.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof (istihsan)
The dhimmi's wine is like vinegar for us, and his pig is like a sheep for us—they are valued in their religion. We are commanded to leave them to their religion, so their property rights remain. Destroying such property requires compensation.
The key principle is that taqawwum (being property) is determined by the owner's belief system.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i proof (qiyas)
Since wine and pigs are not property for Muslims, and dhimmis are subject to Islamic rulings, they are not property for dhimmis either. Therefore, no liability.
Shafi'i bases this on the hadith that dhimmis have what Muslims have and upon them what is upon Muslims.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In Hanafi fiqh, a dhimmi can claim compensation from a Muslim for destroying his wine or pig. In Shafi'i fiqh, no such claim is recognized. Also, transactions of wine/pig between dhimmis are valid in Hanafi but invalid in Shafi'i.
This distinction affects property rights and commercial dealings in pluralistic societies.

Source Text

كتاب الغصب
جب تلف کر دے مسلمان ذمی کی شراب یا اس کا خنزیر تو ضامن ہوگا اور اگر یہ چیزیں تلف کیں مسلمان کی تو مسلمان ضامن نہ ہو گا
فصل في غصب ما لا يتقوم . قال واذا اتلف المسلم خمر الذمى او خنزیره ضمن فان اتلفها لمسلم لم يضمن وقال الشافعي لا يضمنهما للذمى ايضا وعلى هذا الخلاف اذا اتلفهما ذمى على ذمى او باعهما الذمى من الذمى
ترجمہ فصل اس چیز کے غصب میں جو قیمتی نہیں ہے ) جب تلف کر دے مسلمان ذمی کی شراب یا اس کا شتر بر تو ضامن ہوگا اور اگر یہ چیزیں تلف کیں کسی مسلمان کی تو ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ذمی کیلئے بھی ان کا ضامن نہ ہوگا ۔ اور اسی اختلاف پر ہے جب ذمی کی یہ چیزیں کوئی ذمی تلف کرے یا ان کو ایک ذمی دوسرے ذمی کے ہاتھ فروخت کر لے۔
تشریح قوله و اذا اتلف..... الخ اس مسئلہ کی چار صورتیں ہیں:۔
مسلمان کا کسی مسلمان کی شراب تلف کرنا۔
-۲ ذمی کا کسی مسلمان کی شراب تلف کرنا ( کتاب میں یہ صورت مذکور نہیں ) ۔
۔ ذمی کا کسی ذمی کی شراب تلف کرنا۔ - مسلمان کا کسی ذمی کی شراب تلف کرنا۔
پہلی دوصورتوں میں مختلف پر بالا جماع ضمان نہیں اور آخری دو میں ہمارے نزدیک ضمان واجب ہے برخلاف امام شافعی کے۔ قوله فان اتلفهما .... الخ - ہما ضمیر کا مرجع خمر اور خنزیر ہے۔ بعض نسخوں میں اتلفہا ہے جس سے مراد بقول تاج الشریعۃ اتلفهما ہی ہے جس کی نظیر ارشاد باری ہے: "وَإِذَا رَأَوْا تِجَارَةٌ اَوْ لَهُوَا بانفَضُّوا إِلَيْهَا" - وَقَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى " وَالَّذِينَ يَكْذِرُونَ الذَّهَبَ وَالْفِضَّةَ وَلَا
يُنْفِقُونَهَا فِي سَبيل الله -
مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مسلمان نے کسی ذمی کی شراب یا اس کا خنز بر تلف کر دیا تو وہ ضامن ہوگا اور اگر مسلمان نے دوسرے مسلمان کی شراب یا اس کا خنزیر تلف کیا تو ضامن نہ ہو گا۔ امام مالک بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ امام شافعی اور امام احمد فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مسلمان نے کسی ذمی کی یہ چیزیں تلف کیں تو اس میں بھی ضامن نہ ہوگا ۔ اور یہی اختلاف اس صورت میں بھی ہے جب ایک ذمی دوسرے ذمی کی یہ چیزیں تلف کر لے یا ایک ذمی دوسرے ذمی کے ہاتھ فروخت کر لے کہ ہمارے نزدیک ضمان واجب اور بیع جائز ہے برخلاف امام شافعی و امام احمد کے۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل
له انه سقط تقومهما فى حق المسلم فكذا في حق الذمى لانهم اتباع لنا في حق الاحكام فلا يجب باتلافهما مال متقوم وهو الضمان ولنا ان التقوم باق فى حقهم اذ الخمر لهم كالخل لنا والخنزير لهم
كتاب الغصب
كالشاة لنا، ونحن أمرنا بان نتركهم وما يدينون والسيف موضوع فيتعذر الالزام واذا بقى التقوم فقد وجد اتلاف مال مملوک متقوم فيضمنه بخلاف الميتة والدم لان احدًا من اهل الاديان لايدين تمولها الا انه يجب قيمة الخمر وان كان من ذوات الامثال لان المسلم ممنوع عن تمليكها لكونه اعزازاً لها، بخلاف ما اذا جرت المبايعة بين الذميين، لان الذمى غیر ممنوع عن تملیک الخمر، وتملكها، وهذا بخلاف الربوا لانه مستثنى عن عقودهم وبخلاف العبد المرتد يكون للذمى لانا ما ضمنا لهم ترك التعرض له لما فيه من الاستخفاف بالدين وبخلاف متروک التسمية عامدا اذا كان لمن يبيحه لان ولاية
المحاجة ثابتة
ترجمہ امام شافعی رحمۃ اللہ علیہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسلمان کے حق میں ان کا قیمتی ہونا ساقط ہے تو ایسے ہی ذمی کے حق میں بھی کیونکہ وہ احکام میں ہمارے تابع ہیں ۔ پس ان کے تلف کرنے سے قیمتی مال یعنی منمان واجب نہ ہو گا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان کے حق میں قیمتی ہونا باقی ہے۔ کیونکہ شراب ان کیلئے ایسی ہے جیسے ہمارے لئے سرکہ اور خنزیر ان کیلئے ایسا ہے جیسے ہمارے لئے بکری اور ہم کوحکم دیا گیا ہے کہ ان کو ان کے دین پر چھوڑیں اور ان سے تلوار اٹھا دی گئی تو کسی حکم کا لازم کرنا مستعد رہے اور جب تقوم باقی رہا تو مملوک متقوم کا تلف کرنا پایا گیا۔ لہذا ضامن ہو گا۔ بخلاف مردار اور خون کے کیونکہ کوئی بھی دین والا ان کو مال کے طور پر نہیں رکھتا۔ صرف اتنی بات ہے کہ شراب کی قیمت واجب ہو گی اگر چہ وہ متلی چیزوں میں سے ہے کیونکہ مسلمان اس کی تملیک سے روکا گیا ہے اسلئے کہ ایسا کرنا شراب کا اعزاز ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے جب دونوں ذمیوں میں شراب کی خرید و فروخت جاری ہوئی ہو کیونکہ ڈمی کو تملک و تملک خمر سے نہیں روکا گیا اور یہ بیاج کے خلاف ہے۔ کیونکہ بیاج ان کے عہد ذمہ سے مستقلی ہے اور بخلاف مرتد غلام کے جو کسی ذمی کی ملک ہو کیونکہ ہم نے ان کیلئے مر تو سے ترک تعرض کا معاہدہ نہیں کیا۔ اسلئے کہ اس میں دین کی ہتک ہے اور بخلاف عمد امتروک التسمیہ کے جبکہ وہ ایسے شخص کا ہو جو اس کو مباح سمجھتا ہے۔ کیونکہ حجت سے قائل کرنے کی ولایت
ثابت ہے۔
تشريح .... قوله له انه سقط ..... الخ - امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسلمان کے حق میں خمر وخنزیر کا تقوم ساقط ہے تو ذمی حق کے حق میں بھی ساقط ہوگا کیونکہ احکام میں یہ لوگ ہمارے تابع ہیں ۔ لقوله علیه السلام فاذا قبلوا عقد الذمة فاعلمهم ان لهم ما للمسلمين و عليهم ما على المسلمين پس خمر و خنزیر پر تلف کرنے سے قیمتی مال یعنی ضمان
واجب نہ ہوگا۔
قوله ولنا ان التقوم .... الخ - ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ذمیوں کے حق میں خمر خنزیر کا قیمتی ہونا باقی ہے کیونکہ یہ ان کے حق میں ایسی ہیں جیسے ہمارے حق میں سرکہ اور بکری ، اور ہم شرعاً ان کو ان کے دین پر چھوڑنے کے مامور ہیں پھر وہ لوگ جو ان کی مالیت کے معتقد ہیں اس کا ابطال تلوار ہی سے ہو سکتا ہے۔ حالانکہ ذمہ کی وجہ سے تلوار ان کے ذمہ سے موضوع ہو چکی تو کسی حکم کا لازم کرنا متعذر ہے اور جب
ان کے حق میں تقوم باقی رہا تو متقوم مملوک کا اختلاف پایا گیا لہذا ضامن ہوگا۔
Book of Usurpation. When a Muslim destroys a dhimmi's wine or his pig, he is liable; if he destroys them for a Muslim, he is not liable. Chapter on usurping what is not property. He said: And if a Muslim destroys the wine of a dhimmi or his pig, he is liable; if he destroys them for a Muslim, he is not liable. Al-Shafi'i said: He is not liable for them for a dhimmi either. And on this disagreement [is] if a dhimmi destroys them from a dhimmi, or if a dhimmi sells them to a dhimmi. [Urdu commentary follows, repeating the above and explaining the four scenarios, then giving the proofs of al-Shafi'i and the Hanafis.]
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the liability (daman) for destroying wine (khamr) or pigs (khinzir) that belong to a dhimmi. The Hanafi position (supported by Imam Malik) holds that a Muslim is liable if he destroys a dhimmi's wine or pig, because these items are considered property (mal mutaqawwim) for dhimmis by their own religion. However, a Muslim is not liable if he destroys these items belonging to another Muslim, since wine and pigs are not property for Muslims. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad argue that the dhimmi's wine and pig are not protected property even for the dhimmi, because dhimmis are subject to Islamic rulings and these items are not considered property in Islam. The Hanafi proof is based on istihsan: the dhimmi's wine is like vinegar for us, and his pig is like a sheep for us — they are valued in their religion, and we are commanded to leave them to their religion. The sword of fighting is lifted from them due to the dhimma contract, so we cannot force them to abandon their beliefs. Thus, property value remains in their regard, and destroying it requires compensation. The passage also discusses related cases: transactions between dhimmis involving wine/pigs are valid among them, unlike the prohibition of riba which is excepted from their contracts. The key practical consequence: Hanafi law protects the property rights of dhimmis in their religiously lawful items, while Shafi'i law does not recognize such items as property.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation or illegal taking of property; here extended to destruction of property that is not owned by the taker.
تقوم (taqawwum): The quality of being considered property (mal) in Islamic law, i.e., having legal value.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under the protection of an Islamic state, bound by a dhimma contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a Muslim destroys a dhimmi's pig?
A) The Muslim is not liable because pigs are not property in Islam.
B) The Muslim is liable and must compensate the dhimmi.
C) The Muslim must pay double the value as a penalty.
D) The Muslim is not liable because the dhimmi is under Islamic rule.

Key Takeaway
A Muslim is liable for destroying a dhimmi's wine or pig because it is property in the dhimmi's religion, and Islamic law preserves their religious practices.

intermediate
6 min
Guarantee for Destroying Dhimmi's Wine and Pig
Inter-madhhab dispute: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on value guarantee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the guarantee for destroying a dhimmi's wine or pig, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the principle of consensus (ijmāʿ).

Core Idea
A Muslim must guarantee a dhimmi's wine or pig because they remain valuable property in the dhimmi's religion.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafiʿī regarding the liability (ḍamān) of a Muslim who destroys wine (khamr) or a pig (khinzīr) belonging to a dhimmī. The Hanafi school holds that guarantee is obligatory because these items are considered valuable property (mutaqawwam) in the dhimmī's religion, while the Shafiʿī school denies any liability. The dispute hinges on whether the valuation (taqawwum) depends on the owner's religious framework or the general Islamic classification. This lesson unpacks the proofs and reasoning that lead to the Hanafi ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the legal ruling: a Muslim who destroys a dhimmi's wine or pig must pay its value (qīmah). This is considered wājib (obligatory) because the items are mutaqawwam for the dhimmi.
The Hanafi ruling applies even though the Muslim cannot possess these items.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafiʿī argues that no guarantee is required because wine and pig are not valuable property for Muslims, and dhimmīs are subject to the same rulings as Muslims. The proof is the hadith: 'They have what Muslims have and upon them what is upon Muslims.'
The Shafiʿi position is based on the idea of legal symmetry.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafi school responds that the hadith is specified (takhṣīṣ) by consensus, as demonstrated by the practice of Caliph ʿUmar, who allowed dhimmīs to sell wine and collected 'ushr from its price, treating it as valuable property. This indicates that the prohibition of wine is limited to Muslims.
Consensus (ijmāʿ) overrides the general implication of the hadith.
4
Understand the Hanafi argument from original permissibility
The Hanafi school also argues that wine and pig were originally permissible and valuable in earlier revelations and at the beginning of Islam. The Quranic prohibition (avoid it) applies only to Muslims by context, leaving dhimmīs under the original ruling.
This reasoning relies on the principle that what is established remains unless removed by a clear text.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The practical consequence is: under Hanafi law, the Muslim must pay the value; under Shafiʿi law, no payment is due. This affects actual court decisions and fatwa guidelines.
The Hanafi position is muftā bihi and supported by the majority of Hanafi scholars.
